Summary

After Agatha claws her way out of the Scarlet Witch’s distorted spell, vulnerable and weak and shattered, Rio picks her wife up and takes her home, like she’s a stray cat she’s saving from the streets. She scratches and spits and fights the entire time. Death loves her all the more for it.

aka: an au where our two semi-divorced disaster lesbian witches sort out their shit, deep in the new england woods, while one of them recovers from a traumatic mind-control spell and the other is an immortal cosmic entity struggling with the idea of letting go.

Notes

title - ‘need' by taylor swift (unreleased)

'tis I, the anonymous author behind the supercorp fic 'the fifth force', running to ao3 after sobbing my heart out over these two lesbian witches who i was screaming at through my screen to just fucking sit down and TALK

so now i am trapping them in a cottage in the mountains together where agatha and rio have no choice but to confront their issues because agatha is sick and injured and rio will not let her wife die

Chapter 1

Agatha Harkness, Rio thinks when she first learns of her, is rather like a feral cat. She freely wanders the forests of New England like an opportunistic predator, hunting down the mousy little witches who stray too far into the shadows and pouncing when their backs are turned. She startles easily, and sees every person around her as a threat, suspicious of kindness, as if she sees all forms of affection as lures to a trap.

Ironically, when she learns to shapeshift one day after stealing the power from a witch who bit off more than she could chew, her animal form is that of one of the quick-footed little felines that roam the wilds of Britain, with thick glossy chocolate and charcoal fur and a long sleek tail that constantly twitches. It suits her. The hairballs, however, discourage her from shifting again.

Agatha, like a cat, also seems to have nine lives. Siphoning power and killing witches is a lifestyle that creates many enemies, and while Agatha stalks the woods in search of her next piece of prey, others in the form of witch hunters and the aggrieved family members seek vengeance.

And they catch her. Agatha is young, and she makes mistakes. She suffers for it. She is tied up and tortured and nearly killed, numerous times. But Agatha is resilient and slippery. Two decades of neglect and abuse at the hands of her mother have taught her how to escape bindings. The people who attempt to make her pay in blood end up choking to death on their own.

She evades death with practice and ease, as if the threat of it is a mere inconvenience to her. She thrives as danger hangs over her head like an axe, and no amount of pain deters her from her path. Whenever she is hurt, she simply licks her wounds and moves on, ready to hunt down her next meal.

Rio likes cats. Coincidentally, she also likes Agatha. She’s fascinated by her, in fact. And it is extremely rare, nigh on paradoxical, for a mortal to capture the attention of Lady Death.

When she first encountered her face-to-face, Rio watched in awe from the opposite side of a clearing as Agatha ripped apart the witch-queen attacking her. She claimed to have tracked the siphon down to ‘put her out of her misery’. Agatha drank in her power as if she was ravenous, and hadn’t fed in weeks. When she caught sight of Rio, hovering, she went utterly still, not moving a muscle, staring back.

Her eyes glinted with distrust and rage and fear. Her hands flexed at her sides, crackling with purple sparks. Rio did not attack, and so Agatha did not either. She stood frozen, observing, as Rio approached the witch-queen’s cold, shriveled form to extract the soul, tilting her head. When Rio bowed her head in gratitude, Agatha slunk off into the shadows of the forest, casting one last wary glance back at Lady Death before disappearing.

Since that night, Agatha has always hovered around her kills, waiting for Rio to appear. They rarely exchange a single word, and yet Rio gets the sense that Agatha trusts her; she knows that Rio isn’t ever there to take her, and so she feels safe in Death’s presence. Occasionally, Agatha will nod back to her. Thank you, Death nods at her, and Agatha nods back, you’re welcome.

Rio’s curiosity is never sated; every meeting between them leaves her aching, yearning, for more. When they do eventually begin to strike up conversation over corpses, Agatha’s caution departs; she’s bold and brash, and refreshingly shameless. She doesn’t care that Rio is a cosmic entity she should simultaneously revere and cower away from. She talks to her witch to witch, as if she is a person, as if she is a friend.

They do not become friends, though. They become more. Agatha wants her in a manner that is charged, primal and blasphemous, and after they’ve kissed each other breathless, she makes Rio fight to make her submit. When Agatha rolls them over, pins Rio’s wrists to the ground with one hand, and possessively places the other on her throat, she’s shocked and delighted. Nobody else would have the courage or audacity to try and dominate Death.

After the battle is over, and they are both naked and sweaty, covered in red marks, and oh so satisfied, she curls up to Rio in a bed of worn-thin blankets and moss in the clearing where they first met - and she purrs.

Te veo, Rio says to Agatha, every time before she departs. I see you. Because she does. Rio understands Agatha Harkness on a molecular level.

Agatha is this beautiful, fearsome, tough creature who radiates darkness and leaves a trail of bodies in her wake. Presents, gifts, their souls left behind for Death like slaughtered mice at her feet. She’s by far one of the most efficient killers that Rio has ever encountered in the universe. The way she licks into Rio’s mouth whenever they kiss makes her toes curl, and her cries to the heavens as Rio brings her to ecstasy make her feel alive. Her magic is wild and uncontrollable, and Agatha herself is ferociously defiant, despite her past filled with pain, trauma, and fear.

Agatha is a murderer. A survivor. When she looks at her, Rio sees an untameable, vicious, lonely woman, who thinks she is unworthy of understanding and affection. She looks at Agatha and sees her equal.

Is it any wonder that she falls in love?

No, she thinks. It was inevitable.

All roads lead to Death, and Death’s road always circles back to Agatha Harkness.

Centuries pass. There is a handfasting beneath a canopy of maple and white pine trees, under the light of the full moon. There is a cottage built in the middle of a mountainous forest, far from civilization, where no witch hunters or vindictive covens can find them. There are days of long walks hand-in-hand by the creek and kisses in fields of wild blooms, and nights of passion and pleasure, blessed by the stars. There is a baby, born of love and death, gifted six years of stolen life. There is a song, composed by a boy and his mother.

And at the end, there is heartbreak: a small grave, piled with stones and draped in handwoven garlands of ivy and lilacs and chrysanthemums.

Love turns into guilt, grief, and hatred. The loss of their child scars them both irrevocably.

Nicholas dies. Agatha cries. Rio begins to question whether her role as Death is as merciful and sinless as she thought. Agatha blames her, and Rio lets her. She screams that Rio doesn’t love her enough to save their son, and Rio sobs because she never imagined a day when Agatha would flinch away from her. Communication breaks down. Her wife will not allow herself to mourn, and Rio is Death, so doesn’t know how. All that is left is despair and pain.

Agatha leaves. She runs, like a cat from a fire, which makes sense, because their relationship has gone up in flames. She cloaks herself in the darkest of magicks, and once she has possession of the Darkhold, she vanishes from Rio’s senses completely.

She doesn’t lose hope; she chases after her, following the corpses of the witches she drains, but Agatha no longer waits for her to appear; she flees, before Rio can even catch a glimpse of her.

Over time, as Agatha continues to leach magic from the Darkhold, she kills fewer and fewer witches, until eventually, Rio cannot trace her anymore. If she is killing witches, it is not in a way that is detectable to her. Agatha is gone.

It hurts. She gave Agatha her heart, and Agatha threw it at her feet and stomped on it. While she wants to resent Agatha, and starts to wonder why she gave her special treatment when she clearly didn’t deserve or appreciate it, Rio can’t bring herself to resort to loathing. Agatha is the only person she has ever loved, who has ever loved her. But Agatha is drowning in sorrow and has surrendered her hope. Rio cannot hate Agatha for being human and having feelings.

Several times, Rio very faintly senses Agatha’s lifeline snag and falter, as if she’s teetering on the edge of a cliff, close to death. Moments later, that feeling fades. She worries about her lost love. Is Agatha being reckless with her life? Punishing herself? Is she falling back on pain as a coping mechanism, when the grief is too much to bear? Rio is terrified that one day, she will feel that call to collect Agatha’s soul and ferry her to the other side, and her wife will die still hating her, questioning if they ever truly loved each other.

When Agatha finally pops back up onto Rio’s radar, her soul bright and shining and singing, she races to her side. She’s horrified by what she finds. Her wife’s mind has been damaged and ensnared by a corrupted spell, that has twisted and warped since its caster, the infamous Wanda Maximoff, perished.

Agatha’s power has been ripped from her, her magical core mutilated, and she is trapped living in delusions. Rio observes her acting out roles in different non-existent TV shows while neglecting her health. She is alive, thanks only to the Westview residents encouraging her to drink and eat, but she is not living.

Despite their care, Agatha is an emaciated mess of a human being. If any of her enemies were to discover her in this state, they could kill her easily. Rio notes in relief that she does, at least, have a familiar to help protect her; a demon that Agatha has tamed and disguised as a cute and fluffy bunny rabbit, who sleeps on her chest and guards her at night.

Nevertheless, when Rio arrives in Westview and senses danger approaching, she realizes that she needs to free Agatha from the enchantment and whisk her off somewhere safe - and she needs to do it fast.

It takes two days of plucking at the threads of the spell and unraveling the chains around Agatha’s mind for Rio to finally reach her. Her wife is convinced that she is Agnes O’Connor, a small-town detective solving a murder case, and Rio plays the role of an FBI agent butting into the investigation, in hopes that it might trigger Agatha’s buried memories to emerge. And slowly, they do; Agatha instantly casts her as a lover-turned-ex-turned-rival, and her caution is so incredibly nostalgic.

Her wife is guarded and defensive, bristling with suspicion, but desperately craving her love. She stutters adorably when Rio flirts and teases, bears her teeth and growls when she antagonizes her. Rio tries to prod her to remember why she hates her, praying that maybe Agatha’s complicated feelings toward her will help tear her free, but she backs off when Agatha blanks out and shuts down, panicking.

Eventually, Agatha begins to struggle, fighting the binding. Rio can only encourage her, putting the pressure on, because these last shackles are ones that Agatha must bust herself. She stands back and watches with pride as Agatha shakes and pants, stripping out of her clothes as she shreds the last vestiges of the hex.

As soon as Agatha has clawed her way out of the Scarlet Witch’s distorted spell, bone tired and the most physically weak she has ever been, Rio swoops in. Agatha is naked and disorientated, and doesn’t quite understand what is happening, but she sees Rio’s face, recognizes her, and raises high hell.

Rio picks her wife up and teleports them to that old cottage in the White Mountains National Forest Park that was abandoned so long ago along with their hopes and dreams. Kicking the door open, she carries her inside - like she’s a stray cat she’s saving from the streets. Agatha scratches and spits and fights the entire time, screaming and sobbing until Rio’s shoulder is wet with her tears.

Rio’s heart pangs as she listens to her wife cry. She knows that this is the last place Agatha would likely want to be. But her wife is in no state to look after or protect herself. Case in point, after barely five minutes of uselessly raking her blunt nails over Rio’s neck, Agatha collapses, exhausted. When Agatha is stronger and lucid, and her mangled magical core has healed, she can make her own decisions. Until then, Death is asserting her authority.

“You’re home, my love,” she whispers, gently lowering Agatha onto what used to be their shared bed. A quick cleaning spell removes all traces of dirt and dust, leaving the cottage as good as new. She runs her trembling fingers over Agatha’s weary, distressed face, tucking stray locks of dark silky hair behind her ear. Her wife’s shivering naked form is quickly covered by fresh sheets, warmed with a wave of her hand. “You’re safe. You’re free.”

“Rio,” Agatha murmurs feebly, eyes fluttering as she succumbs to sleep. “Why?”

“Because you are mine. And I am never going to let anybody hurt you, ever again.”

Rio is forced to briefly leave Agatha by herself in the cottage to command her agents to continue to reap souls in her absence. They don’t dare to question where she is going, nor do they ask how long she will be gone, but Rio answers the question that she senses on the fringes of the majority of their minds: why? She tells them: her consort has returned home, and she is injured, so Death must tend to her to ensure her recovery. Her agents rejoice on her behalf, and request that she pass on their well wishes to their Mistress’ partner.

The cottage is remote, charmingly rustic, and minimalistic, everything made out of American oak and mountain ash wood sourced from the forest it’s situated in, with accents of hunter green and auburn. Dried herbs and flowers hang from the rafters to manifest good health and peace, and ward off evil spirits. The still room hasn’t been disturbed since the night Agatha went into labor with Nicholas; the spirit witch’s favorite set of cast iron pans are still sitting in the sink after being washed, without a speck of rest, thanks to an enchantment cast long ago.

It’s like stepping back in time. If they were still living in the 18th century, it would be perfect. For the 21st century, however, everything is tremendously outdated. Rio adds modern appliances and amenities to the cottage that she reckons Agatha will have gotten used to utilizing in the past couple of decades. The kitchen and bathroom, for one thing, need serious upgrades. Electricity, running water, and gas are equally as important, especially as Vermont can get extremely cold in the later part of fall and during winter.

She then fills the fridge and larder with food that she remembers Agatha favored in their days of married bliss; it’s as she’s doing this that her eyes fall upon the bundles of kale, lettuce, and watercress, and she remembers Agatha’s cuddly demonic familiar, left behind in Westview.

The rabbit is a sassy little shit, kicking at her unhappily when she grabs him from where he’s hiding in Agatha’s basement. It’s definitely Agatha’s familiar, she thinks annoyedly. Honestly, why couldn’t she have bonded to a cat? Maybe Agatha herself is too cat-like to consider a cat companion.

The rabbit - name unknown - only calms down when she dumps him unceremoniously at the end of the bed where Agatha is still sleeping, so deeply that she looks almost dead. The bunny hops carefully up onto his sleeping witch’s belly, where he splays out and lies there, napping.

Rio can tell that Agatha won’t wake up for a while. Returning to the Westview house, Rio recovers clothes that she suspects belong to her wife, and a meager number of personal belongings, including her beloved locket that contains a lock of their son’s hair. There’s a pocket dimension down in the basement where she found the rabbit, and upon breaking into it, discovers that Agatha has amassed a huge collection of grimoires and magical artifacts over the centuries.

There’s no trace of the Darkhold. Rio knows that the Scarlet Witch took it from her wife, likely by force, and ultimately destroyed it. She hates how relieved she feels that the Book of the Damned will no longer have any sort of influence over Agatha. Unfortunately, the damage has probably already been done.

She seals the pocket dimension back up and, being the cosmic entity that she is, stores it away in her own for safekeeping. Agatha is starving for power at the moment, but her magical core is too mauled to contain it. The contents of her magical collection are too dangerous for her to handle while she is so weak. She’ll give everything back once Agatha’s powers are restored.

Death is the original Green Witch, so she forages in the overgrown garden outside the cottage, bursting with herbs and plants she seeded when they first acquired the land. She concocts a potent reinvigoration elixir (that yes, does include her saliva, Agatha will be thrilled when she finds out), and bottles enough for a daily dose for the next fortnight. Agatha needs to heal, and for that, she needs both rest and energy. Rio trying to heal her quickly with her magic might kill her, while her magical core is incapacitated.

Slipping back into the bedroom, Rio lines up Agatha’s Hecate brooch, a glass of lemon water, the elixir vial, and for good measure, some migraine pills, on the bedside table. Agatha will probably have a killer headache when she regains consciousness. That spell messing with her mind was a nasty little creation, and she suspects there will be some psychic aftereffects. Rio stores her clothes in her half of the closet, and her belongings in the chest at the foot of the bed. She casts one last wistful look at her slumbering wife before retreating to the living room.

Now all Rio can do is wait. She’s still wearing her Lady Death robes, and so sheds them for more appropriate, comfortable clothing. The cottage has always brought out a domestic side to her that Rio was honestly shocked to discover exists. Rio’s not one for unnecessary faff, and uses magic to change into black snakeskin patterned leggings, a black crop top, and a distressed dark green wool cardigan.

She can’t feel the cold, but it’s nice to match the cottage’s cozy fall vibes. She doesn’t need to drink or eat either, but she’s grown fond of tea over the centuries, mostly because Agatha used to enjoy lemon, ginger, and sage tea in the mornings during her pregnancy; she can’t bring herself to drink the same blend, so brews up some loose leaf oolong tea instead. She sips at it absentmindedly while reclining on the couch, flicking through one of Agatha’s grimoires.

Hours later, as the sun creeps below the horizon and bathes the surrounding forest in a soft tangerine glow, Rio senses Agatha stirring. As much as she wants to rush to her side, she suspects that her presence will not be well received, and so decides to leave Agatha to wake up slowly, by herself.

She re-focuses on the grimoire, which she is about halfway through reading. It’s an interesting book that is more philosophical than instructional, commenting on the marriage between Green Craft and Spirit Craft. It stupefies Rio that Agatha owns this book, only because she was certain that Agatha would steer clear of anything Green Craft related, to avoid having to think about Rio. The grimoire proposes that Green and Spirit magic work synergistically - they are stronger when combined. It’s not new information to Rio, but she’s intrigued to know how Agatha would have reacted to reading it. She expects that she might have been tempted to burn the tome.

Something she does not expect is for Agatha is come tearing out of the bedroom, half-hazardly dressed in a flower-pattered robe, and immediately make for the kitchen. Rio sets the book aside on the couch cushions, watching with a raised eyebrow as Agatha snatches up a knife from the butcher’s block. She then throws herself at Rio without hesitation, howling furiously.

Rio teleports behind her seconds before Agatha is about to drive the blade into her side, laughing in glee at the enraged, crazed gleam in her wife’s eyes. Rabid feral cat Agatha has made her dramatic reappearance. Oh, how she missed her.

It’s cute, and almost flattering, how much effort Agatha is putting into trying to stab her, even though she must know that her murder attempts are futile; Death cannot be killed, after all. That doesn’t mean Agatha’s not giving it a real go. She swings her arm wildly, trying to slash Rio with the knife blade. Her sloppy movements and awful aim give away the fact that Agatha is tired, and likely running solely on adrenaline. She’s more likely to skewer herself by accident than cause any sort of damage to Rio.

When Agatha next attacks, Rio seizes her arm and twists it behind her back. The knife clatters onto the ground and Agatha mewls as Rio presses her up against the nearest wall. She adjusts her grip slightly when she feels that Agatha’s shoulder is close to dislocating, and rests her weight on her back to pin her.

Her knee ends up separating Agatha’s legs; Rio grins smugly as her wife jolts and squirms, fighting her grasp and then instantly stopping when it inadvertently results in her grinding down on Rio’s thigh.

Just to make her twitch, Rio sweeps her hair to the side to expose her neck and exhales hot air against her skin, lips brushing over her pulse point. Agatha nearly collapses, but instead of whining like she usually would at the sensation of Rio kissing her throat, she growls thunderously.

“Hello, Agatha,” Rio murmurs, drawing out her name teasingly. She steps back to give her enough space to turn around, but remains reluctant to release her. “I’ve missed you.”

Agatha jerks, yanking her wrist from Rio’s grip and cradling her sore arm to her chest as she whips around, back flush to the wall. “I hate you,” she croaks, eyes ablaze.

Chuckling, Rio grabs her by the hips, leaning in. “Oh, darling, such sweet words to greet your beloved wife with, after two hundred years of separation.” Agatha recoils when Death anchors their bodies together, arms wrapping around her waist. She pushes back, hissing.

“Why the fuck would you bring me back here?” she says shakily, shoving at Rio’s shoulders uselessly as she attempts to free herself. “What kind of s-sick game are you playing, you psychopath?”

Psychopath. Goddess, from Agatha that’s practically a term of endearment.

“This is cat and mouse, and I’ve finally caught up to you, witch killer,” she purrs.

Agatha inhales sharply at the moniker, averting her eyes. Rio hopes that she’s recalling the nights when Agatha joyfully played the role of Death’s most loyal and devoted disciple, attentive and vehement in her worship. Rio would call her witch killer then, while Agatha’s mouth was occupied in proving her adoration.

So often, Rio would be the one on her knees in their dynamic, showering Agatha with praise and sweet words that would make her fall apart on her fingers or tongue. But when the nights rolled around when Agatha would gift Rio her submission, she would break her, wielding the truth as a weapon, calling her murderer, outcast, anathema. Agatha would cry, and then Rio would build her back up again by reminding her of her true worth until she found release in the catharsis.

“You were the one who started this, when you acquired the Darkhold, when you hid behind all that dark magic,” Rio reminds her. She strokes a thumb gently over Agatha’s pale cheek and tips her chin up with a lone finger, inviting her to make eye contact again. She does, her sky-blue eyes wet and red-rimmed. “But then you lost them. The Darkhold and your purple. Got in over your head with that Scarlet Bitch.”

“Do I detect some jealousy in your voice?” Agatha bites out, jerking her chin away. “Don’t like me spending time with another witch? It’s none of your business.”

“If my wife is whoring herself out to the Harbinger of Chaos, then it is very much my business.” Rio crowds her against the wall, smiling viciously. “You thought you could get away with cheating on me, baby? You thought I wouldn’t find out?” she coos.

“Cheating implies a relationship. As far as I’m aware, we were over two centuries ago,” she snaps.

Now that, that infuriates her. Rio may be Death, but she is also the original Green Witch. And when witches marry, when they handfast under the light of the full moon, they permanently bind themselves to each other. Their magic becomes eternally entwined, their souls linked. There’s no such thing as a witch divorce.

“Until death do us part, do you remember that?” she taunts. “And as Death, I say we’ll never part, because you belong to me. We’ll be married until the end of the universe.”

An expression of disgust flits over Agatha’s face. “You’re obsessed,” she spits.

“Mm, I prefer possessive.”

Rio twirls a lock of her wife’s brunette hair around her finger. She leans in further, until her lips are inches away from Agatha’s, until she can feel her frantic, gasping breaths against her face. Her hand rakes through her hair, fingertips scraping Agatha’s skull, until she’s cradling it in her palm. Agatha resists, her eyes flickering down to Rio’s lips, panicked. She thinks that Rio is going is kiss her, clearly. And oh, she is so tempted.

“I protect what’s mine. And right now, as much as it may pain you to admit, you need me. That red-haired homewrecker drained you dry, and you’re powerless. Which means you’re vulnerable,” Death sneers.

“Only physically,” Agatha breathes.

And then, in a stunning turn of events, slams her forehead against Rio’s with enough force that if she were human, she would undoubtedly be knocked out. Because she’s not human, though, it just sends her reeling, stumbling back as her vision turns blurry and white. Rio barks out a laugh of sheer disbelief. Agatha is scrambling away from her, trying to reach the knife once again.

She’s magnificent. Despite being powerless, weak as a kitten, and caught in a snare by Death herself, Agatha doesn’t back down. She is just as crafty and devious as ever. Rio is awestruck. Three years of being trapped in a horrific, mind-scrambling enchantment would have left any other witch helpless and traumatized. But Agatha’s spirit wasn’t broken. It’s battered and bruised and abused, but still just as strong as ever; she survived having her magical core mutilated by the Scarlet Witch, against all the odds. She is still every bit the ferocious little witch who Rio fell in love with back in the 17th century.

Rio banishes the blade a fraction of a second before Agatha’s fingers are able to wrap around the hilt, and she screeches in frustration. She throws the nearest object - Rio’s abandoned mug of lukewarm tea - at her instead. She manages to duck just in time, wincing when the ceramic smashes on the wall behind her. She liked that mug.

Agatha switches tactics, maintaining her distance now. They circle each other, the couch a barrier between them. Perhaps she wants Rio to blast her with magic, forgetting that her special brand of green would almost instantly kill her if she siphons it.

They circle for a good half a minute, like two caged warring tigers, waiting for the right time to pounce. Impatient, Rio vaults over the sofa and charges her. When she tries to restrain and subdue her wife again, Agatha claws and scratches at her face like an animal. At one point, she sinks her teeth into Rio’s forearm, biting hard enough that she’s obviously trying to draw blood. They grapple with each other until Agatha manages to hook her leg around Rio’s and flip them mid-air. Rio lands on her back on the floor with a thud, Agatha straddling her hips with her trembling hands squeezing her throat.

When the spirit witch’s grip tightens, she realizes that Agatha is trying to cut off her oxygen and circulation by applying pressure to her carotid. Has she forgotten that Rio doesn’t need oxygen? Or blood? “You can’t kill me, Agatha,” she smirks.

Ashen-faced, Agatha looks dazed, her breathing uneven and shallow, but adrenaline is fueling her rage. “You can’t kill me,” she managed to say, voice slurred. “S’not allowed.”

She presses her weight down through her arms. Rio is flooded with arousal upon seeing her wife’s determined expression, reaching up to grasp her wrists; instead of ripping Agatha’s hands off her, she encourages her. Fuck, she is so turned on. “Yeah, baby, choke me. C’mon, harder,” she goads. “I know you can do better than that.”

Agatha falters, her grip weakening. “S-stop it,” she stammers.

A moan rips from Rio’s throat, and she bucks her hips up against Agatha, nearly unseating her. “Make me.”

“I…” she stutters, her voice dying out.

Agatha’s eyes roll into the back of her head. She slumps on top of her like a rag doll, her hand around Rio’s neck going slack.

Rio freezes. She jolts upright, her wife limp in her arms, and she swiftly rolls her over so that her head lolls in her lap. “Agatha. Agatha,” she says urgently.

The spirit witch doesn’t respond, even when Rio frantically taps on her cheek. And then her body tenses and begins to jerk uncontrollably, her limbs shaking. Rio panics. She can do nothing but watch in horror as her wife suffers from a seizure. It only lasts half a minute, but it’s still incredibly disturbing to witness. When the seizure comes to an end, Rio gently maneuvers her into the recovery position on the floor, snagging a pillow from the nearby couch to cushion her fragile head.

Seconds later, she feels a prickle of unease, the tiny hairs on the back of her neck tingling. She realizes that Agatha’s chest is still.

She’s not breathing.

Alarm floods her veins like liquid ice, and Rio lurches to her feet, the unconscious witch cradled to her chest.

“Fuck. Stay with me, sweetheart, stay with me.” She moves Agatha to the couch, yanks her robe open, and presses her hand to her bare chest, directly above her heart. It beats very faintly. “Shit shit shit.”

What was she thinking, wrestling and fighting with Agatha when her wife’s body is under such considerable stress? It was fun, yes, but it was ridiculously irresponsible of her. She feels actually physically sick with guilt. She should have known better. She brought Agatha here to the cottage so she could keep her safe while she recovers from three years of psychic torment, not to exchange blows. Now Agatha’s life is on the line.

She summons one of the reinvigoration elixirs, unstoppers it, and carefully coaxes her unconscious partner to drink it down, making sure there’s minimal risk of choking or regurgitating the liquid. The elixir works fast, and within a minute or so, Agatha looks less frail, a soft pink flush returning to her pale face. She starts to breathe again, regularly and deeply. Her heartbeat steadies out.

Rio sighs in relief. She bends over to press a delicate kiss just above her witch’s brow, smoothing her tousled hair away from her eyes and lips. “You’re okay,” she whispers, unsure whether she’s trying to comfort Agatha or herself, at this point. “I’ve got you, mi vida, you’re okay.”

That was close. Too close. Agatha may have instigated that fight, but it’s Rio’s fault that it escalated.

Re-tying Agatha’s robe to give her some modesty, the green witch scoops her up and carries her bridal-style back into the bedroom. The quilt has been tossed to the floor and the sheets are rumpled, telling of a turbulent awakening. She rolls her eyes when she sees that the reinvigoration elixir she left on the bedside table hasn’t been touched. Agatha took the time to pick up her Triple Goddess locket brooch and pin it to her robe, but did not drink the vial to aid her healing.

It explains why Agatha was staggering around like a newborn fawn during their fight. Rio should have spelled it directly into her stomach earlier, instead of believing, for some reason, that Agatha would trust her enough to drink it without complaint. At least she has a dose of it in her system now.

The bunny familiar is flopped over on top of the comforter, and his black-eyed gaze is disapproving and accusing when he sees his bonded witch passed out in Rio’s arms. It makes Rio feel worse about her actions.

“What are you looking at?” she snipes. The rabbit’s little nose flares. “You don’t like me, huh? Well, you wanna meet my pet? Maybe you’ll get on better with her.” With a wave of her hand, she manifests Victoria, her Mexican redknee tarantula. She crawls down Rio’s arm slowly. The bunny squeals and flees underneath the bed. “Yeah, you little shit, that’s what I thought.” Victoria goes back into her pocket dimension, with a lovely cicada snack to thank her for her service.

Rio tenderly lays Agatha down on the mattress, on her side as she prefers, and then yanks the quilt from the floor, shaking it out. It’s draped over the spirit witch’s body; Rio tucks it in around her knees so that it will insulate her.

Now that the sun has set, the bedroom is beginning to feel cold. There’s a draft bringing in the chilly mountain air from the window, so Rio seals it before crossing to the other side of the room where the traditional obsidian fireplace lies. Green flames erupt to life within the grate, without the need for any tinder or logs. The fire will burn for as long as Rio wants it to. Within minutes, the bedroom feels warmer.

Although she momentarily debates manifesting a chair to sit on next to the bedside, Rio shakes her head, and climbs onto the mattress next to Agatha. She needs to be close, to monitor her temperature and breathing, is what she tells herself; she settles onto her side on top of the comforter, facing her sleeping wife, watching every twitch of the arteries she can see in her throat - proof that Agatha’s heart is still pumping.

She reaches out tentatively, grazing her fingertips over her wife’s exposed clavicle. Nestled beneath her ribs, invisible to everybody except Death, her soul burns as brightly as a compressed star, interwoven with Agatha’s damaged magical core and holding her together. Rio’s close proximity makes it thrum excitedly. Agatha may not be happy to see her again, but her soul certainly is.

Maybe it’s Rio’s mind playing tricks, but she thinks Agatha looks even smaller and more brittle than she did before when she was unconscious. The seizure she suffered from has sapped all the remaining strength and energy from her body.

But she’s alive. That’s what matters. Now Rio just has to keep her alive long enough to heal up and get her powers back. And she knows that Agatha will not make it easy.

“What am I going to do with you?” she murmurs.

Chapter 2

Chapter Notes

TL;DR:
rio: *pets agatha* poor baby just needs love
agatha: *hisses, bites her*
rio: BAD AGATHA NO BITING
agatha: *cries* omg you hate meeee
rio: *frustrated* PLEASE JUST LET ME LOVE YOU

thank you all for your support!! hope you continue to enjoy :)

cw: implied-referenced self-harm, suicidal ideation, discussion of child loss and past child abuse

Agatha slumbers through the night. Rio dares not rouse her, hyperaware of the fact that Agatha is in desperate need of rest, considering her severe sleep deprivation. Midnight comes and passes. Rio, who cannot sleep, dozes as best as a cosmic being can to waste the hours away. The bedroom is shadowed and dark, lit only by a lone lamp in the corner and the fireplace. The sound of the flames crackling away in the grate is soothing, and the heat it’s emitting makes the room feel even cozier. It’s all too easy to zone out.

As time slips by, Agatha gravitates closer and closer to Death, until she’s practically snuggling up to her, head nestled on her shoulder. A stray hand has slipped beneath Rio’s cardigan, pressed against her bare stomach, seeking her warmth. If Agatha were cognizant of her actions, she would be scandalized. But she’s not. And for that reason, Rio draws her wife into her arms, one wrapped around her waist and the other tenderly combing through her hair. Agatha used to love it when she would do that; it was one of the only things she requested as part of her aftercare, along with gentle kisses and reassurance that she had been good.

Rio will savor this moment for as long as it lasts, because she knows that as soon as Agatha wakes up, she will try and vivisect Rio with her clipped nails. She’ll screech so loudly that it will risk rupturing Lady Death’s eardrums. This might be the only chance she gets to sleep next to her wife before Agatha heals, gets her powers back, and creeps off into the shadows to hide again.

When Agatha slowly begins to fight her way back to consciousness, Rio carefully shifts away from her and sits upright, shuffling to the edge of the mattress to sit cross-legged. She rests her chin on her hand. She would usually pull her blade out to fidget with it, twirling it around her fingers, but there’s a chance Agatha might lunge for it and injure herself. She won’t take that risk. So Rio resigns herself to sitting, waiting, and watching.

Her name is on Agatha’s lips the second her eyes crack open, a sleepy, bemused mumble of, “Rio,” that sets her heart racing.

“Milady,” Rio greets her with a soft smile.

Blinking groggily, Agatha tilts her head up, blue eyes hazy. She’s shivering, her teeth chattering, but it’s from shock, not the cold. “What h-happened?”

Rio can do nothing but comfort her, trailing her fingers up and down her wife’s arm soothingly. “You had a seizure,” she explains quietly. Seizure, Agatha mouths, bewildered, as if the word is foreign to her. “I got carried away, I’m sorry. No more fighting, not even as foreplay. You need to rest, mi vida.”

Agatha’s face screws up as she asks dazedly, “Why does my mouth taste like shit?”

She barks a laugh. “That would be the reinvigoration elixir.”

“An elixir?” she repeats. “Why the fuck would you give me that?”

“Because I can only heal so much with magic and I didn’t think you wanted me licking over your entire body while unconscious. You tend to prefer being awake for that,” she answers dryly. “I’m Death, Agatha. I’m not all that talented at bringing people back to life once they stop breathing. And earlier? You stopped breathing.” Leaning in, she whispers with a wink and a light pinch to Agatha’s arm, “The elixir does contain my saliva, if you were wondering. If you’d like a pure application, you can ask me to spit in your mouth. I’d be very happy to.”

“Fuck off.” Agatha jerks her arm, dislodging Rio’s hand. Her own raises, fingers twitching, as if she’s preparing an energy blast. But not a lick of purple materializes. Her magical core judders. Her arm flops back to the mattress as she curls up into a ball with a tiny whimper, quaking with pain. Her eyes fill with tears as she gasps out, “What’s happening to me? Why did that hurt so much?”

Aching with sympathy, Rio explains, “That abomination of a witch tore your magical core to shreds when she ripped your power from you. If you try and reach for your magic right now, you could kill yourself. The spell she trapped you under... it messed with your mind to the point where you forgot to drink, eat… sleep.” Agatha is shaking her head in horror, clearly in denial. “Your body is tired and malnourished. It will take time for you to recover. Hence the daily dose of the elixir. It should help your body slowly gain strength over time.”

Agatha manages a nod, staring up at the ceiling as tears bead at the corners of her eyes, slipping silently down her cheeks. It finally appears to dawn on her where she is, her frantic gaze darting around the bedroom. She looks as if she’s about to throw up.

“Why did you bring me here?” her wife croaks.

Rio sighs. “So I can protect you.”

She’s not lying, but she’s also not telling the whole truth. As much as this lodging situation is to keep the world away from Agatha, it’s also to keep Agatha away from the world. So long as Agatha is inside this cottage, tucked away in the mountains, vulnerable and isolated, she will be completely reliant on Rio. She can keep Agatha by her side. The spirit witch has no choice but to let Rio take care of her. And it may be wrong of her, to enjoy asserting such control over her wife - abusive, really - but their relationship has always been fairly toxic. It’s not new.

Eventually, when Agatha is strong enough to put up a proper fight, Rio will let her leave. She will happily transport her to wherever she wants to go, in fact. But she will not let Agatha go when she is at such a high risk of being attacked and killed. Agatha is not allowed to die. The truth is that she doesn’t trust Agatha to look after herself; she will neglect her own health and place herself in danger, just so that she can pursue power. If Rio has to essentially hold her hostage to ensure her continued survival, then she will do so. If that makes her a monster, then so be it. Agatha already thinks of her as one, so it won’t change anything.

Agatha stares at her, incredulous. “Why?”

“You’re my wife,” Rio says simply, “And I love you.”

It’s factual. The grass is green. The sky is blue. Rio Vidal loves Agatha Harkness.

But Agatha looks disquieted. She eyes Rio shrewdly, as if she’s searching her face for certain microexpressions that may give away whether she’s lying. She doesn’t believe her. “No, you don’t. You hate me, you want me dead,” she retorts, her voice sharp.

That’s insulting to hear. Rio swallows hard. Agatha has thrown a lot of harsh, cruel words in her face before, but nothing is as hurtful as hearing her wife accuse her of lying about loving her. She did it after Nicholas’ death, and is doing it again now. She has to resist the urge to lash back at her and ask if Agatha even knows how to recognize love, because that would be truly heartless of her. Agatha’s family didn’t love her; Evanora treated her daughter atrociously, from the day she was born up until the day she died attempting to murder her.

It took Agatha decades to acknowledge how badly her mother traumatized her, and even longer to learn that love is not meant to be toxic, painful, or punishing. Rio learnt alongside her, and was the one to teach her that true love is unconditional. In return, Agatha taught her about human nature: hopes and dreams, turmoil and strife, altruism and greed. Agatha did not pretend to be a paragon of righteousness any​​ more than Rio pretended to be human. Agatha accepted her as Lady Death and loved her regardless.

Or at least… she used to.

Before, she used to trust Rio when she told her that she loved her. That seems to no longer be the case.

“You think I would break you out of that enchantment and bring you home if that were true?” she counters.

Agatha scoffs. “Home,” she echoes, mockingly.

Rio grinds her teeth, infuriated that she would ridicule the cottage where they planned to live together forever and raise a family, before everything imploded. “We built this place from scratch, Agatha, it will always be your home as much as it is mine,” she asserts, gesturing around the bedroom.

She jumps when she hears a thud behind her. Turning, she blinks down at Agatha’s bunny, who has emerged from under the bed and thumped the ground aggressively to get her attention. He hops up onto his back legs, tiny front paws batting at the air as he squeaks at her.

“Why is the rabbit acting like that?” she asks, baffled.

“You said his name,” Agatha tells her flatly. Rio shoots her a confused look. A blush flooding her cheeks, Agatha averts her eyes, admitting in a rush, “He’s called Señor Scratchy.”

“You-” Rio’s throat closes. She’s at a loss for words. Señor Scratchy. Scratch. That adorable nickname Agatha gave Nicholas, because of the way he was conceived. Nicky used to adore bunnies. Rabbit was the one type of meat he would categorically refuse to eat. He would cry whenever they got caught in Agatha’s snares. “You named your familiar after our son?” she whispers.

Agatha plucks at a loose thread on the quilt, bending her head forward so her hair covers her flushed face. “And you,” she mumbles.

That did not escape Rio’s notice; she could have called him Mister Scratchy, but specifically chose to name him Señor, as a nod to the form that Death has chosen to take as a Latina woman. Rio softens, glancing between Agatha and the bunny, who is blinking up at her, ears wiggling. The rabbit is irritating, but maybe she can learn how to get along with it. As Agatha’s familiar, he carries a tiny piece of her soul, meaning he is technically a part of her. And Rio loves every part of her wife.

When Agatha sneaks a glance to check her reaction, she bristles upon seeing Rio’s smile. “Don’t look at me like that,” she huffs. “And don’t say anything or I’ll cut your tongue out.”

Rio snags the bunny from the floor with a single hand, dumping him on the bedspread and giving him a light prod to encourage him into Agatha’s arms. “Here.” Agatha draws Scratchy into her protective embrace, eyeing her warily. “You’re so fucking jumpy,” Rio groans. “Relax, I’m not gonna do anything to you.”

“You sure about that?”

“You’re the one who came at me with a knife,” Rio points out.

She expects Agatha to snap at her for that one. What she does not expect is the spirit witch to deflate, stroking over her familiar’s sleek fur as she admits, her voice barely audible, “I was scared.”

It’s astonishing to hear those words drop from Agatha’s lips, because she never outwardly admits to fear. She must be feeling unwell.

“That I’d hurt you?” Rio questions, puzzled. Agatha tenses. That’s a yes. She’s a bit surprised, really. She supposes that she did technically kidnap her wife and bring her to the cottage without her consent, but she didn’t restrain her or lock her away. She tucked Agatha into bed, brought her familiar along, and gave her water, meds, and a potion to make her feel better. Did that not prove that she has good intentions? “I won’t, I promise.”

It’s the wrong thing to say. Agatha’s agitation ramps up. She’s not at feral cat level yet, but she is definitely on her way there. “Your promises mean nothing to me. They’re worthless. You always break them,” she says shakily.

She pushes Scratchy to the side and tries to roll out of bed. Agatha can’t gather enough strength to lift her torso, let alone sit upright. The quilt pools at her waist once she manages to get herself into a sitting position, leaning heavily against the bed’s backboard. Her legs shift restlessly beneath the comforter. She clenches her hands into fists in the fabric anxiously as she appears to realize how the seizure has affected her already fatigued body. The mental exhaustion must be hitting her too, because Rio can see tears springing to her eyes.

She hesitates, but extends her hand out, planning to set it gently on her wife’s shoulder to offer some silent comfort. She cannot imagine it’s at all easy for Agatha in her current position. She knows how much she despises feeling helpless and needing to rely on other people. Agatha has nobody except her rabbit familiar and Rio to support her right now. But the moment her fingertips make contact with Agatha’s arm, Agatha reacts like her very touch is poisonous, her whole body jolting away violently.

She whips around with sudden energy to slap Rio’s hand away, snarling, “Don’t touch me. I don’t want to be here, I don’t want to look at you, I want to leave.”

Goddess, Agatha is unpredictable at the best of times, but Rio somehow forgot how it’s always hot and cold with her. She’s achingly sad and vulnerable one second, and then spiteful and affronted the next. Has she always been this volatile? Yes, Rio thinks, but she became much less impulsive after they started seeing one another.

Maybe Agatha just needs to get laid. Rio keeps her mouth shut; Agatha might try to strangle her again if she makes a comment about it. Sensing the rising tension, Scratchy jumps to the ground and lopes away, disappearing from the bedroom, probably in search of some plants to nibble on.

“You can’t. You go back out there alone, and you’ll die,” Rio says, honest and blunt. “It won’t take long before your enemies find out you’ve lost your power and that you’re sick from the aftermath of the spell, and they’ll come for you.” Agatha glares at her disbelievingly. Does she think Rio is over-exaggerating? She’s not. To emphasize her point, she informs her, “The Salem Seven were already sniffing around Westview when I broke you out.” The two bird shapeshifter witches were actually surveilling the house when Rio arrived. She reckons they would have attacked the day Agatha escaped the spell, if Rio hadn’t stepped in.

“So you’re - what, going to keep me prisoner here?” Agatha scowls, incensed.

“If that’s what it takes to keep you alive, yes,” Rio replies calmly.

Agatha draws her legs up to her chest to hug her knees, on the very edge of the bed now, leaning as far away from Rio as possible. She sneers, lip curling. “Would’ve thought you’d want me dead. Then my soul would belong to you forever. You’d have free rein to drag me to your realm as your consort and keep me chained up as your eternal bed warmer.” Her voice drips with venomous derision, making it plain that she intends her words to be provocative and cutting.

Rio, however, is not cowed, and instead smirks, quirking an eyebrow. “You’ve thought a lot about warming Lady Death’s bed, hmm?” she teases, in a deliberately sultry tone.

Agatha turns red. Called out. And her embarrassment angers her as she fires back, “No. But you’d like that, wouldn’t you? To finally have full control over me - my life and my death. You’ve been my sick, twisted stalker since that night my mother and coven tried to kill me, and even after you ruined my life and took everything from me, you can’t take no for an answer.”

Rio lurches off the bed, enraged. Ruined her life? Is Agatha trying to gaslight her or has she hyper-focused so much on her negative emotions over the past two centuries that she’s forgotten everything good?

“And when exactly did you say no? I remember you giving me your very enthusiastic consent throughout the entire length of our relationship, Agatha. You spoke to me first, you kissed me first. You were the one who decided when we first slept together, you agreed to marry me, you were the one who wanted a child, and I gave you everything,” she argues.

Her voice raises in volume until she’s shouting, towering over the spirit witch intimidatingly. Black lightning sizzles at her fingertips, begging to be unleashed. Rio is angry, yes, but she’s also overwhelmingly upset and disappointed. Agatha truly does not appreciate anything she has done for her.

“Rio -” Agatha tries to interrupt her, the fury having vanished from her eyes as she looks stricken.

But Rio won't let her cut her off. “Everything you ever asked for, I gave it to you! You say I'm the one who took everything from you? Look in the fucking mirror. You’re a siphon, Agatha, and all you know how to do is take. Even when it threatened the cosmic balance, I bent the rules to make you happy, so you wouldn’t despise me.”

Even though Agatha is recoiling away from her, she won’t back down. “I never asked you to do that!” Agatha yells.

“You begged me for Nicky’s life.” Rio points at her accusingly. “You said you would hate me forever if I didn’t save him! I nearly fucking shattered spacetime, just so he could live for six years, constantly sick and needlessly suffering. Just so that you could get the chance to be a mother. And then the time you did have with him, you wasted.”

Agatha blanches abruptly, paling. She ducks her head, chastised. The truth hurts. But Rio isn’t done. She’s fueled by frustration, by years of sorrow and wrath at being cast away for doing her job. When in reality, her actions freed their sick son from his chronic pain. It feels so amazing to have the chance to finally unload all of that, and vent her feelings. This is the argument that she and Agatha should have had centuries ago. Rio didn't fight back then, when Agatha kicked her to the curb. So she'll fight back now.

“You used him to lure in witches to drain and forced him to participate in your murder spree. And what happened in the end?” Rio throws her arms up in the air with a bitter, sarcastic laugh, and delivers one final, devastating blow. “He still died, just like he was meant to before he was born. And you hated me anyway. You squandered the six years I gave you with Nicky, that he was never meant to have, admit it. Maybe you didn't deserve that time with him in the first place!”

Agatha bursts into tears.

Rio feels the floor fall out from beneath her feet at the sight.

Oh.

Oh. Fuck.

“I hate you,” Agatha says brokenly. She rocks back and forth, scoring deep scratches into her arms with her nails. It’s as if she’s trying to claw herself out of her own skin. Rio’s harsh words are so effective at bringing Agatha back down to Earth that they have ripped it out from under her. She’s dissolving, breaking down, chanting through her sobs and cries, “I hate you, I hate you, I hate you.”

She can hear, in the way Agatha’s voice cracks and trembles, what she really means. I hate myself.

Rio’s heart shatters the second she sees the first beads of blood on Agatha’s wrists. She shows no sign of stopping, the pain of digging her nails through her skin negligible in comparison to the agony that Rio’s statement has caused her. She’s scarcely breathing because of how hard she’s crying. Agatha is tearing at her arms in such a vicious manner that if she doesn’t stop soon, she’ll accidentally slit open an important blood vessel and begin to properly bleed out.

What has she done? Her wife might actually kill herself if she carries on like this, and it will be her fault. She dragged Agatha here to the cottage to protect her, to take care of her - to help her heal. This is not healing. This is wounding. She’s causing her wife more pain.

Agatha’s raised hackles and snappish attitude are so typical of an injured animal feeling cornered. She’s putting on an indignant facade, but in reality, she’s unsettled and scared. Rio poked at her, amused by her growling. And then, when Agatha understandably bit at her, Rio struck back, harder and harsher.

How does she fix this?

She climbs onto the bed, on her knees, grasping her witch's blood-stained hands and pinning them to the mattress. “Stop, Agatha. Stop,” she implores desperately. “I'm sorry. I'm sorry, okay? I went too far, that was cruel of me. I didn't mean what I said."

“Yes, you did,” Agatha sobs.

Rio grimaces, because Agatha is right; she did, and that's the worst part. “Please stop. You’re going to seriously hurt yourself, and you’re weak enough already.”

“So what? What does it matter? I didn’t ask you to save me, I didn’t want you to,” Agatha weeps. “You should have left me in that cesspool of a town to wither away and die under Wanda’s spell. If you weren’t Death, then you could’ve finished the job yourself, and performed a mercy killing.”

Rio is crying herself now as she pulls Agatha into her arms, hugging her fiercely. Agatha doesn’t fight her, simply burying her face into Rio’s shoulder, resigned. What Agatha is saying is devastating. The weight of her words is trampling Rio’s soul. She feels splintered. Agatha pleading for death is so wrong that Rio has no idea how to process it. Agatha fucking Harkness, a witch who has notoriously survived everything thrown her way in the past, begging for a mercy killing?

It’s undignified. It’s unfathomable. It’s heartbreaking.

Agatha’s voice is muffled against Rio’s chest as she murmurs, in a defeated rasp, “Why can’t you let me go, Rio?”

She strokes her hand down her wife’s back soothingly. “Because I don’t know how,” Rio confesses. She feels Agatha’s breath hitch, but she remains silent. She probably has no clue how to respond. As seconds pass, her body becomes heavier and heavier, her weight sinking into Rio’s embrace, as exhaustion begins to overcome her once again. “Sleep, Agatha. We can fight more after you’ve rested, if it’ll make you feel better.”

“I don’t wanna sleep,” she mumbles, as she slides out of Rio’s arms and slumps onto the bed, shuddering. Her eyes flutter closed as the green witch draws the covers back over her. “I don’t wanna fight either,” she admits, her voice quiet with shame. “It never makes me feel better, it makes everything worse. But I always start it because I don’t want you to hurt me first.”

That revelation shines an entirely new light on Agatha’s hostility towards Rio over the centuries. Agatha is perhaps the most self-deprecating person Rio has ever encountered, but she would rather self-immolate than ever concede an argument.

Her wife was raised in a household where conflict could not be resolved without further conflict; Evanora Harkness was such a stony, unkind woman that the only way Agatha survived her younger years was by reacting preemptively to her abuse, often resulting in her appearing to be the aggressor.

In the case of her relationship with Rio… well, it makes sense that after things turned sour between them, Agatha would regress back to that mindset. She lashes out at Rio because she’s afraid of what will happen if Rio takes a hit at her first. And Rio has just proven to her that her fear was completely valid; Agatha upset her with her snarky words and Rio went for her throat by using the most cataclysmic, traumatic event of her life - losing her son - against her.

She exhales, continuing to pet Agatha’s hair. Eventually, though, she stops, because she doesn’t know if her wife is actually tolerating it or is too tired to smack her hand away. “Okay. Then… maybe the cottage can be like our Switzerland? Neutral ground,” she suggests. “I will make an effort to be less antagonistic, if you make an effort to control your temper and let me take care of you.”

Agatha gnaws at her nails anxiously, blinking in fatigue as she contemplates the offer. “My tolerance level is extraordinarily low and I’m a lousy patient. I’m still gonna end up yelling at you,” she mutters.

“But you’ll think before you speak?” Rio presses. The only reason their arguments get so rough and tumble is because Agatha blurts out her curt, caustic comments without pausing to think how they might be received.

“I’m not a child,” Agatha scowls. Rio crosses her arms, raising an eyebrow pointedly at how immature she sounds. She tugs the blankets closer, so she can gather them to her chest and hug them. “Fine. Truce?”

She nods. “Truce.”

A beat of tense silence, and the. Agatha says hesitantly, “Can I make a request?”

Rio blinks, surprised. “Sure.”

Her wife exhales shakily. “Don’t… talk about him,” she says. “Please.”

Rio’s heart cracks in two. “Agatha -”

“Don’t,” she pleads.

Nicky was such a huge part of their lives when they were together, and losing him is what broke them apart. There is no way they can spend any substantial amount of time here in this cottage together without discussing Nicholas - especially when the nursery they designed and built for him, but he didn’t get to use, is down the corridor, behind a locked door. And would it not be disrespectful to avoid talking about him?

“I can’t talk about him with you,” her wife whispers, with wet eyes. “I just get… so insanely angry thinking about what happened.”

“Angry at me?”

Her breath hitches, blue eyes darkening. “Don’t ask questions you don’t want to know the answer to,” she replies lowly.

So she is angry at Rio. Well, at least she’s on brand. She’s blamed Rio for Nicky’s death for the past two centuries; nothing has happened to change that. “I won’t actively bring him up in conversation, but if the subject naturally drifts there then you can’t get mad at me for that,” Rio allows.

Agatha mulls that over and then reluctantly agrees, “I suppose that’s fair.”

Her jaw cracks in a yawn. Rio doesn’t need to check the time or how dark it is outside to know that they are well into the witching hour. She rises from where she’s seated on the bed to quench the fire in the grate slightly, withdrawing her magic to dampen the flames but not enough to extinguish them. As soon as it partially dies, the temperature in the bedroom drops. Returning to the bed, Rio lifts the quilt to slither beneath it, planning to use her body heat to keep Agatha warm.

As soon as she clambers under the comforter, however, Agatha stares at her as if she’s grown a second head, suddenly much more awake than before. “What are you doing?” she demands.

Rio blinks. She would have thought it would be obvious. “Lying in bed next to you.”

Agatha scoffs. “Get the fuck out. Truce or not, I’m not sleeping in the same bed as you.”

Rio rears back, annoyed. One step forward, three steps back. “There’s only one bed, Agatha, and it’s our marital one. This is my bed too,” she reminds her. When her wife sneers, Rio needles with a smirk, “Or it is that you don’t think you’ll be able to resist me?”

Rio purses her lips. “Touché.”

Agatha releases a stuttering breath. “I can try. That’s it. That’s all I’m offering.”

“Good enough.” Rio raises an eyebrow. “Can I get back to brushing your hair now?” She waves the comb in front of her face teasingly.

“Yes,” she grinds out. She swallows and then mutters, as if to remind herself, “You’re doing this because you love me.”

Rio doesn’t deign to reply verbally. She can only hope that whatever time they end up spending together over the next week, as Agatha rests and heals, will prove to her wife that she’s telling the truth.

Chapter 4
