It takes a remarkably long time to brush Agatha’s hair, as she soaks in herb-infused steaming bathwater with her eyes shut, trusting Rio to take care of her, despite all the animosity between them.

Agatha seems to visibly enjoy the sensation of Rio’s fingertips raking over her skull. An involuntary contented mewl breaks free from her lips, which she immediately tries to stifle by pressing them together. She’s always loved having her hair played with. That, it appears, hasn’t changed.

Back in the day, when Agatha was wrung out and overstimulated after endless rounds of sex, Rio learned that she could bring her wife to the brink of orgasm just by pulling her hair. She wonders absentmindedly if she could reproduce that result, two hundred years later. If Agatha let her, that is. Right now, she reckons that the spirit witch would rather claw her face off than allow her to touch below her waist.

Shaking her head to dispel those thoughts, Rio sets to work on taking care of Agatha’s hair. She collected Agatha’s haircare products from the Westview house when she took a jaunt over there to pick it clean of her personal belongings, so picks up the bottle of shampoo left next to the sink. It looks luxurious and expensive; silicon and sulfate free, with ingredients like manuka honey, shea butter, marshmallow root, and avocado oil, with biotin and hydrolyzed collagen and a load of other things added to rack up the price point.

Rio despises how sticky it feels between her palms, but dutifully massages it into Agatha’s roots. It lathers easily, and a small teaspoon-sized volume is able to cover her wife’s entire head.

Rio rests her chin on the edge of the bath as they wait for a while, letting the shampoo sit and hydrate Agatha’s hair. She looks so adorable with all the frothy bubbles piled on her head. “I don’t think I’ve ever seen your hair this long,” she muses aloud. It’s so long that it must hang down below her waist. Untameable and wild, just like Agatha herself.

“Because you used to cut it for me,” Agatha reminds her. Her lips twitch into the tiniest wistful smile. “You were terrible at it.”

Gasping dramatically, Rio places a hand on her chest in mock offense. In reality, she knows that she was awful at cutting Agatha’s hair; she only did it out of necessity. “Only you would turn Lady Death into your personal hairdresser.”

“You were all too happy to do it, when I told you I would try and cut it myself otherwise,” Agatha huffs. “You loved playing with my hair, you wanted it well taken care of.”

And that’s true - Agatha flat-out threatened to give herself a bob at one point because her hair kept getting caught on bushes and thorns out in the forest when she was foraging. Tying her hair up helped a little, but it still got in the way a lot. Agatha was highly reluctant to actually cut her hair so short, though; short hair was associated with sickness and made it more difficult to infiltrate villages to acquire supplies. Rio offered to shear it to a reasonable length and regularly helped her brush it.

One of her favorite things to do in the evenings she could take some time off from fulfilling her cosmic duties and go home to Agatha, was to braid her hair before making love with her under the moonlight.

“I did,” Rio remembers, reaching out to give one of her wife’s sudsy locks a playful tug. “And you have really let yourself go. The amount of split ends you have today - atrocious.”

Standing, the green witch turns the taps to restart the flow of water out of the shower attachment. She taps Agatha’s chin to encourage her to tilt her head back again so she can rinse out the shampoo. Agatha keeps her eyes pinched shut to avoid getting any soap in them, her face adorably scrunched up. Rio darts out to press a quick kiss to her wet forehead, beaming when her wife barely reacts beyond an annoyed huff. Probably because the kiss itself eases her headache slightly.

“Not surprised,” Agatha murmurs. “Haven’t had somebody else cut it since that last time you did.”

“Did you become allergic to scissors, after you left?” she asks, partially joking but also confused. It’s been two hundred years. Agatha hasn’t cut her hair since then? She supposes that the witch could have effortlessly utilized magic to style it, but not a single haircut? “Because I remember you definitely were not when we were together. In fact, you were a self-certified expert in scissoring. I think we invented it,” she laughs.

She anticipates an answering chuckle, or at least a little huff of amusement, but receives nothing. Agatha’s eyes are open again, electric blue, and peering up at the ceiling. Concerningly, however, she looks as if she’s a million miles away.

It’s not a daydream about her and Rio’s sexual exploits and invention of various positions; the expression contorting her face is one of discomfort and melancholy, and she would like to think that Agatha recalls their intimate moments with fondness and yearning, not sadness. No, Agatha looks as if she’s lost in her more somber memories as she stares dazedly upward, dissociated, her whole body tensed.

Scooting over, Rio sets her hand over Agatha’s, which has a white-knuckled grip on the edge of the tub. “Agatha?” she calls, hesitant.

She sees it, the moment Agatha is torn from wherever her mind wandered off to and jerked back to the present, jolting to awareness. Her guard slams back up almost instantly, and she plasters an unimpressed mask on to hide her distress.

“Haha. Great joke. Very funny,” she deadpans, slipping her hand free from Rio’s. The indifference is so forced that it’s agonizing to witness. “Lesbians around the world are giving you a standing ovation.”

Rio is not going to let it go that easily. “No, hey - where did you go just now?” she says softly. “Don’t laugh it off. You were thinking about something that upset you.”

Agatha turns away, looking conflicted. Getting the sense that she needs a little time to gather her discombobulated thoughts, Rio busies herself working conditioner into her hair. Glossy conditioner that feels and smells equally as expensive as the shampoo is rubbed into the bottom half of her hair, and Rio focuses on the split ends she mentioned, which desperately need some hydration. She rinses her hands in the murky water, turning the shower off as she returns to her place by the bath to wait for that round of treatment to marinate.

As Death, she has an infinite amount of power, but there are some things that she can’t do, and one of them is that she can’t force Agatha to talk.

She can’t read Agatha’s mind, either, without her express permission; her mental barriers have always been impenetrable, which is part of her nature as a siphon. Agatha herself is a witch who continues to exist purely on the back of defense mechanisms, of which her impassable mind shield to keep out telepaths is one. Even without her powers, she’s strong enough to keep Rio out if she so wishes, and she will not risk damaging her wife’s mind further by prying her way in.

So Rio washes Agatha’s hair and remains patient, hoping that she will open up.

It’s as she’s doing this, the water trickling down over her wife’s bare shoulders, that Agatha does lower her walls to explain, her voice trembling, “After we separated, I couldn’t trust anybody else to wield anything sharp while standing behind me. I’d been stabbed in the back too many times. I wasn’t going to let it happen again.”

Rio can feel another fissure ripping into her heart. She tries to maintain steady, calm breathing, even as tears prick at the corners of her eyes. It genuinely hurts her to hear Agatha say that. Her spirit witch was abused, shunned and vilified by her own coven, so she fell into that role because she didn’t see any other alternate path of life.

She was briefly unshackled from her condemnation when she and Rio settled down together, finding peace in learning how to love and be loved. Nicholas’ birth gave her a new purpose as a mother, although that, of course, ended tragically, leading her back to a life of rejection, fraud, thievery, and loneliness.

Rio contributed to that pain, even though she was just doing her job, and finally righting the wrong she wrought in the universe by allowing Nicky to live six years of stolen life. Despite her lack of options at the time, Rio deeply regrets her part in hurting the love of her life. It was entirely unavoidable, but devastating nonetheless. She was forced to break Agatha’s heart by taking their son away, and it’s clear to her now that Agatha has never recovered.

Agatha has lived her entire adult life without a coven because she has learned that relying on anybody, trusting anybody, only results in pain, heartbreak, and eventual abandonment.

She’s a lioness without a pride, surviving only through her constant scavenging for power. Hunted, reviled, distrusted.

The world turned its back on Agatha Harkness, so she turned her back on the world.

Agatha, the Scourge of Salem, cast herself out of the witch society that called her a filicidal abomination, because she didn’t see the point in even trying to fight for understanding and acceptance. She earned the title of witchkiller, and did not shy away from it. She threw herself at the Darkhold and had nobody around, not a coven nor her wife, to stop her from succumbing to dark magic. For the past two centuries, she has taken her grief and resentment out on the witches who spurn her, stealing their power. And, it seems, has never trusted anyone ever again.

She knows Agatha will not accept any form of comfort, considering how she spat at Rio earlier for showing sympathy, so instead she offers, “I can cut your hair for you, if you’d like.”

There’s a beat of silence, where Agatha stays motionless, but then her throat bobs in a swallow as she nods shyly. “Have your skills improved since the last time you took scissors to my head?”

“Wouldn’t know,” Rio replies simply. “Haven’t had any more practice. You’re the only person whose hair I’ve cut.”

“That’s a lie.”

Rio cocks her head. “Is it?”

Agatha won’t look at her now, averting her gaze. “You cut his hair,” she whispers. Bringing up Nicholas, even though she made Rio promise not to.

Rio’s blood turns cold. How does she know about that? She used to visit Nicky as he was growing up, but only ever when he and Agatha were asleep. On the rare night when there were no souls for her to ferry, she would watch over them, shielding them from the wind and cold, very occasionally leaving a flower bloom behind for one of them to find. Nondescript, native flowers, to avoid arousing Agatha’s suspicions, because she was terrified of Death visiting their ailing son, petrified that every day could be his last.

“Once,” she responds truthfully, her voice hoarse.

On one of her visits, when Nicky was just two months old, Rio had sneakily snipped a tiny little lock of his hair, and Agatha’s too, casting them in black volcanic glass to form a gem of obsidian. She has worn it over her heart ever since, as a good luck charm and a reminder of whom her heart belongs to.

“It took forever for his hair to grow in as a baby,” Agatha muses aloud, sounding forlorn. “You really thought I would miss the fact that it just disappeared one night? Clean cut, as well?” Her lips twitch in a facade of a sad smile. “You weren’t subtle, Rio.”

She didn’t think that Agatha would have noticed. “It wasn’t for anything sinister, if you were worried.” A vast majority of black magic involves the usage of hair.

“I wasn’t.” Her wife draws patterns in the water with her pruny fingertips. “I did the same.”

She raises her hand to place it over the point just above her sternum, where her locket containing that tiny lock of their son’s hair usually rests. She’s not wearing it right now, having taken it off for the bath, and she no doubt misses the sensation of the metal pressed against her skin, warmed by her body heat.

Rio doesn’t know what to say, at a loss for words. Instead, she rinses the conditioner out of her wife’s hair, combing through the strands thoroughly to wash it out. She really had no clue that Agatha figured out, all those years ago, that she was visiting her and Nicky at night.

At the time, she was determined to keep her drop-ins secret, scared that Agatha would lose her mind if she woke up to find Death looming over their son. But Agatha knew Rio visited them. She knew since Nicky was a baby. She never said anything, never called out, never purposefully stayed awake to talk to her. Was she just as uncertain about the appropriate etiquette as Rio? Was she fearful of acknowledging Death’s visits? Rio regrets that Agatha was right to be intimidated; it was after one of Rio’s late-night visits when Nicky was six that Agatha woke up with the rigid, cold body of her dead son next to her.

As Rio picks up the comb once again to de-tangle her wife’s freshly washed hair, she hears Agatha grumble, barely audible, “This is so degrading.”

She pauses, and twists Agatha’s long hair in her hand until it’s in a ponytail and she has a strong, firm grasp of it. It gives her total control over her wife’s head movements. Tugging on the ponytail pulls on her roots and stretches her scalp in a way that Rio knows from experience feels delicious. Judging by the faint gasp that escapes Agatha’s open mouth, she agrees. She pulls down on her hair until Agatha’s forced to look up and make direct eye contact with her.

Her cheeks are flushed, her cerulean eyes wide and nervous. Her fingers dig into her bare knees, hands twitching. Rio does not doubt that Agatha is internally debating whether she would prefer to slide them between her thighs or wrap them around the green witch’s throat.

“It’s not, Agatha,” Rio tells her sharply. “You survived being attacked by the Scarlet Witch. Not many people can claim that. It’s something you can be proud of. This weakness and lack of power, they’re temporary. You will be that formidable witch feared and revered by the world once again. So quit it with the brooding. ¿Claro?”

Agatha responds with a slow blink, just like how a cat shows affection, her tongue wetting her dry lips. “Sí, claro,” she answers huskily. “Entiendo, mi Señora.”

“Bueno.” Releasing her grip on her wife’s hair, she rakes her fingers and the comb through it a few more times. She manifests a small length of twine so she can tie it in a loose messy bun on top of her head, so that the ends don’t dip back into the water. “Hair’s done.”

Agatha doesn’t thank her, but she does shoot her a grateful look, which is more meaningful than hearing the words. She slumps down beneath the water up to her shoulders again to enjoy the heat of the water whilst it lasts. It will do her good to sit and absorb the minerals and ions from the salts added to the water, as they’ll ease her muscle tension and encourage blood flow.

“Did you bring my make-up bag?” she asks.

Rio halts, in the middle of fishing out the muslin bag full of oatstraw and plants from the water, since they have done their job. “Chest at the end of the bed,” she remembers.

“There’s hair oil in there.”

She raises an eyebrow. “Is there meant to be a question in there somewhere too?”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “Please will you work it through my hair?” she emphasizes.

Rio smirks. “So polite.”

“I do have manners, I just don’t see the point in using them most of the time,” Agatha sniffs, sinking deeper into the water until it touches her chin.

Well, she’s already spent an absurd amount of time washing Agatha’s hair today; she might as well finish the job properly. Plus, it will give Rio an extra opportunity to touch her wife again, and she’ll snap up any opportunity to lay her hands on Agatha and feel the warmth of her skin again.

“What does it look like?” she questions, squinting as she tries to remember its general shape and color. The only irritating part of summoning items is that a witch needs to have a solid image of things in their mind. Rio may be Death, but she’s still governed by the laws of the universe when it comes to magic.

“You’ll know it when you see it,” Agatha replies nonchalantly. “If you can’t summon it with magic then just use your legs and go get it yourself.” When Rio doesn’t move, refusing to leave Agatha by herself in the bath, she assures her, “I’ll be fine alone for the minute it takes you to run to the bedroom and back.” She must see the uncertainty on Rio’s face, because she smiles with faux innocence and offers, “I’ll let you share the bed with me again.”

Cosmic entities are usually immune to bribery. Death, however, very much believes in the phrase happy wife, happy life; the chance to earn Agatha’s favor and be allowed back into their marital bed, which she was banished from last night, is far too enticing for her to resist. She purses her lips. Should she call for support in the form of Señor Scratchy, to babysit Agatha while she’s gone? No… it’s sixty seconds. Agatha should be fine, for sixty seconds.

“Don’t move,” she orders, pointing at Agatha seriously.

She darts out of the bathroom and into the bedroom, light on her feet. When she returns, with the bottle of Agatha’s argan hair oil in hand, it immediately slips from her grasp and clatters to the ground. When she walks in, she’s horrified to see her wife unconscious beneath the water.

Agatha has passed out and slipped down the side of the bath so her mouth and nose are covered by water, meaning that she can’t breathe and is on the verge of drowning. Her lifeline is once again faltering, her soul warbling in distress.

Yelling in shock, Rio snakes her arms around Agatha’s torso and hauls her out of the bath, not caring how incensed her wife will be when she finds out about her touching her without her consent. Water splashes everywhere, and Rio herself gets soaked. Lowering Agatha onto the fluffy bath mat, flat on her back, Rio immediately begins CPR.

Performing rescue breaths on her unconscious wife was not how Rio imagined kissing Agatha again after centuries apart.

Doing the CPR helps force the water up from Agatha’s lungs while also resulting in Rio’s saliva, with all its healing properties, entering her mouth. Thirty seconds later, Agatha is half-conscious, coughing up cloudy, green-tinged water.

Rio groans in relief as she helps roll her wife over, seeing her lifeline snap back into a strong, rigid cord. She wraps her arms around the spirit witch’s waist and bears her weight so that Agatha can hunch down on all fours and hack her lungs out. She starts to gag ferociously at one point, and Rio cringes, prepared for body fluids to go spewing everywhere, but by some miracle, Agatha manages to hold herself back from throwing up.

Once she’s mostly stopped heaving, her wife flops face down onto the soaked bath mat, breathing laboriously. Rio shoves her into the recovery position, because she is not having Agatha suffocate on the stupid mat after surviving drowning.

“For fuck’s sake,” she snarls. “Stop nearly dying!”

“I’m not doing it on purpose,” Agatha gasps out, as she continues to cough. “Is it getting you off?”

Getting her off? Rio wants to punch the fucking wall. Agatha thinks that it would be arousing for her to be forced to watch her wife’s lifeline sever and her soul detach itself from her body? “If this is you trying to flirt with me then it’s a bit too extreme, even for me, and I’m Death itself. I much prefer you alive and breathing, Agatha.”

“Noted,” she huffs. Agatha narrows her bloodshot eyes, and glances up at Rio with a reproachful look, licking her lips as if she recognizes the taste. “Were you kissing me?”

Rio blinks, thrown. That’s what Agatha cares about?! “Rescue breaths.”

The spirit witch glares at her. “You did kiss me!”

“I was saving your life!”

Agatha has the audacity to slap her. It doesn’t hurt, of course, but Rio stares at her, thunderstruck. Nearly 14 billion years of existence, and no creature has ever mystified her as much as Agatha Harkness.

“You nearly drowned just now and you’re throwing a tantrum over the fact that I had to kiss you to give you CPR?” she says in disbelief.

“I wouldn’t have drowned,” Agatha denies, but then buckles into a coughing fit once again. “And CPR doesn’t require rescue breaths anymore. You’re a pervert, Rio Vidal, kissing an unconscious woman. Taking advantage of me. How dare you.”

“How dare I -? Oh, fuck you, Agatha.” Rio crumples against the side of the bath, muttering furiously, “‘I’ll be fine alone for a minute’ and then you try to drown yourself in a bathtub. Honestly. A minute. Can’t even leave you alone for sixty seconds! At this rate, it’s a miracle you didn’t accidentally smother yourself in your sleep last night.”

Maybe from now on, she should do her ‘wellness checks’, as Agatha nicknamed them, every ten minutes instead of an hour. Hopefully, if Agatha was sincere in her deal to let Rio back into their bed, she can make sure that her heart doesn’t randomly give out in her sleep.

She brought Agatha here to keep her safe so she can heal, not to endure numerous near-death experiences. But… perhaps those near-death experiences go hand in hand with cohabitating with Death herself. Agatha has a flagrant disregard for safety and the rules, and a non-existent sense of self-preservation. This is going to be much harder than she thought.

“What can I say, I like to live dangerously,” Agatha chokes out from her position curled up on the floor, wet and shivering. “I hate this,” she croaks. “And I hate -”

“Me, yes, I know,” Rio sighs.

“No.” Agatha shakes her head, with a heavy, wheezing sigh. “Not what I was going to say.” She pauses and then adds hastily, “But - yes - that too.”

“What do you need?” she asks, delicately sweeping Agatha’s wet hair away from her face.

Agatha shifts, agitated by the question because she doesn’t seem to know the answer. “Hold me?” she finally says, sounding small and ashamed. “I’m cold.”

Oh! That’s a change of heart, considering she was slapping Rio a minute ago. Well, if she’s asking for it…

Rio shuffles closer so she can help her wife sit up. “I’ve got you,” she assures her, embracing her tightly.

Too exhausted and shaken to be angry, Agatha huddles into her, her head tucking beneath Rio’s chin.

“Don’t read into this,” her wife mumbles. “I’m only letting you hug me because you’re like a space heater.”

“Of course,” Rio says patiently, glad that Agatha can’t see the smug smile that’s spread across her face.

“You’re always so warm,” Agatha says, dazed. “You’d think Death would be cold but you - you’re hot.”

“Thank you very much.”

“Temperature wise, Rio.”

“I’m both. And not everything that dies is cold,” Rio comments. “Stars burn brighter and hotter as they decay.”

The spirit witch snorts. “Makes sense. You’re a cosmic entity, after all.”

Rio pretends not to feel her partner’s hands latch onto her arms, trapping them in place, so that the green witch cannot release her from the hug if she tries. How long has it been since she held Agatha like this, she wonders. How long has it been since Agatha has let herself be held? She’s so desperately touch-starved, and yet touch-adverse at the same time, which creates a real conundrum for herself. She really is like one of those grouchy cats who like to crawl onto people’s laps and cuddle with them, wanting to be close, but hissing and snarling if petted, because that’s too close.

She jerks concernedly when she hears the rattling coughs that burst out of her wife’s mouth, followed up by asthmatic-like puffs and arduous breathing. “Does it hurt to breathe?” she questions.

“Chest feels weird,” Agatha coughs.

“That would be the water in your lungs,” Rio murmurs worriedly. Gathering her green magic and using her fingers to draw out the required runes mid-air, she then presses her glowing hand over Agatha’s upper chest. “Hold on, this is going to burn,” she grimaces. “I need to draw it out so you don’t develop pneumonia but it will feel like your lungs are on fire.”

Agatha doesn’t scream as Rio’s magic spreads throughout her organs to purge them of the water she’s inhaled, but she fights against her grip, contorting her body to try and escape Rio’s arms. She does not begin to siphon as she would usually instinctually begin to, because of how damaged her magical core is; a good thing too, considering it would kill her to absorb Rio's magic. Perhaps part of Agatha also recognizes that Rio is trying to help her, not attack her, so she's holding back. Guilt lashes through the green witch as her wife silently sobs, but she continues to funnel her power through Agatha’s lungs to cleanse them, knowing that it will be better for her in the long run.

She hangs on tight, holding Agatha through it, shushing her gently when an agonized whimper tears from her throat. The witch is left trembling all over, hand curled into Rio’s turtleneck, her frantic breaths hot against her neck. Rio strokes over her wet hair to try and comfort her, heavy with remorse.

“Was that spell originally invented to inflict torture, by any chance?” Agatha eventually croaks.

It was actually invented shortly after the Salem trials commenced, as a last-resort spell to save witches condemned to death by drowning. “Anything else feel weird?” Rio asks her wife concernedly, clicking her fingers aggressively in Agatha’s face when she begins to nod off, all of her energy gone. “Agatha, focus up.”

“Head,” she manages to grit out.

“Headache or something else?”

Agatha kind of just shrugs weakly in response. Rio eyes her, troubled. Agatha seemed to be coping with her headache well, throughout the bath. She rarely experiences migraines, and when she does, she’s completely light and touch-sensitive, so they would know if that was the cause. From what Rio can discern, her wife lost consciousness rapidly, probably within seconds of her departing the bathroom. The last time Agatha fell unconscious that quickly was yesterday, when she suddenly fainted during their fight… because she started having a seizure.

“What do you remember before passing out?” she asks urgently.

“Started feeling numb and then couldn’t move. Locked up and then went black,” Agatha mumbles, her tired voice muffled. Rio’s anxiety intensifies. It must translate in her body language, because Agatha says, subdued and frightened, “That’s not good, is it?”

No. It’s not good. It’s not good at all. If Agatha starts to suffer from frequent seizures, Rio has no clue what to do. She’s Death, not a fucking doctor. She doesn’t know enough about human brains and neurological conditions to heal them. At what point does she admit to being over her head and take Agatha to a hospital? When she doesn’t wake up, after her next seizure, when it’s too late?

“Seizures are a pretty extreme spell aftermath side effect,” she finally responds, knowing Agatha is growing uneasy in her silence. “There’s a possibility that Wanda did something to your mind when she cast the spell on you, to discourage you from trying to break out from the hex. She probably never anticipated that you actually would manage to break free. Perhaps the cleansing bath accidentally triggered whatever circuit breaker she left behind.”

Agatha struggles against her, attempting to sit up herself. Rio allows her to, but keeps one hand anchored to Agatha’s lower back to support her. She looks bemused, outraged, and scared. “What, you think she left some sort of… fail safe, hidden away in my brain? A kill switch, so her magic could just shut me down if I fought the binding too hard?” she whispers.

She sounds so betrayed. Rio’s heart hurts for her. She thinks that in some twisted, fucked-up way, Agatha did care about Wanda Maximoff. She, like Agatha, was a witch outcast, with powers that were difficult to control, and a tragic past. Agatha most likely saw herself in her. She tried to steal the chaos witch’s powers, yes, but Rio knows that in other universes, their counterparts were friends. Sometimes, much to her jealousy, they were even lovers. But this universe’s Agatha is hers and always will be, and Wanda is gone. She has nothing to worry about.

Rio’s not sure about the kill-switch theory, but it’s the best guess she has for now. “If it’s any consolation, I doubt she intended for it to be such an aggressive deterrent. The only way we’ll know for certain is if we astral project and travel into your subconscious to check.”

Agatha instantly shuts that down. “No. No, we’re not doing that. You are not allowed in my head.” She turns away, quivering all over. “It’s - you don’t know if that’s true, if that’s what Wanda really did. You’re theorizing. The seizures, they might just be stress. That’s a thing, isn’t it? Stress-induced seizures. So - so they might just go away on their own, as I rest and heal.”

Rio bites her lip. There is a chance that Agatha’s seizures are down to the physical and mental stress she’s currently going through, as a result of breaking free of mind control. But if they’re a result of the mind control itself, then they will not magically vanish. They’ll continue. And they could kill her.

She understands that Agatha is far too emotionally fragile right now to give Rio access to her thoughts and memories - the deepest and darkest parts of her mind - and is partially in denial about her vulnerability, so she doesn’t push. Removing whatever metaphysical kill switch the Scarlet Witch may have planted in Agatha’s mind will take effort, and cooperation, so she cannot astral project in alone. If Agatha has another seizure, then she will force the issue.

But currently, she’s mostly worried about Agatha developing a cold as she freezes her ass off on the bathroom floor.

“Alright,” the green witch acquiesces. “Resting and healing, for now. But we will need to revisit this conversation if it gets any worse.” Agatha nods in agreement. “Let’s get you back into bed so you can get a headstart on that resting bit, shall we?”

She stands, and scoops her wife up off the floor into her arms to carry her bridal style back into the bedroom. Agatha yelps and throws her arms around Rio’s shoulders, clinging to her as the now lukewarm towel dangles from her hand. Her robe is also left behind.

Agatha didn’t make the bed earlier, so it’s easy to carefully lower her to the floor, gently towel her off, and then ease her onto the mattress. She sits with her bare legs dangling off the edge, head bowed with exhaustion.

“Do you need help getting dressed?” she asks, ruffling through the drawers to find underwear and pajamas. She finds a set of midnight blue silk ones she brought over from Westview.

“No,” Agatha argues weakly, but upon trying to stand to get her panties on, and collapsing back onto the bed, breathless, admits, “Yes.”

Rio nods, and says nothing as she aids her wife, bundling her into the warm set of fresh pajamas. Agatha tenses with every touch at first, but then relaxes, actually leaning into Rio’s shoulder as Death devotedly does up every individual button of her shirt. Agatha, meanwhile, manages to grab her Triple Goddess locket from where she left it on the bedside table and fasten it back around her neck with trembling fingers.

Rio kneels to slide fuzzy socks on her feet to keep them from freezing, smiling when Agatha wiggles her toes. It does not seem to escape Agatha’s notice that Rio lingers, knelt on the floor in front of her, for far too long.

“You’re enjoying this,” her wife says accusingly, in a scratchy, gravelly voice. “You like me being powerless and needing you to help me do basic things like bathe and dress and put socks on. Don’t lie. You probably think this is funny.”

“I like taking care of you,” Rio answers honestly. “I don’t like that the reason why I have to is that you’re sick. Helpless and needy is only a good look on you when it’s a position you’ve put yourself in and there’s a safeword in place.” She takes hold of Agatha’s freezing hands, noting that she doesn’t flinch, this time, so she can rub them between her palms to warm them. “And I don’t find it funny at all. If you still had your purple, it might be, a teeny bit.” She spreads her fingers apart to demonstrate, which prompts Agatha to huff in faint amusement. “But you were mentally tortured for three years, and stripped of your faculties and power. Nothing you could have done to the Scarlet Witch would have meant you deserved this. I’m mostly just relieved that I’m the one who found you.”

“What would you have done?” Agatha asks with a frown. “If the Salem Seven got to me first?”

“Killed them,” she replies simply.

“You’re not allowed to kill.”

“No.” As Death, she is only allowed to ferry souls who are ready to depart their dead mortal vessels. Rio is the natural order of all things, and it is against the natural order to speed that process up, for Death to claim a soul too early.

Agatha blinks slowly. “But you would have killed them anyway?”

“Yes.” Rio squeezes her hands before letting go. “I’ve broken the rules for you before. You’re the only exception, Agatha.”

“Would you be punished in some way for it?” her wife asks, curious and yet her expression full of dread.

“In some way,” Rio agrees, trying not to show on her face that she knows precisely what would happen to her.

After all, she spent six years holding back from claiming her son’s soul that rightfully belonged to the Realm of the Dead, and was living entirely on borrowed - no, stolen - time. She gave Nicky as many years with his mother as she could, and then faced the consequences of those actions with her head held high.

“But you’d still do it anyway? Because… because you love me?” Agatha says, her mouth twisting around the ‘L’ word as if it’s almost unrecognizable. At least she’s not outright denying that Rio loves her anymore. She seems to have begrudgingly accepted it.

Rio nods. “You’re worth it.”

Agatha visibly clams up, her blunt, ragged nails digging into her arms. “How’d you decide that? Make one of those fucking pros vs cons charts and tally up all my charming personality quirks and sexual prowess against my psychopathic tendencies and general shitty behavior? Who am I kidding, you accepted all the witches I killed as gifts, the fact that I’m a serial killer is why you were attracted to me in the first place.”

Regarding her wife calmly, not rising to her cutting words, Rio explains, “You looked Death in the eye and freely offered her your companionship. You didn’t run, or cower, or plead for mercy or power. You gifted me bodies, yes, but also your heart, your body, your womb. You bore me a son. And you willingly bound your soul to a cosmic entity, for eternity.”

She frees Agatha’s fingers from where they are scoring deep red indents on her wrists, and raises each one to her lips, pressing a kiss to each palm before setting them back down to rest limply on her thighs. Agatha watches with wide eyes in silence as she kisses the marks on her arms too, wiping away the scratches and nicks left behind.

Rio pauses when she reaches Agatha’s shoulders, raising her head so their faces are inches apart. Agatha is flushed. She looks beautiful, so flustered and speechless. Rio wants to kiss her, but settles on swiping her thumb reverently across her blushing cheek instead. “You are the only creature, in this universe and all those beyond, who is worthy of Death’s love,” she says softly.

“Despite what happened?” Agatha says, her voice cracking with emotion.

“Despite anything and everything,” Rio tells her firmly.

Her wife exhales sharply, and it's an amazed, tremulous sound. “Oh.”

Rio rises to her feet. “Now… will you let me steal one of your sweaters?”

“Not like I can stop you,” Agatha replies, with a tiny, wobbly smile. It’s as good a 'yes' as Rio is going to get. But the fact it is not a ‘no’ means that her wife isn’t against it. She’s not complaining about her stealing her clothes, so it’s a win.

The spirit witch sways a little, watching with half-lidded eyes as Rio fishes out one of Agatha’s sweatshirts. It’s too big for her, but she likes that it smells of her wife, and she yanks it over her head to cover her bralette. She’s surprised, really, that Agatha hasn’t made some sort of snarky comment about Rio stripping off as soon as she found the opportunity.

“Lie back,” Rio urges her when she returns to Agatha’s side, poking her shoulder.

But Agatha shakes her head, refusing. “Hair oil,” she demands.

Rio sighs in exasperation. “Really?”

Agatha looks seconds away from falling asleep, but still manages a killer pout. Rio gives in, because her wife is cute when she’s pouty, and massages the expensive argan oil into her wet locks, before drying it with a wave of her hand. No hairdryers needed when one has magic.

“Where’ve you been, señor?” Rio asks in annoyance, when Agatha’s familiar appears out of nowhere. His little bunny tail twitches, and his whiskers quiver. “Miss all the dramatics, and only show up for cuddles with your mom in the aftermath, huh? I see where your priorities lie.”

“Don’t call me his mom,” Agatha snorts. “That’s wrong on so many levels.”

“Here, your menace of a rabbit wants snuggles,” Rio scoffs, lifting the soft little creature up onto the bed so he can bound over to his mistress and snuffle over her nervously. “Could have used your help earlier when your witch was drowning, you dumbfuck.”

Agatha frowns, placing her hands over the bunny’s ears. “Don’t insult Señor Scratchy. He’s a delicate soul.”

“He’s a demon,” Rio deadpans.

“Demons have feelings too,” Agatha counters. “You should know, since you are one.”

She’s not. She is much more than a demon. She is multitudes. “I’m Death, baby. He’s the equivalent of a demonic cockroach.” Señor Scratchy kicks at her, thumping her thigh. Rio resists the urge to throw him off the bed. “Oh, it’s war, cabrón.”

Another dose of the reinvigoration elixir is downed without complaint, and Rio slips her a couple of valium pills as well. Witches have a lot of great healing spells, but nothing beats good old diazepam. Agatha scowls, but swallows them down when Rio shows her the little information packet that came with the tablets, saying that they can be used as rescue medication post-seizure episodes. It helps that the pills act as sedatives too.

“Get in,” Agatha mutters, when Rio sends a pointed, questioning look, and then glances at her side of the bed. “Don’t stare at me while I sleep, okay? Pervert.”

“As you wish, milady,” she replies with an amused grin. She draws the drapes to cast the room into darkness, switches off the lamp, and then slips beneath the sheets next to her wife. The stupid little rabbit is curled up on the pillow between them. “I’ll wake you in time for dinner.”

“Fine.” A pause, and then a small, reluctant, “Thank you. For saving me, earlier. And for... being so patient with me.”

Rio grins. “What was that? Don't think I heard properly. Did Agatha Harkness just utter the words 'thank' and 'you' in the same sentence?”

“I’m not saying it again.”

Agatha is fast asleep by the time Rio responds, a few minutes later, voice deep with affection and longing, “Anything for you, my love.”

Chapter End Notes

cw: near drowning experience, performance of CPR, near vomiting

Chapter 5

Chapter Notes

im kind of in disbelief that this fic has somehow hit 1k kudos!? that's amazing!! thank you so much to all of you for your support - and your patience considering how long it's been since the last update. a long chapter this week to thank you!

i will warn you in advance that this is going to be a long haul. is there so much thing as a slow burn angst? because the next few chapters will be rough. importantly, i have updated the tags accordingly. ultimately this is the calm before the storm, so buckle in :) (but i can promise happy ending)

usual content warnings in the tags apply and there is mention/discussion of sexual BDSM and related kinks.

I have been convinced to open a tumblr so you can message/ask questions separately from the comments! https://www.tumblr.com/anonfandombandit

Rio lounges in bed, absentmindedly stroking over her wife’s hair as she watches her sleep with one hand, and twirling her scythe blade in her other like some kind of celestial fidget toy.

Agatha slumbers deeply due to her fatigue, and snuffles adorably as she curls up next to Death, buried under the covers. Her bunny familiar is snoozing too, pressed up against his witch’s sternum.

Her wife sleeps exactly the same way she has always done; on her side, one arm cushioning and protecting her head, knees pulled up to be level with her hips. Her other hand is gripping tightly onto Rio’s borrowed sweater, as if to reassure herself that her wife isn’t going to abandon her.

Agatha exhales, emitting the cutest, softest little noises as she turns her face into Rio’s touches, like a cat pleading to be pet. She cranes her neck, exposing the long length of her vulnerable throat.

Rio tightens her grasp around her knife. There’s a tiny greedy voice at the back of her mind that wants her to run the very tip of her blade down, nicking Agatha’s fragile skin and causing beads of blood to erupt. Those droplets of blood would then run down her throat in thin rivulets for Rio to lap up with her tongue, tracing upwards until she could heal the cuts with gentle kisses.

Blood play was something her wife was all too eager to explore with Rio after their soul bond, because it would allow Rio to tune into her emotions and experience the sweet biting pain, in a way that Death had never felt before. But Agatha is weak enough already, and her body will not tolerate any blood loss. It would undoubtedly wake her, and Rio much prefers her asleep right now, so she can watch her.

If this were any other person, Rio would rapidly get bored of simply lying next to them and waiting for the hours to pass. But Agatha… well, she finds Agatha sleeping fascinating, mostly because of her breathing patterns, microexpressions, and body language as she dreams.

“Mm, what are you dreaming of, mi vida?” she murmurs in a hushed voice, brushing her fingertips lightly over her wife’s furrowed brow. “What’s going on in that mystifying mind of yours?”

For as long as Rio has known Agatha, the spirit witch has had a strange relationship with dreaming. She was plagued by nightmares for the longest time throughout her childhood and early teens, and then a couple of times every week after she killed her mother and Salem coven in self-defense.

Rarely would she experience good, happy, peaceful dreams. And the reason for that is that Agatha primarily dreams of her own memories. When a person has lived as rough a life as Agatha, that results in a lot of night terrors.

As a primordial entity with jurisdiction over souls and the spirit realm, Rio has long since been able to enter people’s minds, and therefore their dreams. They are, of course, reflections of people’s souls; manifestations of a human's thoughts, desires, and expectations.

To welcome another witch into one’s mind is the greatest exercise in trust, as it exposes the witch’s soul. When they married, handfasting under the full moon, they performed a bonding ritual, whereby they linked their souls eternally. It created a permanent and unbreakable connection between the two of them. For Agatha Harkness to open her soul and mind up to another was extraordinary in itself, notwithstanding the fact that she was making herself vulnerable to Death.

Shortly after they married, Agatha gave her permission to bring her out of her nightmares and wake her by slipping into her mind; Rio would interrupt whatever tirade of physical or emotional abuse Evanora and her coven were attacking her with.

The green witch was allowed to partake in Agatha’s good dreams as well, not just her nightmares; sometimes just sitting back and watching her memories like little movies, or influencing them if she wanted, if they were of the NSFW kind.

(Those, predictably, were both Agatha and Rio’s favorite of her dreams. Rio would replace the dream figment of herself and ensure that when Agatha awoke in the mornings, her legs were sore and the sheets suitably soaked beneath her.)

Even when Nicky was born and they stopped seeing each other, Agatha still welcomed her wife into her dreams - albeit rarely. The spirit witch’s dreams about Nicky were Rio’s favorite ones to spy on, because she got to see their son grow up through Agatha’s eyes.

Then, after Nicky’s death, and after their subsequent break-up, Agatha cut her off. Rio, regrettably, took her access to her wife’s thoughts and dreams for granted; she didn’t think that there would be an end to their arrangement - that Agatha would ever shut her out. But the day after Rio ferried Nicky to the afterlife, Agatha raised her mental shields and refused to let Rio back in.

She used her connection to her partner’s soul to check in on her every couple of days, those first few years after their son’s passing. The link formed by their handfasting ceremony allowed her to sense Agatha’s general emotions, even with her mind blocked. Agatha was determined to put on an outward show of despising Rio to her core, but Rio could tell from her everpresent yearning that she still dreamt of her often.

But then, even that connection between them, allowing her to sense her love’s feelings, was crippled. Not severed, as that was impossible, but dampened. It was before Agatha acquired the Darkhold, so Rio knows it wasn’t dark magic of that kind; whatever Agatha did, it was mightily effective, and majorly pissed her off.

Today, Agatha seems to be drifting between dreams, judging by her ever-changing expressions. The magic that was keeping Rio shut out of her dreams before is gone, she can tell. She could force her way in and take a wander through Agatha’s mind and peek in on her if she so wished, but she doesn’t dare to.

Rio no longer has permission to do so, and if Agatha were to sense her and catch her out, she knows that the fragile trust that has scarcely survived between them, and is still ticking along, will shatter entirely. Agatha does not want her astral projecting into her subconscious, so she will definitely not want Rio taking a gander through her dreams.

“Are you dreaming of me?” she wonders aloud. She reckons that there’s a high possibility, considering the events of the past two days.

Agatha mumbles nonsensically in her sleep, eyes flickering beneath her lids. “Rio,” she thinks she hears her wife breathe out, but that might be wishful thinking.

Sensing the sun beginning to set outside, Rio banished her blade to its extra-dimensional sheath; she pries her sweater out of Agatha’s fist before scooting to the edge of the mattress.

Agatha has not eaten since breakfast that morning, and will need something nutritious, rich in calories, and easy on the stomach for dinner. Rio could just let her green craft do all the work to magic something up to eat, but she’s never been the best at conjuring food. Maybe it’s because she technically does not need to eat. She enjoys cooking, though, having taught herself how when she and Agatha lived together, and her wife was constantly fatigued from Nicky growing in her belly.

Rio hesitates as she stands, hovering next to the bed; she doesn’t want to leave Agatha alone. If she has a seizure in her sleep, she could stop breathing again, and what if Rio is too late to rush to her side? Her and Agatha’s bond is still strained and weak. In its current state, she won’t be able to tell if Agatha is approaching trouble until the moment occurs. A monitoring spell might work, even if it is invasive.

Snaking her hand around Agatha’s wrist, she closes her eyes and focuses in on her wife’s pulse, until her heartbeat is drumming in her ears. It’s steady and soothing; Rio has had it memorized for centuries.

In fact, there were days when Rio would bury herself in the memory of lying her head on Agatha’s sleeping chest to listen to her heart thrum, to escape the loneliness and emptiness of her realm.

The Realm of the Dead is populated by her reapers and also the souls of the decreased; it acts as a collecting pool, gathering all of the matter and souls of the denizens of the universe. But it’s vast, and dark, and endless.

When Agatha dropped off her radar, Rio no longer had much of a reason to linger on the Earthly plane; she retreated to her realm and immersed herself in her memories of her wife - her gentle but stern hands, her loving embrace, her warm skin and soft lips and, Rio’s favorite, her steady, unique heartbeat.

Focused on the rhythmically pumping organ, Rio reaches out delicately to brush up against Agatha’s soul. It squeals in delight as Death attaches a tiny thread of magic to her wife’s lifeline, that she can easily unweave later when Agatha inevitably notices and demands she remove it.

Now she will be alerted to any distress, whether that be physical or mental. She will be aware of anything bothering Agatha long before it causes her lifeline to trip and fumble.

For good measure, Rio sends a little vine shooting out of her hand to aggressively poke at her wife’s rabbit familiar, where he’s plastered against Agatha’s chest. He jolts awake, batting his paws at the tendril with an annoyed scowl.

“Keep an eye on her,” Rio orders him, pointing at Agatha, who slumbers on serenely. “I need to cook dinner. Don’t let her die in her sleep. If you do, you’ll be tomorrow night’s meal.”

Señor Scratchy eyes her beadily but releases a little huff, which she assumes to be an agreement. Flipping him off, Rio checks on her sleeping wife one last time, tucking pillows around her body so she doesn’t accidentally roll over and smother herself in her pillow. She then adjusts the blankets so they cover her body, brushing Agatha’s thick wavy hair away from her face.

This time, Rio doesn’t hesitate to bend down and plant a kiss on her wife’s cheek. If the only time Agatha will allow her to show her physical affection is when she’s asleep, then she will unashamedly take advantage of that.

The temperature outside is beginning to drop along with the sun’s descent beneath the horizon, and clouds are blocking out the last remaining sunlight of the day, threatening rain throughout the night later.

Aware of the chill that is seeping through the cracks in the window frame and leaching through the floor, Rio stokes a very small fire in the grate opposite the bed, casting a charm to keep it burning low and contained.

She hears Agatha shift around on the bed, emitting a soft sigh; even unconscious, she is able to instinctually sense a change in her environment, just in case it presents a threat to her.

Once she’s quietly padded out into the kitchen, Rio rolls up the sleeves of Agatha’s sweater and gets to work. Cooking is one of those mindless chores that she learned how to do once she realized, when she and Agatha started living together so long ago, that her wife is absolutely dismal at it.

And she’s dismal by choice. If Agatha actually put some effort into it, she would definitely be able to produce something edible. Unfortunately, Agatha used to find it somewhat hilarious to create as much chaos in the kitchen as possible, while Rio watched on in disbelief and wonder that her partner found a way to break the laws of physics and burn water.

She dissects the chicken in the fridge and sears the pieces off in avocado oil, in a giant stock pot loaded on the stove. Roughly chopped carrots, onions, and celery are added and fried off. She pours a carton of bone broth to cover the chicken, with a handful of herbs that Rio summons from her garden outside, spices, and a teaspoon of bouillon powder.

Now, it only needs to simmer for twenty minutes to cook the chicken pieces. The soup will make for a simple but hopefully not too bland meal, and should help by boosting Agatha’s immune system and aiding her in sleeping better.

While the soup simmers, she heads into the bathroom and waves her hand; her magic sweeps through with a crackle of green lightning, emptying and cleaning the bath of the cold murky water. She summons the wet towel from within the bedroom to set it on the towel rail to dry. The cottage is old and cold enough already, and she doesn’t want any lingering dampness making Agatha’s sickness worse.

Returning to the kitchen to set the table, Rio lays out cutlery and glasses of water on the table. She fishes out a pair of wine glasses and sets them aside on the counter to fill later. If Agatha is in a prickly mood when she wakes up, a small glass of chilled white wine will no doubt cheer her up.

She fishes out one of her favorite old vases, and blooms stunning white chrysanthemums from her palms. One of her favorite flowers; white, to symbolize her devoted love, loyalty, and honesty, and the particular variety she has chosen blooms in colder months, representing Agatha’s ability to survive and thrive in challenging conditions. Agatha may be sick and powerless now, but she will fight through this period of adversity and come out the other side as a beautiful and formidable witch queen.

The spirit witch knows the meaning of flowers - it was one of the first things she dedicated herself to learning, after she fell in love and married the Green Witch. Flowers are a love language that Rio adores to use with her wife, and Agatha loves to interpret her little floral missives.

Rio hopes that Agatha understands the message that she is sending with the chrysanthemums - that Rio is committed to her, and committed to repairing their relationship; she believes that their love is strong enough to survive the hardships they have suffered through, to bring them back together at the end.

She is busy picking the steaming hot chicken off the bones to drop them back into the soup stock when she feels a streak of anxiety coursing through her body. She hears a rapid heartbeat thudding in her ears. It’s the monitoring spell, activating. She freezes, completely still, and then immediately magics her hands clean and rushes back into the bedroom upon hearing faint whimpers, and the rabbit’s distressed bleating.

Agatha is tossing and turning on the mattress, cold sweat beaded on her forehead, which is creased with anguish. Her wife is desperately grasping at the sheets with white-knuckled fists, which are tangled around her legs from her thrashing. Every couple of seconds, a petrified, panicked little whine escapes her lips, often accompanied by full-body shivers.

At this point, Rio would typically dive into her wife’s mind and ease her out of the nightmare, but since she doesn’t have Agatha’s consent, that’s not an option.

“No,” she’s mumbling urgently, her voice slurred but scared. “No… please, stop. Can… be good. Please, I can… good, I can be…”

My own crown? Do I get to give orders?” she asks eagerly. “There must be some afterlife perks to being married to Death.”

“What can I say? Queen Agatha Harkness has a good ring to it,” she says in a sing-song voice, lifting her chin triumphantly.

Her reapers probably would be all too happy to donate power to Agatha to stay in her and Rio’s good books. “My subjects’ fondness for you is the only reason I can afford to stay with you here for so long. You’ll have to occupy yourself on the days I have to go to work.”

Solve newspaper crosswords. Paint. Throw pottery. Do some fucking baking or even gardening - so long as you don’t ruin my plants.”

Her wife might try and purposefully piss her off by spraying pesticides on them, knowing her. And the baking is a bad idea, in reality; Agatha might burn the cottage to the ground just attempting to bake cookies.

Agatha looks revolted. She pushes the half-empty bowl of soup away. “I think I would rather chop my own arms off than subject myself to the New York Times daily crossword. And if you think I would willingly get down on my knees in the dirt to play around with weeds, then you’ve got another thing coming. I’m no green witch, and you won’t catch me dead with a trowel in my hand, unless I’m using it to bash somebody’s head in.”

It’s always deliciously disastrous.”

“Agatha…” she says warningly. “You’ll hurt herself.”

“Shut up,” her wife snarls.

Rio winces in sympathy when Agatha’s breathing grows ragged and pained as she tries to draw on her injured magical core, and prepares herself to step in, lest Agatha start to actually cause harm to herself. But she doesn’t. Her hands flop limply onto the counter in defeat.

“Hey, no existential crises before dessert,” she jokes. But Agatha just stares at her, spaced out and anxious. Rio’s shoulders slump. “Agatha, your entire life since we parted cannot have just been scamming covens to siphon their powers, collecting grimoires and magical objects, and studying the fucking Darkhold.” It would be immensely sad if that were the case.

“No, some of it entailed triggering disasters and starting riots for shits and giggles, and selling binding spells and faux healing potions to make a quick buck,” she snaps, straight away on the defensive. But when Rio nods, quirking an eyebrow to prompt her to go on, Agatha appears to wilt. The fight drains out of her, and she looks broken. “Rio, my whole existence has involved magic. I - I don't know what to do without it. The only reason I’ve survived past infanthood is because of it. Who even am I without my purple?” she croaks.

Agatha has tied both to magic, the study and hoarding of it, since she escaped her attempted execution by her mother and coven. She taught herself spirit craft and became a masterful scholar in matters of dark magic.

For a time, she gained other roles, and had other aims and goals in life; she became a wife, and a mother. She dedicated herself to not just her craft, but to love and motherhood. But then she lost Nicky - and she lost Rio too. So as a coping mechanism, the trauma too much for her mind to handle, she funneled all of her energy into becoming the most powerful, knowledgeable, and skilled witch in the world. To block out the agony of losing her family.

The Scarlet Witch, however, knocked her down. Not just a few pegs, but stripped her flag off the ship’s pole entirely. Now, powerless and unable to pursue restoring her reserves whilst her magical core is damaged, she is at a complete loss for what to do. She can no longer hyperfocus on witchcraft to avoid that gaping hole in her heart.

She is being forced to confront and process her emotions regarding the fracturing of her and Rio’s relationship, and the death of their son. And Agatha is petrified. She does not think that Agatha is awful, but saying that would be contrary and invite Agatha to quarrel with her, so Rio responds, “Then reflect on the past, and not the present. You may think you’re a horrible person now, but what about in the past?”

Agatha’s face contorts into one of panic. “No. No, I don’t - I don’t want to think about that.”

She sighs, rubbing her thumb over the spirit witch’s knuckles. “I know it hurts, sweetheart, but pain is the best teacher. If you resist it, you will never accept it. Without acceptance, there’s no understanding.”

“I don’t need to understand my pain in order for it to be real,” Agatha argues, her expression bleak. “Sometimes there is no understanding. Rio shakes her head. What Agatha is describing is not at all healthy, and screams of denial, but it’s all she’s known to do to survive. Her grief after Nicky’s passing was so great, so all-encompassing and agonizing , that Agatha did the only thing she could: she shoved her crushing heartbreak and sadness into a box and locked it away.

Only when her emotions were too great, when she experienced a trauma trigger, did she allow them to explode outwards, and her suffering was overlaid with rage and hatred.

“And let the memories die with it?” she says gently. “I don’t think you want to forget the events that made you the person you are today, Agatha.” She stretches out her hand, fingers brushing over her wife’s, coiled around the locket containing their son’s lock of hair. “You don’t want to forget him. Or us. Do you?”

Agatha sniffles, releasing her locket to frustratedly wipe at her wet eyes. “Of fucking course not.”

Rio withdraws her hands. She so badly wants to pull her wife into a hug, but she has a feeling it would not go down too well currently. Instead, she rests her fingertips on Agatha’s knee, offering silent support. “Do some soul-searching, explore new interests,” she suggests lightly. “Just let me know if you need anything and I’ll conjure it for you.”

“You’ll help me?” the spirit witch asks quietly, looking up through her eyelashes at Rio, mortified but also awed.

“Unconditionally,” she swears.

Agatha appraises her wordlessly, and after a minute or so, swallows heavily, nodding. She believes her.

Rio breathes out in relief. It’s another very small step towards healing. A branch that she’s been steadily and warily holding out, that her wife has finally touched the other end of. Agatha is accepting her help and it feels utterly monumental.

The green witch sees no point in dragging it out, so utilizes magic to wash the dishes and wipe down the table top and sides. Seeing as her wife was somewhat subdued after their conversation at the end of their meal, Rio seeks a simple way to lift her mood in the form of dessert.

Agatha would never admit it, but she has developed quite a sweet tooth over the centuries. She reckons it’s because of all the wild blueberries that Agatha used to forage; they were small, easy to collect, and rich in nutrients.

Conjuring a bowl of fresh apples, Rio cores and slices them before tossing them with brown sugar, cornstarch, and winter spices, adding in a handful of cranberries. She uses her powers over decomposition to carefully speed up the maceration of the fruit; tipping the bowl into a buttered baking dish, she sprinkles a layer of oaty crumble over the top before sliding it into the oven.

When she goes in search of her wife, following the link created by the monitoring spell, she finds Agatha reclined on the couch, leafing through one of Rio’s books on green craft on the sofa arm. She’s dragged one of their old tattered woolen blankets out and draped it over her lap and her bunny. Señor Scratchy is lying starfished on his back like a tiny fluffy arrogant diva, exposing his furry belly for Agatha to rub.

She’s still nowhere near as strong and healthy as she used to be, and there’s a gaping hole where her magic should be, but Agatha feels much more emotionally stable, unlike before. Being around Rio still sets her on edge a little, but she’s no longer so irritable and upset that she will lash out at her at every opportunity.

When she approaches, Agatha glances up at her with a blank expression. Smiling softly, Rio reaches out to push a straggling strand of her wife’s dark hair behind her ear. Agatha flinches, at first, but then, after Rio’s touch remains tentative and gentle, she turns her face minutely to nudge into her palm.

“I don’t know, can you?”

She rolls her eyes. “May I sit, please?”

It’s an ironic statement, considering the page she’s reading. Elder is used for protection, like hawthorn and brown, to ward off evil spirits and hostile sorcery - notably siphon magic. Witches have long since believed that elder must be harvested with respect and patience, thanking the tree for its bounty. Agatha would probably find that immensely amusing.

“As the original Green Witch, I assure you, I am The Big Deal,” Rio winks.

Agatha fails to stifle her smile of amusement. “You wish. You know most people don’t even know that Death is a witch, let alone a green witch. Your kind are rarer than amur leopards.”

She scans the diagram of the elder tree, having to lean forward and squint a little, as if she’s struggling to read the smaller text.

“I think somebody needs glasses now her magic isn’t automatically fixing her terrible eyesight,” Rio laughs. She summons a pair of generic black square reading glasses and offers them to the spirit witch, who ignores them. “Don’t strain yourself, honey. C’mon, I’m sure you’ll look super hot in these frames. I’m only squinting because whoever wrote this grimoire was a sadist, and not in the good way. This is Latin chickenscratch. Anybody would struggle to read this crap.”

Rio banishes the glasses. She did actually really want to see Agatha wearing them, but maybe she can convince her another day. “It’s the only crap you’ll get your hands on for the duration of your stay here, so best learn to appreciate it.”

“How come you’ll leave these grimoires out in the open but hide my ones?” Agatha whines, pouting. “You know book censorship is a slippery slope to fascism.” She raises an eyebrow. “Are you a fascist, Rio? Makes sense. Death begets fascism… or is it fascism begets death? I can never remember which way around it is.”

After all, it’s rather difficult to nurture life when one’s ingrained instinct is to steal it away. Agatha’s nature as a siphon witch is to absorb power and transform it into her own. Green magic is all about giving, whilst siphon magic is about taking.

“I’m not a fascist, and you’re not a green witch. You can’t access any of the magic described in those tomes,” Rio informs her simply. “That one you’re currently reading doesn’t really have many spells in it anyway. It’s more of a witch’s guide to botanical medicine and pharmacognosy.” Leaning across and dragging the book towards them - nearly crushing Señor Scratchy in the process, making him bleat in disdain - she thumbs through it until she reaches the chapter she’s recalled it contains, smiling wickedly and winking at Agatha. “This here is a particularly riveting section on herbal aphrodisiacs. Her tears spill. Rio can’t stop them as they race down her cheeks, carving red-hot canyons as they descend.

They’ve never talked about the others.

The sons and daughters before Nicky.

Never discussed them, never acknowledged them. Rio has not allowed herself to even think about them. The ones who never made it past the first trimester. The embryos their combined magic was not strong enough to grow and nurture. The powers of Death and the most powerful siphon witch in the universe… were not enough to give life - it was in neither of their inherent natures.

It was only the harnessing and amplification of Rio’s green magic, and a whole lot of fertility and magic suppression spells that nearly killed Agatha, that they ended up with Nicky. Who of course, survived for thirty-nine weeks. Their miracle. Their destruction.

“Agatha,” is all Rio is able to croak out, between her sniffles and weeping.

Her wife is shivering all over, clutching at her arms and digging her nails in so deeply that she’s drawing blood. “I know, I know that they - they never would have made it anyway. And it wasn’t our fault. But years of trying and failing, Rio, nearly a decade, and Nicky nearly made it - he survived up until that final day before his birth,” she rasps. To Rio’s astonishment, she leans towards her, pressing her thigh up against Rio’s own. “And I know you gave me six years with him that he shouldn’t have had in the first place, and believe me, I’m so grateful for that. So unbelievably grateful. But - how it ended. How you took him. I can’t - I can’t accept that.”

She crumples, folding at the waist. She cries. Rio wonders if this is what dying feels like, to humans, because this crushing, catastrophic feeling in her torso cannot be normal or healthy. She cries too, and draws Agatha into her embrace. Her wife curls up next to her on the bed, forehead pressed to Death’s sternum, where her black heart lies beneath.

“I know you had to take him,” Agatha whispers. “I understand - you’re Death. Nicky was dying and you wanted to ease his suffering. But if you loved me then you would have at least let me say goodbye.”

Now that - that is a thought that has plagued Rio for the past two hundred years. Should she have woken Agatha, in the middle of that cold autumn night, when it was time for Nicky’s soul to depart? Would it have made things worse, or would it have helped Agatha with processing her grief? She will never know now, and that kills her.

“I had him kiss you twice on your cheek before I left with him,” Rio tells her quietly. “A kiss from him, and a kiss from me.”

Agatha smacks her closed fist against Rio’s chest, a keening, agonized cry bursting from her lips. “You think that makes me feel better?!” she howls. “Knowing that my son was able to say goodbye to me, but I wasn’t able to say goodbye to him? You think it’s a comfort to know that I can’t and won’t ever remember the last time my son kissed my cheek because you got him to do it while I was asleep, entirely aware that I would wake up to the dead body of my child in my arms?”

All Rio can do is hug Agatha despairingly as she succumbs to her anguish, bawling uncontrollably and smashing her fists against Rio’s body - the only way she seems to be able to express her despair beyond crying. Rio lets her. Better she take her fury out on a body that cannot bruise, than on herself.

Maybe it would have been kinder if Rio had taken Nicky as he was born. Birthing a stillborn baby is agonizing - Rio has claimed enough of them to see the effect on their mothers. She saw the effect it had on Agatha, to suffer through so many early-stage miscarriages; it weighed on her, weighed her down, eating away her hope and aspirations to become a mother, before Nicky came along. Now, she realizes…. loving and caring for a sick and ailing child as they grow up with a shortened lifeline, and then losing them - that might be worse.

She dragged out Agatha’s suffering for six years, because Rio couldn’t deal with her threat of hating her forever. It was a threat she should not have taken seriously, issued by Agatha during a moment of sheer panic at the thought of her son being born dead, after so many failed pregnancies before him.

Rio could not process the idea of Agatha leaving her - and so she gave Agatha what she wanted, in the form of her son taking breath and living on stolen time, only to ultimately destroy her by taking him anyway.

Coiled up in a ball, her face buried in Rio’s sweater, Agatha sounds wrecked as she laments, muffled, “You didn’t warn me. You didn’t give me a chance to make sure his last weeks were comfortable and full of happiness. I would have brought him here so he could have fallen asleep in a warm bed with a full belly, not tired and hungry and curled up on the ground on a ratty blanket in a cold forest.” She yanks at Rio’s sweater, coming close to ripping it. “You could have joined us. You could have cooked for him, read him stories at night to help him sleep, and picked flowers with him every day.”

It’s a wonderful fantasy, Rio has to admit. It sounds like it would have been amazing. The three of them would have been able to be a proper family. But it never would have happened, in reality. “Don’t lie. Not - not about that. Not about him,” she counters, hand cradling Agatha’s skull but gripping the back of her neck tightly. “You wouldn’t have let me anywhere near him. And if you’d known his death was approaching then you would have done anything to prevent it or stave it off - sought out healers, forced potions down his throat, searched for dark magic. You would have been an anxious mess and Nicky would have been terrified seeing you like that.” She shakes her head, and repeats what she has told herself since that night to justify her choices, to assure herself she was doing the right thing: “Nicky deserved to go abruptly and peacefully, without anticipation, pain, or fear.”

“And you don’t think what I just described would have been peaceful for him?” Agatha says accusingly.

“Those tiny comforts you just described would have been to make you feel better, not him,” Rio insists. “And they wouldn’t have worked. So I did what I thought was best for him. Because I love you and I know you would have wanted me to think of his wellbeing first, so long as he lived.”

She intends for her statements to calm Agatha, and convince her that she was trying to make Nicky’s passing as quick and painless as possible for him - but Agatha must hear something different. Because her wife shoves her aggressively and claws her way out of Rio’s embrace, staggering off the bed.

Rio follows her, stepping in front of her wife when she makes for the door. No, they are mid-conversation. She will not let Agatha abscond now.

Agatha snarls at her like a rabid animal. “And what about after? What about when he stopped living, Rio?” she screams. “You think your actions demonstrated love then?”

She grabs Rio by her sweater and slams her up against the closed door. Considering her lack of energy earlier, Rio is dazed, and just lets Agatha push her around however she wants.

Tangling her hand in Rio’s hair, her wife pins her head down, roaring, “I was alone. I woke up to Nicky dead next to me, alone. I buried him, alone. I mourned and grieved him, alone! You weren’t there! I needed you, and you left me, you fucking coward!” She gulps in frantic breaths, her face nearly turning blue from lack of oxygen. It’s actually pretty impressive she’s managing to shout for so long after nearly drowning earlier in the day. “You took him and you left and when you eventually came back, you had the audacity to be upset that I was angry!”

Recalling the fight that Agatha is talking about, Rio thinks her indignation at Agatha was warranted. She escapes from the spirit witch’s grasp, taking hold of her wife’s fragile wrists with one hand so she can loom over her, spitting, “You were angry at me for doing my job.”

Agatha backs off a single step, but does not back down. She raises her chin and straightens her spine so that Rio no longer has a height advantage. “No, I was angry at you because you didn’t stay after!” she yells.

Okay, that is… a valid criticism. As much as she despises to admit it, she did leave Agatha alone that night, and not return until much later. “I knew you would despise me for taking him and tell me to leave and never come back. I couldn’t face that,” Rio reveals, deflating. “I couldn’t fathom the idea of being forced to let you go.” In truth, she was petrified by the idea of losing Agatha after the death of their son. If she lost Agatha, then she would have nothing.

Her wife rips her wrists free from Rio’s grip just to throw her hands in the air in disbelief. “So you decided it would be better to leave? Leave your grieving wife by herself, while you gallivanted off to reap more souls?”

Gallivanting? Is that what Agatha thinks she did? No, she threw herself into the deepest, darkest pit in the Realm of the Dead and wallowed. Why does Agatha always focus on her own grief and suffering?

Does she not understand that Rio was struggling to mourn as well? That she was just as lost and hurt and in pain as her wife? That she was frightened of losing Agatha, on top of losing Nicky? That she perhaps she was confused because she wasn’t built to experience loss in that manner, wasn’t meant to feel these things?

“I was giving you space,” Rio says, and even she can hear how weak a defense it is. “I thought that when I came back you would have calmed down and processed enough to realize that I didn’t have a choice, that I never wanted to take him or hurt you.” She twists her hands together, confessing in a small voice, “I was scared, Agatha, okay? You’re right, I was a coward. I thought that by leaving, in time you would be willing to take me back.”

The spirit witch gapes at her. “In what world does that make any sense?!” she splutters.

It’s not meant to make any sense. Rio was grieving. “I’d just reaped my own son’s soul, Agatha, I wasn’t exactly thinking clearly at the time!” she argues.

Grief, she has learned, can simultaneously be one of the most understandable and senseless states of existence in the universe. It can be both rational and irrational. And therefore lead a person to do senseless and irrational things.

She had to ferry her own son’s soul to the afterlife - and Rio can acknowledge now that it was incredibly traumatizing for her, a deity who was never meant to experience trauma at all. And then she lost her wife after, because she was scared of losing her - and so left before she could feel the sting of Agatha’s rejection.

She wasn’t sure exactly how much time passed before she finally returned to her wife’s side, so engulfed in her own grief that it caused existence to blur together; it could have been weeks, months, half a year. But when she did crawl back, cautious and daunted and afraid, she found her fears validated; Agatha cast her out and condemned her to a lonely existence - after teaching her about what love and belonging and family are in the first place.

WHY IS MY GRIEF NOT AS VALID AS YOURS? WHAT ABOUT HOW I FELT? WHAT ABOUT HOW YOU TREATED ME? DON’T I MATTER? she wants to scream.

But she’ll have her time to express those feelings. Right now, Agatha needs this emotional release in order for her to begin the process of healing. Rio will have her chance in the future to vent her frustrations later.

“And you thought that I was thinking clearly?” Agatha says in disbelief.

Rio bristles. Oh, Agatha wants to go there? Then she will go there. “Didn’t take you long to return to your murderous coven-slaying ways. You placed the last stone on Nicky’s grave and not half an hour later, you were back to attacking witches,” she hisses.

Not just luring witches in using her con of the Road for the very first time - but utilizing and defiling Nicky’s song to do so. Shitting on the memory of their son, to kill.

She’s witness to the moment that Agatha sees red. “BECAUSE I WAS HOPING THAT IT WOULD BRING YOU HOME!” her wife shrieks.

Chapter End Notes

ducks and hides

Chapter 8

Chapter Notes

........ sorry

cw: discussion/mention of child loss, child death; mental breakdown; discussion of child abuse and neglect; unhealthy coping mechanisms in regards to grief

I still have custody :) I have simply transferred it over to a new account so it is easier for the fandom to find my other fics. thank you to everybody who was so supportive of me posting anonymously, I would not have had the courage to do this without you!!

Rio immediately wilts, shocked. She takes a stumbling step back. “What?” she breathes.

Agatha started murdering covens, after their son’s death… to try and summon Rio to her?

Agatha has turned as white as a sheet, all of her fury drained out of her, leaving her looking shaken and weary. She looks both mortified and disturbed by her own confession, as if she has never lent a thought to it before, and did not expect it to come out of her mouth. Uncontrollable tears are flowing down her face once again.

“Is that true?” Rio demands. “Agatha, are you telling the truth?”

She doesn’t know if she believes her. If she can believe her. Did Agatha start killing again so soon after Nicky’s death because she was desperately trying to call Rio to her, or was it simply a way for her to bury and avoid processing her grief?

She knows from having watched Agatha siphon witches that she experiences an almost euphoric high whenever she absorbs power, since her magical core can only store, not generate.

Agatha has killed witches ever since she decimated her original coven; throughout Nicky’s childhood, Agatha wiped out covens to covet power, clearly in an attempt to gather enough to keep their son safe. But she essentially became a power addict, and when Agatha drained a coven on the same day as burying Nicky, Rio lamented, thinking that it was just her junkie wife hunting a fresh fix to escape her sorrow.

“It doesn’t matter,” Agatha chokes out. “It never mattered, not to you.”

“Agatha, you’re telling me that you committed mass murder after burying our son because you were trying to summon me,” she says, shocked. “Of course it matters.”
