“No, it doesn’t!” Agatha argues, crying. “Because you didn’t come! Those witches - they deserved what they got that day. That blonde bitch disturbed me at Nicky’s gravesite and when she asked me to show her the Road, the only thought in my mind was that I could kill her and the rest of her despicable coven, and it might just be enough to tip the balance and summon you.”

It did tip the balance. It did summon Rio. She felt the pull from the souls of the witches Agatha slaughtered that day, but ignored them and sent a reaper in her place, petrified that if she turned up, Agatha would attack her.

Oh, how she regrets her decision now.

“I killed so many, trying to reach out to you, and you ignored me. You left me alone because you were stupid enough to think I would want space after having to dig a fucking grave for our son by myself, after you got to run away with his soul and keep him all to yourself.” She shakes her head, trembling from head to toe. “Do you know how long you ignored me? Are you even aware of the passage of time? Did you mean to stay away that long?”

“How long?” Rio asks, swamped with dread, already knowing that the answer will destroy her. That it will make her want to throw herself into a black hole.

“SIX MONTHS!” Agatha screams. “SIX FUCKING MONTHS AND NINE DEAD COVENS BEFORE YOU SHOWED YOUR FACE AGAIN! OUR SON DIED AND YOU TOOK HIS SOUL AND YOU LEFT ME TO BURY HIM AND GRIEVE ALONE FOR SIX FUCKING MONTHS!”

Six months. For Rio? That’s nothing. A blink of the eye, for a creature who has existed for millennia. Barely a rounding error. For Agatha, though? A woman who, from her perspective, just had her child’s life cruelly snatched from her, and was left by herself to cope afterward?

Six months must have seemed like decades.

No wonder Agatha was so angry. No wonder she cut Rio off from their soul bond to punish her. She must have wanted Rio to experience the same pain that she unintentionally put her bereaved wife through.

“I - I didn't know,” Rio stutters, stunned. She truly didn’t. Time is tricky for her, as a cosmic being, and does not flow in a linear pattern. Still, it was her fault. She can’t defend herself against abandoning her wife for half a year. And no apology will ever be enough, but she can try. “Agatha, I’m - forgive me, please,” she begs, falling to her knees in front of her wife. “I’m so sorry -”

“What good is ‘sorry’!?” her wife shouts. “You were so scared of me leaving you BUT YOU LEFT ME FIRST! You abandoned me and gave up on me - just like everybody else did!”

Everybody else…. she has to be talking about her original coven. About her mother. Whom Rio has apparently started starring in Agatha’s nightmares alongside.

She feels like she’s just been punched in the stomach, which is a feat in itself, considering that an actual punch wouldn’t cause her pain.

“Don’t you dare compare me to those monsters who abused and neglected you,” Rio says, a snarl on her lips. “They treated you like you were nothing more than dirt under their shoes since you were born.”

“And why shouldn’t I?” her wife thunders. “At least they didn’t pretend to love me! At least their hatred was constant - expected and predictable. You - you promised me forever. You made me believe I was worthy of love and that I didn’t deserve to be beaten and treated like a servant throughout my childhood. You stuck with me through every miscarriage I had and assured me after every loss that I wasn’t broken, that I wasn’t a failure - that you weren’t going anywhere. You swore to always return home to me, that nothing would ever stop you and you would fight the entire universe if you had to. And then Nicky died, and you abandoned me.”

“I didn’t abandon you - I came back!” Rio argues weakly.

“After six months!? How could I trust that?” Agatha cries out. “How could I trust you to stay, when you didn’t even trust me not to send you away!?” She buries her face in her hands with a distraught wail. “After that, I HAD to force you to leave - before you eventually figured out that I was too damaged by the loss of our son and decided to do it again!”

Rio stares up at her in utter horror. It makes too much sense, and it breaks her heart. Agatha did what she has always done when faced with the prospect of being hurt. She lashed out. She attacked, hurling cruel words and accusations of not loving her enough, not loving Nicky enough, in Rio’s face. And maybe part of her actually believed them. But most likely she spent those six months terrified, and wondering if Rio staying away was a punishment, or rejection.

Rio hurt her deeply, and Agatha was so afraid of her leaving again that she drove her back out, so that Rio left her in a manner that she could control. And Rio was so wrapped up in her own fear and grief that she missed it.

“I didn’t want to leave you, Agatha,” Rio whispers. “I never wanted to. I promised you forever and I meant it.” She shakes her head, at a loss. “If we’d talked about this before you flew off the handle -” She abruptly cuts herself off, wincing at her own choice of words.

“Yeah, well, you’re centuries too late to want to talk about this.” Agatha glares at her with tears in her eyes. “And it’s certainly too late for Nicky.”

Before Rio can stop her, she’s storming past, wrenching the bedroom door open, and making her getaway.

“Agatha? Agatha, don’t run!” Rio calls after her, lurching back to her feet. She hears doors open and slam closed in the near distance. “You always do this!” she yells.

Agatha can no longer hear her, and even if she can, she is far too emotional to listen. She is fleeing not just from Rio, but from her own feelings, too overwhelmed to deal with anything. All of her emotions are hitting her a hundred times harder because she is being forced to confront them all head-on after centuries of squashing them down, going mad with grief.

Everything she buried is now rising to the surface and bursting out of the cracks formed in her exterior due to her most recent trauma, and Agatha has no idea how to deal with any of it. Her main coping mechanism, of taking her fury out on unsuspecting covens and stealing their power, is entirely out of reach.

Rio realizes, now, that Agatha might actually be having some form of nervous breakdown - one that she has delayed for over two hundred years. One that can no longer be suppressed. She has just survived three years of being trapped in her own mind and being psychologically tortured. She now has no magic, and no real means to defend herself whilst weak and sick. And Agatha is going the only thing she can, in response to losing all control: running.

Agatha can flee, but she won’t be able to get far. She’s tired, and physically fragile, and prone to seizures. Rio does the only thing that she logically can do, in this situation.

She gives chase.

Rio knows she has to tread carefully, as she treks through the house slowly, in search of her wife. Agatha may be one of the apex predators of the witch world, but she is fully aware that in terms of strength and power, she is nothing more than a tiny, weak little injured animal right now in comparison to Death.

Like all injured animals being hunted, she is prone to making drastic and dangerous decisions. Feral cats have a tendency to flee at the first sign of a threat, but then get defensive and aggressive when cornered, in order to protect themselves. Agatha, like a cat, is not afraid to whip her teeth and claws out if she needs to fight.

Rio doesn’t want that, though. Fighting is detrimental to Agatha’s healing journey. Not that they’ve really made much progress since she dragged her kicking and screaming to the cottage… but those first few steps are always the hardest ones, right?

She could very easily use the monitoring spell she’s attached to Agatha’s soul and lifeline to track her down, but that would, in Rio’s mind, be cheating. The green witch has always enjoyed a good old-fashioned pursuit, when it comes to her wife. She spent several months stalking Agatha from the shadows and trailing her from kill to kill, before they met face-to-face.

Then, after their separation, when Agatha blocked their bond, Rio was forced to resort to following her siphon witch’s breadcrumb trail of magically drained bodies to ferret her out. As aggravating as it was to have Agatha escape her at every twist and turn, it was also rather thrilling to be constantly outwitted; Rio needed to remain on her toes at all times, and she loved it.

There are only so many places Agatha can hole herself away in around the cottage, in this warped version of hide-and-seek. They’ve played this game before, within these walls, although usually, they were both naked, and it was a form of predator-prey roleplay.

This time, however - and to her own astonishment - sex is the last thing on Rio’s mind. All she wants is to make sure that Agatha is okay, after that very emotionally overwhelming argument. Even if Agatha is being an utter pain in her ass right now.

She first manages to discern that Agatha has not been stupid enough to risk running off outside, since the front door is securely locked. At least she’s not freezing her supple buttcheeks off outside in the middle of the mountainous New England forest. She must still be inside, which narrows down the number of hiding spaces. She knows that Agatha isn’t in their bedroom, so that leaves the kitchen and connected living room, the larder, the still room, the bathroom and… Nicky’s bedroom.

“Agathaaa,” she calls out, in a sing-song voice, creeping around the cottage, which has become dark and gloomy with the setting sun. “Come out, come out, wherever you are.”

She pokes her head into the larder, which is empty, and then slinks into the still room, crouching to search beneath the tables and inside cubby holes.

“Agatha, come on,” she calls, growing desperate. “Running and squirreling yourself away is not a productive way of processing your emotions. We need to talk about this.” She pauses, waiting for a response, and hears nothing. “We both know how this is gonna end, sweetheart. Hiding is futile. I’ll find you eventually.”

The kitchen and living room also show no signs of life, and the bathroom is vacant too. Which only leaves one room left - a room that Rio has never had the courage to enter for the past two hundred and fifty years.

Her heart leaps into her throat as she steels herself and approaches it, down the corridor. She immediately halts mid-stride when she sees Señor Scratchy hunched over and sitting like a tiny white and tan loaf, pressed up against the door. He twitches his nose at her, glancing between her and the door and letting out a mournful squeak. Rio sighs, and gently pushes him aside with her foot, ignoring his squeal of exasperation.

The green witch traces trembling fingers over the name carved into the ash wood; NICHOLAS, in delicate capital letters, has been chiseled out using Rio’s scythe blade. They chose his name on the day Rio sensed his gender, on the summer solstice. Greek in origin, meaning ‘victory of the people’. Because Nicholas’s conception and survival into the third trimester was a sweet triumph for the two of them, after years of struggle and hardship in the form of miscarriages.

To commemorate that day, Agatha mixed blackthorn and rowan charcoal powder into melted pine resin, and poured it into the scratches, so that their son’s name will forever be immortalized in amber. If she squints, she can still see her and Agatha’s fingerprints pressed into the resin.

One day, they might have melted the resin a little bit so that Nicky could have added his own fingerprints to join his parents’.

Alas, that day never came.

As a cosmic entity with eidetic memory, Rio can perfectly recall the last time she and Agatha were in this room together. Rio put the finishing touches on Nicky’s mobile while Agatha sat on the rocking chair, her belly so huge she could hardly walk; she hummed and embroidered their son’s name into his tiny handmade clothes.

Agatha entered early labor in the early evening, just as the sun was sinking below the horizon, and it was during that process that Rio sensed Nicky’s heart stop beating within her.

Agatha saw her fall to her knees in abject horror, and she was forced to tell her wife, stricken, that their son was no longer alive. And Agatha, distraught and overcome with despair, ran. In complete and utter denial, screaming at Rio to stay away, she fled the cottage into the night, to labour alone in the depths of the forest. Rio could do nothing but follow after her, helpless and hopeless, feeling their unborn dead son’s soul drawing her in, ready to pass on.

When Death confronted Agatha by that lakeside the next day, her wife shrieking and collapsing against a tree with every contraction, Rio made a choice. She chose love over duty, and bent the rules - a decision that would change everything. Nicky lived, but at a cost. Agatha swindled him away and from then on, Rio was only able to catch fleeting glimpses of their son from the night’s shadows and her wife’s dreams.

The cottage was abandoned.

Nicky never got the chance to even enter his own bedroom, let alone sleep inside of it. It has never had an occupant. And if Rio has never entered it, after their son’s death, then Agatha definitely hasn’t.

Which means that if Agatha is indeed inside… this is the first time she has gone in since Nicky was born. And since Nicky left them.

It’s with immense apprehension - and no small amount of dread - that Rio cracks the door open. There’s no explosion of long-settled dust thanks to the cleansing spell Rio used on the entire cottage when they first arrived here, but it still smells slightly musty. There’s no light, as the curtains are drawn - as they have been for the past two centuries - but Rio has good enough night vision for her gaze to sweep over the room.

The bedroom has been decorated like a forest beneath the night sky, with trees lining the walls and constellations painted on the ceiling. There is a rowan crib in the corner, aged but still intact, with protection ruins carved into the wood; a crocheted toy rabbit is resting inside, with a handmade mobile of pine cones, seashells, feathers, and horse chestnuts hanging above. There’s a rocking chair tucked away to the side. Every part of Rio hurts, examining the effort that she and Agatha lovingly put into creating a nursery that their son never used.

Agatha is curled up on the tiny toddler bed in the opposite corner, cuddling a hand-stitched baby grow to her chest; it’s made of small squares of Nicky’s parents’ various clothes and cloaks.

She thinks of the animals she’s witnessed in the wild, going absolutely insane over their lost babies. Orcas, carrying their dead young on their backs for days on end. Cattle and deer, wandering listlessly for days on end after their calves and fawns pass, bleating and calling to their ghosts. Cats, grooming and trying to nurse their dead kittens, clinging onto scraps of their fur and refusing to let go.

Agatha, wearing a clipping of their son’s hair in a locket over her heart for centuries, lost in a hurricane of turmoil and grief. Now she has this new tiny piece of Nicky to carry around with her, in the form of his baby grow. If anybody tries to take it from her - well, Rio reckons they wouldn't survive very long.

She looks more like a lumpy ball, than a person, from where she’s buried under the blankets. Only the top half of her face is visible, and her brunette hair has fanned out behind her on the threadbare pillow. Rio can partially see that her hand is clenched tightly around her locket containing Nicky’s hair, as if she’s afraid it will disappear at any moment.

She barely twitches as Rio skulks inside, treading lightly so as to avoid alerting her. The green witch is about to pounce on her, when she comes to an abrupt stop, standing directly over the bed and peering down at her wife.

She’s asleep. Or maybe passed out.

And judging by the dried tear tracks on her face, Agatha either cried herself to sleep… or cried so hard that her mind shut down.

Rio quickly checks Agatha’s pulse and breathing. The monitoring spell did not alert her to anything concerning, but she likes to reassure herself. Her wife’s breathing is shallow, but steady, and her heartbeat is thready, but stable. She has not suffered from another seizure whilst alone, thank the gods, but her body is severely fatigued, so she is not out of the woods yet.

The amount of emotional distress Agatha has experienced over the past hour could provoke a seizure. She needs another dose of the elixir and perhaps some more medication, and then Rio will be certain she will make it through the night without another neurological event.

Spotting the vice-like grip Agatha has on Nicky’s baby grow, Rio’s heart pangs. Oh no. This is going to set a very dangerous precedent for future arguments between them. Now Agatha has mustered up the bravery to enter their son’s bedroom, she will undoubtedly want to stay in here constantly. She will cling to this echo of Nicky in physical form and refuse to let it go. And she will suffocate herself in her bereavement and obstinance.

Rio will have to draw a line. And she knows that doing so will break Agatha’s heart, and could drive her away forever. This could be the final nail in the coffin of their relationship, if Agatha does not find a way to understand her actions.

“Lo siento, mi corazón,” she murmurs, caressing the spirit witch’s pale cheek. “I wish I could turn back time and change things for the better. But that has never been within my power, mi vida. You deserved so much more than the hand you were dealt. Lo siento, te amo, lo siento mucho.”

Wiggling her arms beneath Agatha’s prone fragile frame, Rio bundles her wife in the crumpled blankets and cradles her gently to her chest as she carries her out of the bedroom. It still shocks her how light Agatha feels, and how much weight and muscle mass she lost whilst trapped under Wanda’s spell.

A tendril of green magic extends out of her spine and snakes over the floor and up to the handle, pulling the door closed - and locking it. Rio’s eyes slip shut and she squeezes them closed, trying to regulate her breathing, which has become difficult and heavy, as her magic imbues into the lock and secures it.

Now the door will only open to somebody with the use of magic.

Which Agatha does not have.

She can hope that Agatha will forgive her, one day. But Death knows how useless and ineffectual hope can be.

She glances down through tear-filled eyes when she feels tiny delicate paws batting at her bare foot. Señor Scratchy blinks up at her with woeful black eyes, his whiskers quivering. Agatha’s stupid rabbit is showing her more empathy than she could ever deserve, and Rio would scoop him up and cuddle him if her arms were not occupied. Scratchy returns to his post guarding Nicky’s bedroom door as the green witch transports her wife down the corridor and back towards the master bedroom.

Agatha, never one to make things easy for her, begins to stir and squirm in her arms, fighting her grasp. But she’s as weak as a kitten, and her frantic, sloppy pawing is frankly pitiful. “What’re you doing?” she demands in an exhausted, slurred voice. “Don’ touch me. Pu’me down.”

Rio sighs, and stops, adjusting her grip on her uncooperative wriggling cargo. “I’ll put you down if you can tell me that you’ll be able to walk by yourself to our bedroom without tripping and falling flat on your face,” she says gently. Agatha glares at her half-heartedly, too tired to manage anything truly threatening, so Rio tries to lighten the mood. “Don’t want that pretty nose of yours getting broken, do we, amor? Be a shame for a face as beautiful as yours to end up covered in bruises by making acquaintance with the wooden floor.”

She starts towards the master bedroom once again, but Agatha’s anxiety amplifies with every step she takes. Rio has to hang on tight to her when her wife tries to throw herself onto the floor, shaking her head vehemently. “No, turn around. I want to go back to Nicky’s bedroom,” Agatha stutters. “I want to sleep in there. I don’t want to share a bed with you anymore.”

This is exactly what Rio was afraid would happen. She dips her head with a troubled exhalation, until her forehead brushes against Agatha’s. “You can’t. I’ve locked the door and sealed it with magic,” she says quietly. As she predicted, Agatha looks outraged. But also completely devastated. “It’s not healthy for you to be going in there and sleeping in his bed, Agatha. In your current mental state, all you’ll do is dwell on the past and succumb to your depression.”

“No. Please. Please, don’t - I want to go back in there,” Agatha begs, trying to desperately reach out over Rio’s shoulder for Nicky’s bedroom door. Her lack of strength, however, means her arm falters after a few seconds and dangles limply down the green witch’s back. “I want to be with him!” Agatha sobs.

Rio’s black heart shatters into a thousand shards of razor-sharp obsidian in her chest cavity, which slice through her with such agony that she nearly topples to her knees. She hugs Agatha as she cradles her, tears springing to her eyes.

“He’s not in there, baby, you know he’s not. He’s gone, Agatha. He’s been gone for two hundred and seventy years,” she chokes out, her voice hoarse with regret. “I’m sorry, but all that bedroom is, is a remnant. He never even slept there. There is no part of him in there. It’s just an empty tomb. A macabre memorial to the idea of us raising him here.” The harrowed, strangled noise that rips from Agatha’s throat causes the slivers of Rio’s fractured heart to bury in deeper. “I know you’ll hate me for making this decision for you, mi vida, but please, just know that I’m doing it for your own good, in your best interests.”

She feels vindicated, in some ways, because she knows now that she made the correct decision in locking Agatha out. But at the same time, she feels like some cruel, vicious monster, banning Agatha from a room that helps her feel more connected to her dead child, even if that connection is currently more damaging than healing.

She hikes Agatha further up into her arms, ready to carry her into their bedroom - with her wife resisting her the whole way, if necessary - but then Agatha curls her hand into the neck of Rio’s sweater, yanks her head down, surges upwards… and kisses her.

Rio is so honestly shocked for a moment that she freezes. What the hell is happening? But then Agatha emits a soft, frantic little mewl and presses her lips even more bruisingly to Rio’s. Her eyes are squeezed closed with tears falling down her now flushed cheeks and her brow furrowed.

Her wife’s shaking hand rises from her throat to her hair, taking a fierce hold of it. And Rio feels that commanding tug on her scalp, and Agatha taking control, and the ground vanishes from beneath her feet, because yes, yes, kiss me harder, bite my lip, KISS ME, AGATHA.

She sinks into the kiss, eyes slipping closed, responding eagerly with a muffled groan. She traces her tongue over Agatha’s lips until they give way and she can lick into her mouth, and Rio drinks her in as if she’s starving; the spirit witch tastes of apples and cranberries and salty tears and lightning. It’s addicting, and overwhelming, and Rio finds her knees wobbling. She stumbles back until her spine connects with the nearest wall, giving her the traction to kiss Agatha deeper.

She can feel Agatha’s soul crackling beneath her skin, singing in delight at her touch; the sensation of her wife finally, finally reaching out to her, her soul brushing up against Rio’s, sends arousal flooding through her veins. It’s that intense heat blossoming all throughout her body that keeps her connected with it, when she feels like she’s flying, riding the high.

But then as Rio dials back in a little bit, becoming all too aware of how Agatha’s other hand has slipped behind her back and is clawing at her ferociously, and she remembers. She feels the wetness on Agatha’s face from her crying, feelings the way her torso is hitching as if she is suppressing sobs. Agatha’s soul is thrilled, yes, but there is also an undercurrent of bitter heartbreak and remorse.

The green witch breaks the kiss, a frigid, harsh realization dawning on her, and watches in dismay as Agatha gasps for oxygen for a few seconds before trying to dive back in. Rio raises her chin and pulls her head away, so that her wife cannot connect their lips again. The spirit witch whimpers, yanking cruelly at Rio’s hair to try and drag her head back down. But Rio does not feel pain, and will not let her kiss her again.

Because this is not real.

“Agatha,” she whispers. “Stop. You don’t want this.”

Agatha tries to insist, “I do,” but her voice trembles, and more tears well in her blue eyes.

“No, you don’t,” Rio replies gently. “I know what your lips and mouth feel like when you want me. I’ve studied your body language and learned it by heart. I’m fluent in you and all of your idiosyncrasies. You don’t really want to kiss me - you’re trying to get me to change my mind.” Agatha shakes her head wildly, flinching and wrenching her hands free from Rio’s body, to hug them to her chest. “I’m sorry, but I won’t, my love.”

Her wife stares at her, her pupils so diluted that her eyes look like onyx pools rather than their usual glacial cerulean color. Rio thinks, for a second, that maybe Agatha will try and deny it once again. But then her wife’s saddened gaze trawls away from the green witch towards the locked door of their dead son’s bedroom.

“Please, please, just - just unlock the door,” Agatha says, sniffling. “I won’t go back in there tonight, but I want - I want the option, I want to be able to go in if I want to.”

Rio smiles at her, knowing that if she does unlock Nicky’s bedroom door, Agatha will be back in there and despondently lying on the little kid’s cot before dawn. “I’m not unlocking the door. I want you to heal and get better, and all that bedroom will do is encourage you to immerse yourself in your grief. We need to move forward, Agatha. Together.”

She swivels on her heel, marching much more determinedly towards their bedroom now - and away from the nursery. Agatha breaks out into uncontrollable weeping once again, arms stretched out towards the room.

“It’s what Nicky would want,” Rio tells her with a muffled sob, also reminding herself.

When they step inside the master bedroom, and Rio kicks the door closed behind them - blocking off the corridor - Agatha falls entirely weightless in her arms. She stops crying suddenly, and instead goes completely silent. Rio tenderly lowers her down on the bed.

Agatha lies limply on the mattress, eyes half-lidded, looking defeated. With a wave of her hand, Rio uses magic to change the spirit witch into her pajamas, not wanting to struggle with manually undressing and re-dressing her when Agatha is unresponsive.

She tucks Agatha onto her side into her usual sleeping position and then drapes the quilt over her, before tucking Nicky’s baby grow into her arms. That appears to help bring her wife back to the present, because she coils up into a ball and clutches at the tiny patchwork onesie like it’ll vanish into thin air if she dares let go of it. Combing Agatha’s mane of hair away from her face, Rio ducks down to press a kiss to her forehead.

Kneeling down next to the bed, so they are at eye level, Rio leans her arms on the mattress, her chin resting on them. She takes a few minutes to simply sit there and observe her wife, who continues to lie entirely still, wrapped in the comforter, barely conscious but still shivering every so often because of the shock. It’s not the cold, because the fire in the opposite grate is burning strong, casting warmth throughout the room.

She hesitantly extends her arm to very lightly trail her fingertips down the slope of Agatha’s nose, and then strokes her thumb over her cheek. Agatha’s somber eyes peer back at her, dull with resignation and fatigue.

“If you truly don’t want to share the bed, I’ll sit in the corner instead,” the green witch murmurs, “But I’m not leaving you alone. Not tonight.”

Agatha slowly licks her dry lips, inhaling a convulsing breath. “I don’t want you near me,” she wheezes. “I hate you.”

Rio nods. “I love you too,” she says calmly.

“No, I don’t love you. Don’t put words in my mouth,” Agatha rasps. She closes her eyes once again, ducking her chin down to half bury her face beneath the comforter. “I will never forgive you. I hate you. I hate you,” she mutters repeatedly. As if she’s trying to convince herself of the fact, first and foremost.

Rio sighs, hanging her head. She doesn’t believe her, when she says that she hates her, but it is very, very difficult to maintain that position when Agatha is spitting it in her face so frequently. Agatha does love her. Rio knows that she does. She is just in the middle of a mental breakdown and is having an incredibly difficult day.

“Okay, Agatha. You can think whatever you want,” she mumbles. “But I’m staying. I’m here for you and I’m not leaving. Not again. Never again.”

She goes through her routine of closing the blinds and switching off the lights, and then lowers herself to the floor, back up against the side of the bed, to begin her vigil. Her wife can tell her that she hates her all she wants, but she will never leave her when she needs her.

Agatha falls asleep rapidly after that.

Rio, banished from their marital bed, sits and stares blankly at the wall, legs stretched out in front of her. She listens through the monitoring spell to Agatha’s steady heartbeat; she listens to the melodic hum of her wife’s soul, remembering how wonderful it felt for Agatha to have reached out and offered her contact with it for the first time in centuries - and then how horrifying it felt, as Rio discerned that her wife, in her grief and desperation, was trying to manipulate her by kissing her.

As the hours start to whittle away, and a chill begins to seep into the room as the moon rises high above the forest and the cottage, Rio draws her knees up close so she can embrace them.

And silently, with a blank face, she weeps. 

Nicholas’ tiny cold hand is dwarfed by her own as she clasps it tightly, her stomach clenched. His skin is freezing, blood no longer pumping within his veins. The green-flamed torch in her spare hand flickers, casting an eerie light over the child's pale face. Rio forces a tremulous smile as she leads them through the forest, away from where Agatha sleeps, curled protectively around a still, unbreathing physical copy of the little boy walking alongside Lady Death toward the afterlife.

A little boy who so happens to be her beloved son.

Outwardly, she looks calm. Serene. Almost impassive.

Internally, she is clawing apart her insides, screeching like a banshee. She is falling apart.

But she refuses to scare Nicky. His passing should be peaceful. She will not allow herself to traumatize him, no matter how traumatizing this is for her.

“I could hear you calling to me,” Nicky tells her, the excitement in his adorable voice making Rio feel sick with horror. He’s been yapping her ears off for the last ten minutes, telling her all about his and Agatha’s life together. “Your voice, in the wind rustling the tree leaves, in the water rushing over the rocks in the streams that Mama and I fish in.” He leans to press the side of his head against her arm, like a kitten snuggling up to its mother. “I knew I would get to meet you one day, Mami. I knew that I would see you for real, and not just in my dreams. I waited and hoped and prayed to the Triple Goddess like Mama does every night, and my wish came true.”

“That’s wonderful, mijo,” Rio tells him with a false smile, despising how she is shaking all over.

Nicky suddenly stops mid-stride, tugging at her hand. “Wait. What about Mama? We should go and wake her! She’ll want to see you too!”

“Oh, but she can’t come on this adventure with us, Nico. That’s why I got you to say goodbye to her, from both of us.” A tear slips from her eye, that she desperately hopes Nicky doesn’t see. “And it’s the middle of the night. You know what your mama is like… she turns into a big angry bear if you wake her too early.”

Nicky laughs, swinging their joined hands back and forth as he starts forward again. “Yes, she goes ‘grrrrr!’ in your face and pretends to bite your arms off. She’s so funny.” He goes quiet for a minute. “Mami, when will I go back to Mama? She’ll panic and be sad if I’m not there with her in the morning. Why can’t she come with us?”

Her heart shatters. “It’s not time for her adventure yet, mijo. This is your journey, not hers.” She runs a quivering hand through his mop of hair. “It’ll probably be a little while before you see her again.”

Nicky frowns. “But… then she’ll be alone.” His lip wobbles. “I don’t want Mama to be alone. Who’ll pick flowers for her? Who’ll cuddle with her at night? Who will she sing our song with?”

“You will, Nico,” Rio says, tears in her eyes. “You’ll always be with her, so long as you’re thinking about her. And trust me, I know she will always be thinking about you. So long as your mama remembers picking flowers and cuddling and singing with you, you’ll always be in her heart.”

Nicky falls quiet once again. His voice is tentative and shy as he asks, “Mami… am I dead?”

Rio swallows heavily. “Yes, mijo,” she replies hoarsely.

“Oh,” is all he says in response. He doesn't sound sad, or upset. Dawning understanding has overtaken his brown eyes. Rio sees it. Nicky understands now. He understands that he won’t be seeing his mama again until she dies too. “Can I see you now because you’re dead too? Is… is that why I heard you calling for me today in the tavern?”

“It’s complicated,” she whispers.

“Will you see Mama again before I do? Will… will you tell Mama that I love her? That I actually didn’t mind killing all the witches, and that I know she is good, no matter what all the others think?” His hand squeezes Rio’s. “Will you tell her I didn’t want to leave her alone and that I miss her?”

“Yes,” Rio whispers. “I’ll tell her.”

Nicky nods, looking far too wise for a six-year-old boy. “Good. And I don’t want her to feel bad for me getting sick. It wasn’t her fault. I shouldn’t have gone swimming in the lake two weeks ago when she was trying to steal that bread for me.” He smiles happily. “I don’t feel sick anymore.”

They come to the end of the forest trail. The portal that Rio cut with her scythe knife, leading to the front gates of the Realm of the Dead, lies beyond. Her beloved familiar is waiting, in the form of a sweet and gentle black and tan Coonhound. Victoria will accompany him on his journey, keeping him safe and protected.

Rio could walk him further - all the way up to the Gates, if she wanted. But then she would never be able to let Nicky go. She may be the ruler of the Realm, but she cannot interfere with the crossing-over process - not even for her own son. Nicky must go on a journey alone to ascend, be cleansed, and then judged on his Earthly actions. He will be expedited through the system since he is so young.

She has no doubt that Nicky will be judged pure of heart; she has been careful not to taint his soul with her manipulation of the sacred balance to extend his lifeline. Only then will he enter her Realm, and become Rio’s subject. He will, of course, be rapidly crowned Prince, but there’s no telling how long the crossing over will take. It could take days - it could take decades.

“Victoria will take care of you,” Rio informs him, “And I will see you very soon, I promise.” She kneels in front of him, caressing his pale cheeks and tapping his cute button nose as she tries not to sob. “You have to be brave now, Nico. But I know you won’t find that hard. You have the heart of a lion, just like your mama does.”

“I’m not scared,” Nicky says simply. His lips twitch up into a little smile. “I’ll teach Victoria lots of new tricks while she’s with me.”

She huffs a laugh. “Try not to create too much mischief.”

“You should go back to Mama, when I’m gone,” he says, his voice hushed. “I think she’ll need you.”

Rio’s throat closes up. She doesn’t know what to say. Nothing terrifies her more than how Agatha is going to react when she wakes up tomorrow to find that Rio came in the dead of night to help Nicky’s soul move on without forewarning.

“I’m not sure she’ll be happy to see me,” she says.

“She may not be happy, but she’s better off not happy and with you than not happy and alone.” Nicky’s expression grows fierce. “Promise me you’ll watch over her. You’ll look after her?”

“I promise,” she croaks.

“Good.”

“Te amo, Nico,” she whispers.

“Te amo, Mami,” Nicky responds.

He runs through the tear in reality, giggling when he’s bowled over by Victoria greeting him enthusiastically on the other side. He waves goodbye at her with a beaming grin, and Rio waves back. As Nicky leaves her side, the green flames of the torch are snuffed, and the torch itself dissolves into ash in her hand.

It’s only once the portal has closed that Rio releases her physical form and collapses into a pit of oblivion and despair, screaming.

The foundations of the universe quake with the force of Death’s grief. Death was never built to experience loss, and the universe wasn’t built to withstand her agony.

Time slips away. But the world moves on.

Death is forced to gather the scattered, damaged pieces of herself that have been irrevocably splintered by sorrow and fear and anguish, and put herself back together. She is scarred for eternity.

By the time Rio returns to Agatha’s side… it’s too late. Agatha lives, but is lost to her.

Agatha never forgives her.

Rio doesn’t blame her. Because she can’t forgive herself either.

Chapter 9

Chapter by AnonFandomBandit

Chapter Notes

hi all. thanks for waiting so patiently for this chapter. i've had pneumonia these past couple weeks and i'm still recovering, and barely have the energy to write. luckily this chapter was basically already finished

hope you enjoy

please heed content warnings in the tags

Agatha sleeps for two days straight.

Rio would be incandescent with worry if the monitoring spell set on her wife’s soul and lifeline didn’t reassure her that Agatha’s health is not declining. She is not in some sort of coma, merely exhausted.

She has slipped into a deep slumber, almost a light form of hibernation; it’s good, because it means she is not dreaming, and therefore not disturbed by nightmares… and bad, because she is impossible to wake.

It’s been a long time coming, really. She’s been starved and undernourished for three years. Her mind was essentially imprisoned and tortured, and so the mental strain has been building. Drained of power, her magical core wounded and hollow, Agatha’s body can no longer rely on drawing on her magic for energy and healing. So… she sleeps.

Rio tends to her as best as she can, using magic to transport fluids, food, and the reinvigoration elixir into her stomach so that Agatha doesn’t get dehydrated or hungry. She uses cleansing enchantments to wash her body, swap her clothes, and change the bed sheets.

Agatha may consider it violating when she eventually awakens, but Rio knows that she will back down if she reminds her that Rio could do it all manually, without the use of magic. The only thing she does do by hand is brush Agatha’s beautiful long hair.

“The last time you slept so long in this bed was the weekend before you gave birth to Nicky,” the green witch murmurs, combing through her wife’s dark chocolate tresses. “Do you remember, mi amor? You slept for twenty-six hours. I had to wake you, for sustenance and for you to go to the bathroom. Nicky finally settled after a month of assaulting your kidneys and stomach, keeping you awake at night.”

Setting the brush aside, Rio uses her fingers instead, massaging her fingertips into Agatha’s skull, which she knows her partner loves.

“I had to rouse you and pour tiny amounts of water into your mouth every couple of hours. I used the mother-of-pearl conch shell I bought you for your birthday that year, for creating blessed water… hoping it would bring you peaceful dreams. You’re so cute when you’re all sleepy and grumbly,” she continues to say, knowing she is talking to herself, but believing that maybe, there’s a possibility Agatha might be able to hear her in her sleep.

Once Agatha’s hair is smooth and free of knots, she decides to twist it into double dutch braids to prevent tangles. She tucks the braids out of the way, lying down on her side next to Agatha, watching her chest rise and fall rhythmically. Her eyes are still beneath her eyelids. The spirit witch sleeps restfully, without dreams or nightmares, as her mind heals.

She sees a faint shean of sweat on Agatha’s forehead, but determines quickly that it’s not fever, and merely her overheating beneath the blankets because of the roaring fire across the room from them. Rio peels the quilt back so that it pools around Agatha’s waist instead, exposing her torso. Agatha’s sleep shirt has ridden up in Rio’s recent efforts to maneuver her into different reclined positions to better brush her hair.

The silvery stretch marks decorating her wife’s abdomen gleam in the firelight, and Rio cannot resist reaching out with trembling fingers to trace over them fondly. “When I did wake you for food, you stayed curled up on this very pillow, nibbling on crackers and sweetmeats like an adorable little mouse,” Rio whispers. “Your last trimester, you asked me every day to conjure up strawberries, even though they were out of season. Nicky’s sweet tooth made you crave fruit and confectionery like crazy.” She laughs, the beginning of longing tears brimming in her eyes, remembering aloud, “At one point, you tasted like nothing but honeyed apples and maple candy for weeks. Good thing Death can’t develop cavities because I definitely would have from kissing you if I were human.”

On the morning of the second day, Señor Scratchy keeps an eye on Agatha while Rio brews up a fresh, more potent batch of the elixir. The old potions clearly were not strong enough.

As Rio plucks herbs from her garden and muddles them in a quartz mortar, she wonders if Agatha has built up a tolerance to those kind of potions because she has previously abused them. A very similar elixir, one that is essentially an anti-anxiety potion that induces dreamless sleep, uses many of the same ingredients as the reinvigoration elixir.

Did Agatha seek out a potions witch in the past to self-medicate her depression and post-traumatic stress? Did she become addicted to anti-anxiety elixirs and end up taking too frequent, too high doses to overcome her grief and turmoil, and ensure restful sleep at night? If she did abuse potions, when and why did she decide to wean herself off them, and how difficult was it?

Rio suspects that she will never know the answers to her questions, because Agatha is unlikely to be willing to give them.

Despite the stress she is under, Agatha does not appear to suffer any more seizures. Nocturnal seizures are difficult to detect, from what Rio understands, but the monitoring spell would pick up on any - and she doesn’t get alerted to anything.

Death still keeps a cautious eye on her wife, however. She barely leaves her alone, and remains constantly aware of the steady rise and fall of her chest. Agatha will not die under her watch. And if she has her way, she will not suffer any longer either.

A new development that Rio recognizes, late into the second day of Agatha’s mini-coma, is that she can sense her wife’s soul again. It’s obviously a side effect of what happened when Agatha kissed her, where she pushed her soul upwards to brush against Rio’s for a fleeting second, trying to encourage vulnerability. It’s backfired, because now Agatha has unintentionally made her soul vulnerable and accessible to Rio again.

Whatever barrier was set up, whatever block Agatha put in place to dampen down their witch soul bond, has now faded to the point where the link has snapped back into place. It’s weak, still, a metaphorical single frayed piece of string tying them together, but it’s enough.

She won’t do anything while Agatha is asleep. Rio refuses to abuse her wife in that manner by taking advantage of her. Yes, access to Agatha’s soul has essentially given her a backdoor into her mind, but the spirit witch has not given her permission to enter.

Agatha’s mind has been messed with enough without her consent; undoubtedly the spirit witch has set up some very nasty trapdoors for any future intruders. Rio will not pry, no matter how much she wants to. She will not hurt her wife in the same way Wanda Maximoff did.

Her reapers are effectively covering her duties and no souls have called out for her so far. She spends the first day Agatha sleeps sharpening her scythe knife to the point where it can easily nick and slice through the fabric of reality just by swiping it through the air. For the safety of the universe, she’s forced to tuck it away into a pocket dimension and no longer use it as a fidget toy. For lack of better things to do, Rio finds herself summoning paper and charcoal pencils to do some absentminded sketching.

She mostly uses her sleeping partner as her subject. She’s never really dabbled in any human hobbies besides gardening and cooking, much too busy with ferrying dead souls to the afterlife to try anything else. Her conversation with Agatha about hobbies over dinner, however, has her wondering about what she might enjoy passing the time with.

She draws Agatha from various different angles, depending on where she’s sitting in the room or lying on the bed. Her wife makes for an excellent artist’s model when she’s unconscious, not moving beyond occasionally stretching or turning her head.

The sharp angles of Agatha’s face are also challenging to get perfect, and Rio finds herself spending hours tracing out the lines of her delicate jaw and drawing individual thin hairs wisping downwards, attempting to mimic the wild nature of her wife’s mane.

Rio jumps and nearly flies off the bed in the middle of a sketch depicting her wife’s side profile when she hears a loud thump from behind her. She twists around to see Señor Scratchy sitting on top of the bedside table, glaring at her with his soulless eyes.

“You,” she scowls.

Scratchy thumps again, his whiskers twitching in a scornful sort of way that suggests he is responding back, just as vehemently, Yep, me. And what are you gonna do about it?.

She has to begrudgingly admit that she is growing somewhat fond of Agatha’s stupid rabbit familiar. Señor Scratchy can be a fussy little asshole when he wants to be - as most tamed minor demons do - but he adores Agatha. She still has no clue why he chose to glamour himself as an adorable fluffy bunny, which is the least intimidating form he could have chosen, but he makes for a remarkable therapy animal… for Agatha, that is.

Rio, he clearly just tolerates.

The rabbit cuddles up to Agatha ninety percent of the time, and thumps his hind paws aggressively at Rio whenever the green witch gets too close or touches her wife - such as right now. He leaps from the bedside table to return to one of his favourite positions curled up on the pillow next to Agatha’s head.

He squeaks at Death angrily, as if to tell her, yo, back the hell off, this is MY witch.

“She was mine first,” Rio tells him, pissed off.

Scratchy eyes her with obvious distrust. He’s judging her. You hurt her, she can practically hear him sneering at her. You’re the one who makes her cry and have nightmares and breakdowns.

“I’m taking care of her and protecting her as best I can, just like you,” Rio informs him calmly. “And unlike you, I have the opposable thumbs to do it.”

He looks outraged at her. He thumps furiously. Tiny bastard.

Rio grabs him by his scruff, lifting him into the air. He dangles from her grasp with a murderous expression, his beady black eyes glinting and glowing a faint crimson as he lets his demonic nature seep through. “Stop posturing. I’m Death, you’re never gonna beat me in terms of power, kiddo.”

Scratchy glowers at her. And then, with immense agility, twists his body around so he can sink his little incisors into her wrist. It doesn’t hurt at all, but it does pierce Rio’s skin, much to her surprise, and she ends up letting go just out of shock.

Scratchy drops back onto the mattress and hastily backs away, hissing at her with glowing red eyes. When Rio lunges to try and grab him again, he scrambles up onto Agatha’s sternum and loaves there, settling down. He knows that Rio will not risk hurting Agatha whilst trying to grab him.

“Thin fucking ice, buddy,” Rio growls, pointing at him. “We’re on the same side here. We’re both non-negotiable in terms of being part of Agatha’s life so we have no choice but to work together. I’ll continue to play therapy wife and you will continue being the most irritating emotional support animal alive. But bite me again and I’ll turn you into stew,” she states. “Or better yet, I’ll pull out Victoria and you can become tarantula food.”

Scratchy visibly rolls his eyes. He no longer seems intimidated by her threats now, probably because he knows Rio would never go through with them, lest she upset and enrage Agatha. He snuggles up to the sleeping spirit witch, his adorable little bunny tail twitching.

He does kick Rio again, but he also lets her pet him sometimes. Their rivalry continues, to a lesser degree.

To be petty, and get some amusement out of it, the green witch always draws Señor Scratchy as a big black and white smudge, barely visible next to Agatha. It massively annoys him, and he actually tries attacking her pencils, ferociously chewing on them until they snap. She repairs them with a click of her fingers, which makes the bunny sulk and turn his ass to her.

It’s early in the morning of the third day of Agatha’s hibernation that she begins to stir, and of course, Sod’s Law dictates that she will finally wake up whilst Rio is out of the room, brewing apple mint and chamomile tea for herself in the kitchen. She instantly senses her wife’s awakening through the weak thread of their bond and a shift in the monitoring spell.

Nearly dropping her tea in her haste to run to the bedroom, she sets the cup on the dining table and arrives just in time - to see Agatha stumbling out of the door, clinging to the walls, looking disoriented and confused. Despite looking pale and half-asleep, her hair a bird’s nest and her pajamas crumpled, she’s just as gorgeous as always. Señor Scratchy is trying - and failing - to pull her back towards the bed, biting and tugging on her silk pajama pants, releasing exasperated little squeaks.

He shoots the green witch a glare that screams back me up here, you fucking useless cosmic entity!

“Agatha?” Rio calls out worriedly.

Her wife whips around, jolting at the sound of her wife, and comes close to falling over. It’s normal that she’s a bit rocky on her feet considering she’s been unconscious in bed for two days. The green witch lunges to catch her, wrapping her arms around Agatha’s waist to hold the spirit witch upright. It of course results in their hips being anchored together, with her wife having no choice but to brace her hands on Rio’s shoulders.

“Hey! Hey, hey, relax, you’re okay, you’re fine. Welcome back to the land of the living, sweetheart,” she grins. She was beginning to think she’d need to stab her with an epi-pen. Pump her full of adrenaline and force her awake. Softening her voice, she asks much more tentatively, “How are you feeling?”, fully expecting Agatha to take a swing at her.

“‘Welcome back’?” Agatha parrots, wiping sleep dust from her eyes with a scowl. “You’re such a dramatic bitch. I just had a nap, s’not like I went anywhere.” She jabs her finger into the green witch’s collarbone. “And knowing you, you pervert, you probably sat and watched me sleep the whole time.”

Huh. Agatha seems to be… in a remarkably good mood, considering that the last time she and Rio spoke, she was screaming and crying at her and insisting that she hates her. The green witch was honestly expecting Agatha to be completely mortified by her attempt to manipulate Death by kissing her; along with that embarrassment, she’s also anticipating anger and defensiveness in the form of Agatha insulting and lashing out.

But that’s not happening. And why is she getting a weird vibe from what her wife just said? She called her a pervert and accused her of watching her sleep again, when they’ve already had that conversation? Deja vu.

“A nap? Agatha, I think you slept a little longer than you think you did,” Rio says cautiously. Her wife will undoubtedly through the hissy fits of all hissy fits the moment she finds out that she’s been unconscious for two days.

Agatha finally seems to stop swaying and find her feet, because she eases back and away from Rio’s support. She gestures at Señor Scratchy, who leaps into her arms from the floor with incredible strength and agility that a regular pet bunny definitely would not have. She ambles away from Rio and into the kitchen.

The green witch trails after her nervously, bewildered as to what precisely is happening. Agatha no longer seems to be in the middle of a mental breakdown, and no longer seems at all depressed about being locked of out Nicky’s room. It’s a full 180, and she’s baffled as to why and how.

“It’s morning,” Agatha exclaims in audible shock, as she sees the sunlight spilling through the cottage windows and illuminating the kitchen in a soft golden glow. “Did you not wake me up for dinner? Thought you were adamant that I had to eat to get my strength back.” She wheels around, leaning back against the counter as she strokes her rabbit familiar in her arms. “Did you forget? Getting negligent in your nursing duties, Lady Death?” she snarks.

“Dinner?” Rio echoes, her heart plummeting into her stomach like a stone.

Oh.

Oh fuck.

Amnesia. Short-term, but it’s absolutely some form of memory loss. Agatha isn’t distraught or angry about the events that occurred after dinner two days ago, because she can’t remember them at all. No wonder she’s in a decent, fairly stable mindset. Her brain has seemingly reset and she’s lost the memories of their argument and her meltdown.

What’s caused it, though? That’s the main mystery. Rio shakes her head, bemused. Is the amnesia seizure-related? She knows that the brain can take a while to recover from a seizure, so short-term memory can be disrupted for some time. And repeated seizures, particularly in a short space of time, can mean it takes longer for those memories to return. They can even start to cause damage to the brain.

She’s certain that Agatha hasn’t suffered from any seizures in the past two days whilst asleep, because surely the monitoring spell would have picked up on them. Even if they weren’t tonic-clonic seizures like the last two she suffered from, and were instead absence or very mild temporal lobe seizures, Rio is sure that she would have been alerted.

Which means this is not anything to do with Agatha’s seizures. Could it instead be yet another side effect of Agatha breaking out of the Scarlet Witch’s hex? A reset button, this time, instead of a circuit breaker or kill switch?

Or… is this a result of Agatha’s trauma? Rio has always suspected that her wife has chronic PTSD, considering she is a survivor of long-term, prolonged childhood abuse, persecution, and multiple murder attempts. Perhaps this is memory loss triggered by exposure to severe psychological and emotional stress.

She gives the monitoring spell a good yank, and then for good measure, pokes very gently at Agatha’s soul, now she has access to it again. She’s struck with an overwhelming tsunami of turmoil and dejection. Agatha may not remember what happened, but her soul does, and those memories are not entirely lost - they are tucked away at the back of her mind, suppressed. She is indeed suffering from dissociative amnesia - an involuntary coping mechanism to protect her own mind.

Is this Rio’s fault? Did she push Agatha too hard, too fast? Is this a result of her locking Agatha out of their dead son’s room and disrupting her mind’s processing of past trauma?

“You’re acting as if you’re the one whose head got rattled from nearly drowning this morning and not me,” Agatha says, rolling her eyes. She starts to putter around with the coffee machine and searching the cupboards for mugs. “Maybe you’re finally going senile in your old age. You’re - what? Nearly 14 billion at this point?” She glances over her shoulder and smiles faux-sweetly at the green witch. It makes her feel sick. “Don’t worry, I’m sure there’s a nice old retirement home for cosmic entities a good couple of light years away that your loving wife can book you into. Fancy playing fetch and bringing me a witch with some spare magic to feast on one last time, before we get you celestially sectioned?”

Rio wants to cry. Agatha is being so sarky and playful with her, and trying to provoke her into banter, and it’s only because she can’t remember the last two devastating conversations they had. From his witch’s arms, Señor Scratchy stares at Death, his arctic gaze penetrating yet sympathetic. He can see she’s freaking out, but he seems to be rolling with the punches.

Don’t wig out on me now, she can sense him communicating to her crossly. Get your shit together and play the fuck along. Agatha NEEDS us.

And Scratchy is right. Rio has to stay calm. Panicking about her wife’s amnesia will only cause Agatha herself to get agitated, and that’s the last thing she needs right now.

As much as Rio despises it, she has to pretend that everything is normal - their normal - and hope that Agatha’s memory comes back by itself. She has no fucking clue how human brains work. They’re needlessly complex and stupidly fragile. A dose of the reinvigoration elixir with an extra helping of Rio’s healing saliva might help, but there’s nothing else she can think to do.

So she acts as if nothing is wrong, gently hip-checking her wife out of the way so she can shut down the coffee machine and brew them fresh cups of the apple mint and chamomile tea she unfortunately abandoned to go cold ten minutes ago. Squawking in disgust that her efforts to acquire caffeine have been thwarted, Agatha pulls herself up to sit on the nearby counter to sulk, petting Scratchy on her lap.

“No coffee until you are no longer at risk of seizures, and no siphoning until your magical core is healed,” Rio informs her sternly. And then, knowing that Agatha actually will want an answer as to why the green witch ‘didn’t wake her up for dinner’, as she believes, she lies her ass off; “Had to duck out for Death duties so Scratchy kept an eye on you, but I was away longer than expected. I didn’t fancy waking you at three in the morning and dealing with your inevitable tantrum.” She carries the mugs, with their teabags steeping in boiled water and a teaspoon of honey added to each, over to the dining table. “Drink this and I’ll make you some breakfast.”

Agatha hops down from the counter and takes her seat at the table without complaint. Scratchy ends up on her lap again, chewing on some stray blades of hay, while the spirit witch sips at her tea and supervises Rio cooking for her. She doesn’t seem to suspect anything is out of the ordinary, and Rio catches sight of her squishing her rabbit’s cheeks together and silently cooing over him as she rubs his ears.

Avocado and eggs on toast are plated and slid in front of her wife, and Rio passes Agatha a dose of the new and improved elixir to chase the food down. “Eat,” she orders, and adds on a slightly politer, “Please,” when the spirit witch hits her with an admonishing look.

Agatha quirks an eyebrow but obediently eats and drinks her tea. She swallows down the elixir with a sour grimace. “Did you heal me in my sleep after the shit that went down in the bath?” she wonders aloud, scraping the toast crumbs on her plate with her knife. “Because I don’t feel any aftereffects from my near-drowning and I would have thought I’d at least have some chest pain from your terrible CPR.”

Rio pauses. Agatha did have chest pain on the day of the drowning incident, but has had multiple doses of the elixir and painkillers since then. Not that she remembers that.

“I increased the potency of the reinvigoration elixir,” she says, deciding to answer as truthfully as possible. “I spelled it into your stomach while you were asleep.”

“Without my consent? Rude,” Agatha huffs.

“My bad,” the green witch shrugs.

Agatha rolls her eyes, muttering, “She says, with no guilt in her voice whatsoever.”

Rio doesn’t feel guilty about that at all. What she does feel guilty about is her wife’s dissociative amnesia and how she might have contributed to it. She refills the spirit witch’s now empty cup of tea with a fresh tea bag and hot water with a wave of her hand.

Watching closely as Agatha sips at the tea and occasionally rubs at her temples with one hand, she asks concernedly, “How does your head feel? Are you experiencing any aches and pains… any fuzziness?”

Agatha sinks back in her chair, pulling one leg up onto the seat so she can hug it as she carries on nursing her tea. “I feel hungover as fuck, if that’s what you’re hinting at. Is that a side effect or something? That new version of the elixir packs a punch, huh?”

“It can cause some drowsiness,” Rio acknowledges. Drowsiness does not lead to memory loss, though.

When Agatha finishes eating and announces she wishes to change clothes, Rio very reluctantly waits outside the bedroom door, tapping her foot on the floor impatiently. Scratchy has followed Agatha into the bedroom, so she’s not alone, and Rio can easily monitor her well-being using the spell. But she’s still set on edge by the idea of Agatha being out of her sight when she’s in such a frail mental state.

What if Agatha suffers more memory loss while she’s alone? Or worse, what if she remembers?

When her wife finally calls for her to come in, giving her permission to enter, Rio steps inside and her mind goes blank. Agatha is sitting with her legs hanging off the bed, dressed in a faded vintage Fleetwood Mac ‘Sisters of the Moon’ t-shirt and a pair of thick seaweed green leggings, that she’s rolled up to her knees.

Her wife’s calves are entirely exposed and all of a sudden all Rio wants to do is fall to her knees and sink her teeth into them, kissing and licking away the marks. She licks her lips and mentally debates how much she would have to grovel for Agatha to pull her leggings down to hang off one ankle, spread her legs, and let Rio eat her out.

“Where did this come from?” Agatha asks in a quiet voice, and Rio’s gaze flickers to what she’s referring to - and she is almost instantly turned off, the heat in her belly dissipating into a cold uncomfortable ache.

Agatha is holding their son’s crumpled patchwork baby onesie in her hands, staring down at it with glassy eyes. Scratchy is perched on the bed next to her, one paw extended and resting on her arm to offer silent support. When he peers over at Rio, it’s with an expression that is clearly meant to convey, oh, you’re really in the shit now.

Which is true, because her wife can’t remember anything that happened last night, so can’t remember fleeing to Nicky’s room after their argument - so won’t recall how she clung to his infant sleepsuit as she cried herself to sleep.

“It’s Nicky’s,” Rio says for lack of a better reply, her mouth dry.

“I know what it is,” Agatha hisses, looking stressed. “Did you bring it out of his room?”

Technically, she did, when she carried her wife out of there last night. She thinks fast. “You were restless all night and mumbling his name in your sleep, so I thought it might comfort you,” she lies. Taking a hesitant step towards the bed, Rio brushes her hand over the baby grow, giving it a light tug. “I can put it back -”

“No,” Agatha cuts her off in a fearsome growl, her eyes ablaze.

Her hackles raised, she looks seconds away from rushing forward and sinking her teeth into Rio’s arm with a feral yowl, like a cat whose kitten is being taken away from her. Rio knows she is substantially stronger and faster than her wife currently, and could very easily pluck the baby grow from her grasp. The sheer panic on the spirit witch’s face, however, turns her stomach.

Agatha would fight her until her death - not Rio’s, of course - to maintain possession of her son’s onesie now that Rio has threatened to take it away. She releases her hold on Nicky’s baby grow and slowly backs away, hands raised.

Upon seeing Rio’s apologetic expression, and realizing how aggressively she reacted, Agatha tries immediately to act as if nothing happened. She pushes the baby grow to the side, which inadvertently ends up smothering her rabbit familiar, as if she wasn’t just ready to bite Rio’s head off from trying to take it from her.

Flipping her now messy dutch braids over her shoulders, Agatha begins to take them down, running trembling fingers through her locks of hair. The spells Rio has used to clean her body over the past few days have prevented her hair from getting greasy, but she’ll still probably want to wash it later.

Scratchy manages to free himself from where he’s buried beneath his namesake’s sleepsuit, but nearly tumbles off the bed as he kicks it away from him. Agatha reacts just in time, scooping him up as he falls mid-air. He squeaks in thanks and nuzzles into her neck when the spirit witch cuddles him, dropping a fond kiss on his head and then plopping him on her lap. Rio resists the urge to glare. She wants to be the one being kissed on the head by Agatha. The annoying bunny doesn’t deserve it any more than she does.

Ignorant of her jealousy, Agatha gives Señor Scratchy a pet on his plump little rump with one hand, whilst the other stretches out to tentatively stroke over Nicky’s baby grow.

“I… I’d like to keep it in here,” she murmurs.

“That’s okay. Why don’t we put it under your pillow, like a good luck charm?” Rio suggests.

Her wife swallows and nods in agreement. The green witch creeps forward and keeps her movements slow and visible as she takes hold of one arm of the infant onesie. But once again, Agatha grabs it, gritting her teeth. Rio dares not pull on it any harder for risk of tearing the stitches between the patches and ripping one of the sleeves off.

“Agatha? You have to let it go,” she encourages gently.

You have to let him go.

She’s fully aware of just how ironic it is that she is the one urging her wife to let go of something, when she has refused to let go of Agatha for centuries now, despite the spirit witch’s desperate attempts to hide and escape from her. But they’re entirely different situations.

Agatha is her wife, her soulmate, her one and only true love. The chasm between them, started by that first initial fracture of Nicky’s death, may have grown over the last two hundred and fifty years, due to grief and hatred and distance. But Agatha is still reachable. Rio loves her, and she senses, deep in her black heart, that Agatha still loves her in return.

Nicky, on the other hand, is gone. The only way Agatha will see him again is by dying, which she has no plans to do anytime soon - and Rio will not let her die before her time. Agatha’s non-acceptance of their son’s death has not allowed her to process her loss. She does not need to move on, but she does need to move forward.

Agatha clenches her jaw, looking down at Nicky’s baby grow with overwhelming melancholic wistfulness. Rio knows that if her wife had it her way, she would never let it go. Rubbing her thumb over one particular patch of the sleepsuit, she exhales with a shudder.

When Rio catches sight of what that patch is, she nearly falls to her knees and sobs. It’s the square directly over where Nicky’s heart would have lain, that Agatha sewed together from two pieces of cloak: her own worn-thin navy blue velvet cloak, the one that Rio gifted her for her birthday the first year of their relationship, and a section of sheer lacy fabric from the hem of Rio’s Lady Death cape. Agatha embroidered their initials into it with gold thread she pinched from a wealthy merchant passing through the closest village’s market. He deserved it, from what she remembers; he was attempting to sell belladonna eye drops to pregnant women.

There’s a blank spot on the bottom of the square where Agatha intended to sew Nicky’s name beneath their own, once he was born.

She never got the chance.

With extreme reluctance, Agatha finally releases her clingy hold on the baby grow, passing it off to Rio. She watches with beady eyes and pursed lips as Death very cautiously takes it into her possession, shakes it out, and then carefully folds it. Delicately, she places it under the pillow on Agatha’s side of the bed. Even though she’s no longer clasping the baby grow like a security blanket, Agatha appears to visibly relax, now she knows that it’s not going anywhere.

Rio sighs and ruffles the fur on Scratchy’s head before poking him, so he hops off the mattress and away to escape her bothering him. “Come on, let’s go to the living room, hm? I have some green craft books you might enjoy reading.”

The offer of magical literature to read immediately grabs Agatha’s attention, but she scoffs. “Green craft books? What about my books, from the basement in Westview?” Her eyes widen in panic. She can’t remember them having this conversation before, so asks frantically, “Please don’t tell you left them there for some random magic-adjacent crook to stumble upon and pilfer.” She bats her eyelids as she adds, “There might be some spirit magic I can use to study the effects of Wanda’s hex breaking on my mind.”

“You currently don’t have any magic, so they’re of no use to you,” Rio reminds her. Although, that is a good point. She might not want Agatha reading any of the books, lest they tempt her to try and perform magic and injure her magical core further, but Rio could take a peek at them.

Scowling, Agatha waves her hand at her, muttering, “Alright, killjoy, no need to rub salt in the wound, it stings enough already, thank you.” She heaves herself to her feet, giving the pillow where the onesie lies beneath one last longing look, pressing a kiss to her fingers which she then dots on top of the embroidered square patch. Then she glances over at Rio, appears to steel herself, and announces, “I want to go for a walk.”

Rio stares at her.

What.

A walk? “In the woods?” she questions, baffled.

“No, Rio, on the fucking beach. Of course in the woods,” Agatha growls. She strides over to the window to squint out at the forest beyond the cottage, surrounding them. “Don’t you dare blather on about it being too cold and damp, and me being too weak. I’m not going to keel over from going on a leisurely walk.”

She might. She’s suffering from short-term amnesia, for the Divine Mother’s sake, and has experienced multiple seizures. Not to mention she’s been exhausted and starved for the three years where she was being mind controlled and running around Westview, unhinged and off her rocker. A walk in the forest could very well make her incredibly sick and lead to her collapsing.

But Agatha seems desperate to leave the house. Rio casts a glance outside, mulling it over in her head. The weather today is not too harsh; it’s a mild fall day, with not too much wind, and no rain on the horizon. With the cover of the trees, it’s probably warm enough that her wife could get away with just wearing coats and boots.

As a green witch, Rio knows the woods like the back of her hand, and can communicate with nature, so she knows there’s nothing dangerous out there right now. The forest will protect Agatha if she asks it to.

Agatha must see the conflict on her face, because she presses, “I can take Scratchy with me, and he’ll carry me back if I get too tired.”

Laughing, Rio asks her in disbelief, “Your rabbit is going to carry you back?”

“He’s a magical demon familiar. He can shapeshift,” Agatha insists. Rio knows that’s true; shapeshifting is not unique in terms of demon familiar abilities. Her own familiar is capable of it. The spirit witch rubs a hand over her face with a tired exhalation, pinching the bridge of her nose. “I need to get out of this cottage, Rio. I need fresh air.”

“You can get fresh air by opening a window.”

Agatha swats her. “RIO.” And then, knowing that Rio cannot resist her when she pouts, she lays it on thick, her blue eyes watery and pleading.

Rio groans. She’s definitely going to regret this, but she thinks it might actually be a good idea. Agatha may have lost her memories, but being away from the cottage might give her a mental break from the trauma and negative feelings associated with their old home.

“Fine. But I’m coming with you,” she asserts.

“I never said you couldn’t,” Agatha murmurs.

She does, however, look very excited at the idea of escaping the confines of the cottage walls and being able to step out into the New England woods again, which she has always had a special connection to. Ripping open the closet doors, where Rio has stuffed all of her clothes from the Westview house, she begins to throw shirts and pants and other garments over her shoulders onto the floor. Rio leans against the wall, watching on with resigned scorn as clothes scatter on the ground. Agatha won’t be picking up her mess later; Rio will.

Eventually, Agatha pulls out a plain black sweater and a gorgeous deep navy blue trench coat with a plum inner lining. It’s long, and looks warm, and therefore suitable for a hike through the hoods. There are embroidered runes in the lining too, from what Rio is able to spot, but she’ll need to examine it closer at a later time to identify which runes they are. Her wife selects a pair of knee-high black leather boots that will protect her calves from the brambles and thistles.

Agatha is out of breath already, by the time she’s finished yanking on the boots and dressing in her sweater and coat. Rio grimaces, but says nothing as she observes the spirit witch wiping beads of sweat off her forehead with an annoyed expression. If she dares to comment on how exhausted her wife is from simply getting ready to go out on a walk, Agatha will be pissed off with her for the entire rest of the day, even though Rio is right to be concerned.

Unbothered by the cold and used to walking barefoot, Rio doesn’t bother putting on shoes or a jacket. She follows her wife as she marches out of the bedroom. She does manage to convince Agatha to carry another dose of the reinvigoration potion with her, in her pocket, just in case she gets dizzy. She chews on some rosemary and mint for her ‘hangover’ as well, which will help reduce her tiredness and nausea.

Rio, who knows that her headache is a sign of something much more concerning than just fatigue, gives the monitoring spell a little poke, just to check that it’s still working. It seems as if it is, so if Agatha does start to feel bad during their walk and tries to lie about it, at least Rio will know. What she won’t know is if Agatha suffers any more memory loss.

Señor Scratchy is waiting for them by the front door, and as soon as it’s open, he races outside, bounding happily amongst the ground ferns. Agatha shakes her head in amusement and heads after him, casting a look back and beckoning Rio with a single finger.

“Come frolic in the woods with me like the old days,” Agatha says, wiggling her eyebrows.

“Oh, ‘like the old days’, hmm?” the green witch smirks. “You looking for a frisky forest romp, mi amor? I hope you don’t mind those leggings being torn.”

Agatha tuts. “Don’t be crude,” she warns.

“You can’t use the word frolic and not expect me to tease you about how we used to go at it like rabbits in this forest.” Scratchy squeaks in protest from where he’s standing on his haunches, peering back at them. “Oh, shut up, conejito bastardo, it’s just an expression!”

“Behave,” Agatha scolds her. “And try and keep up!” She stalks off into the undergrowth, with surprising speed as she begins to weave through the trees, following the nearest deer trail.

Rio runs her hands over her face with a silent groan, and obediently follows. This promises proper chaos.

Chapter 10

Chapter by AnonFandomBandit

Chapter Notes

9 months huh

finished my phd, submitted my thesis, and got a new job and research contract since then

well. here we go. an 11k chapter

please heed the tags added. this chapter is not wanda maximoff friendly (sorry wanda, you're the villain in agatha's story!). it also goes into depth of some magical lore :D

Agatha stalks through the woods with feline grace, instinctively following along a deer trail, so as to avoid disturbing the thick vegetation around her. She glides along the forest floor silently, like a lithe, elegant big cat. The fall breeze ruffles her mane of dark hair and makes her coat flap behind her dramatically.

Rio shadows her. Despite Agatha’s exhaustion and ill health, her wife never falters. Her steps are sure and steady. She wandered the trails of this forest for decades until she could walk them blindfolded, albeit that was centuries ago. It seems, however, that she still remembers every craggy rock and hindering tree root, ducking below low-lying branches without even having to glance their way to judge their distance.

It reminds Rio that Agatha is not, if she continues to play with the cat metaphor, a domesticated, tame housecat. She is feral, and as wild as the bobcat and rare Canadian lynx who roam the surrounding forests and mountains.

Yes, she does very occasionally enjoy wandering inside to be fed and pampered and admired, but keeping her cooped up is insanity - it’s just asking to eventually get mauled. Allowing Agatha out of the cottage to wander the woods was definitely the right choice here; she seems relaxed, as if she’s finally migrated home.

Scratchy has shifted from the form of a fluffy domesticated rabbit into a spry young hare, although he maintains his unique white, brown, and grey pelt. He bounds through the bushes and grass ahead of his witch, pausing every so often in the boxing position to swivel his ears, alert and looking for danger. Occasionally, he’ll race back to Agatha’s side and circle her a couple of times just to reassure himself that she’s not flagging, before rushing ahead again.

Seeing Agatha’s familiar’s glee at being free to run around, she feels a twinge of guilt in her heart that she tends to keep her own familiar secreted away. Rio releases Victoria from her pocket dimension; the tarantula crawls up onto her shoulder, waving her front legs in a happy hello, before the green witch transforms her into the form of a raven.

Victoria does not seem particularly pleased about this change, cawing viciously and pecking at Rio’s cheek, which tickles and makes her giggle. Agatha’s head whips around at the sound, her eyes wide and startled; she appears to briefly falter in her stride before turning back around and stalking off again.

Victoria fluffs up her feathers and fans her black wings before taking off into the air. A silent telepathic command from Rio orders her to fly high above their heads to scout for danger, and Victoria gains height until she’s a black speck high above them, darting between the towering tops of the trees. 

Lady Death follows in the tail of her beloved wife from a distance, wanting to stay close but not infringe on Agatha’s personal space.
