The forest sings around them, its beating heart coming back to life with the return of the Original Green Witch, who blessed the ground and trees long ago when she and Agatha first decided to call these woods their home.

Rio can sense the pulse of every animal surrounding them for miles on end: the mice that scatter upon feeling the vibrations of their footsteps, the foxes burrowed with their suckling young, and the massive deer herd far to the North, grazing next to a stream in a clearing.

Their souls buzz in her ears, like constant white background noise, their lifelines calling out to her. Rio dials her senses down, tuning them out, until the only creatures she needs to concern herself with are her wife and their two familiars.

Skipping forward a couple of steps to get a little bit closer to her wife, Rio starts off brightly, “So -”

“No,” Agatha interrupts bluntly.

She pouts. “I didn’t say anything.”

“You were going to. Don’t. It’s annoying.”

“Me talking is annoying?”

“Can we not just enjoy a nice, quiet, calm walk in the woods?” Agatha says in exasperation.

Rio snorts upon hearing that, and quickens her stride until she’s walking side-by-side with the spirit witch. She leans in to nudge her with her elbow gently, teasing, “You? Quiet? Calm? I don’t think you know the definition of the words.”

Agatha releases a long-suffering, heaving sigh, not pushing Rio away at all, but also ending up stepping to the side to avoid tripping over a couple of stray rocks. “You’re one to talk. You sure you’re a green witch and not a chaos witch?” she fires back. “Isn’t your expertise anarchy?”

Wrinkling her nose in distaste, Rio complains, “No need to insult me. Life and death are very organised, thank you very much. It’s black and white, as clear-cut as it can be.”

As if she, Lady Death, would ever identify as a chaos witch. Yes, functioning as a primordial magical being and one of the main cosmic entities of the universe, she has access to every type of magic in existence, including chaos, but given her jurisdiction is over life and death, and the fact that she practically invented green magic, she much prefers to be referred to as a green witch. The original.

“You and your rules,” Agatha grumbles under her breath. She bends down briefly to snatch up a branch from the ground, using it as a fidget toy as she begins to pluck and peel shards of bark off it with slightly trembling fingers. “Witches used to accuse me of being a chaos witch, you know. Idiots.”

“If only they knew how impossible that even is,” Rio laughs.

Her wife comes to a halt, casting a look over her shoulder at her with a bemused raised eyebrow. Wait, does Agatha not know? How? Didn’t she study the Darkhold? And surely she’s read dozens of other books about magical compatibility - hell, she owns a grimoire on spirit and green magic synergy. But judging by her bewildered look, maybe she isn’t aware.

She supposes that chaos witches are just as rare as those inclined towards spirit magic, so perhaps no witch has ever written about the possibility of combining the two magic types before.

“Chaos magic and spirit magic are diametrically opposed when it comes to the order of the universe,” Rio explains to Agatha, blooming a beautiful fuchsia gaillardia flower in one hand, and then a scarlet one in the other. She twirls the red flower in her hand while offering her wife the purple one. “Chaos is entropy, spirit is syntropy. As the most powerful spirit witch alive, you would have ripped Wanda Maximoff to shreds if you had truly battled without the Darkhold and her Hex manipulations stunting you. You had her outsmarted at every turn until the dark magic inside of you got a lick of that chaos magic and sent you into a tizzy.” She shakes her head in fond amusement. “You just had to start bragging about the runes and showboating, didn’t you?”

Oh, what a glorious battle it would have been. Rio would have jumped at the chance of getting a front row seat to see Agatha tear the Scarlet Witch apart.

Unfortunately, she’s evidently dropped some new information on her wife, because Agatha stares at her in disbelief, slapping the flower out of her hand as she marches up to Rio and demands, “What do you mean, the Darkhold stunting me? The Darkhold gave me power. I was feeding off its magical energy.”

Rio pouts at her, reaching down to fetch her bruised gaillardia from where it’s drifted to the ground. And then scowls when Scratchy darts in suddenly and grabs it from her hand with a mischievous squeak before running off to hide in the undergrowth. Irritating little shit. That flower was for Agatha, not for her annoying familiar.

“Spirit magic is a form of divine magic, and channels and draws magic from the Triple Goddess, allowing organisation and manipulation of baryonic matter. Dark magic is the same, but allows manipulation of dark matter and is sourced from Chthon.” She spits out the name of the evil elder god, who blatantly disrespects the balance between life and death in the universe and is an insult to her very existence. The idea of her wife borrowing little crumbs of dark magic from him makes her shudder. “You may have felt like you were feeding off the Darkhold, but trust me, Agatha, it was feeding off you in return and crippling your connection with the spirit realms,” Rio informs her grimly. That damned book was also crippling her soul bond connection to Rio.

With every dark spell that Agatha cast from the Darkhold, it stole away a tiny sliver of Agatha’s soul as payment, hence the creeping black rot that consumed her hands. Losing the Darkhold severed the connection that she had to Chthon, allowing her spirit magic to become free and unsuppressed once again - and allowing Rio to finally track her down.

Agatha shakes her head, now hurrying behind Rio as the green witch skips through the forest. Rio busies herself with delicately plucking wood ear mushrooms from the trunks and branches of nearby trees. She munches on a couple of them, and stores the rest of them in a mesh bag she conjures, planning on using them in a soup she will cook for Agatha later.

Agatha gives her a push from behind, just as Rio summons her scythe knife to cut a particularly meaty-looking chicken-of-the-woods mushroom off a dead tree trunk. Damn, Agatha really cannot stand not having Rio’s focus on her when she desires it, poking and prodding at her like a cat constantly meowing for attention.

Yet, Agatha pitches a fit whenever she thinks the green witch is showing her too much attention, similar to how cats will very suddenly turn on a person petting them and bite their hand.

When Rio glances over her shoulder with a raised eyebrow, her wife insists, “The Darkhold taught me dark spells that were leagues above spirit enchantments in power.”

Who is Agatha trying to convince? Rio, or herself? Lady Death hits her with an impassive look, picking the dirt and leaf litter from beneath her nails with the tip of her blade.

“Only because your spirit magic was weakened. The Darkhold would have dampened down your spirit abilities, forcing you to rely on dark magic.” It’ll likely take her a while to learn how to use it properly again. A muscle left unused for so long begins to atrophy. “But when the Scarlet Witch came around - well, chaos magic allows manipulation of all matter, including anti-matter, so the Darkhold would’ve much preferred to bed down with her.” Rio sheathes her knife in her hip holster, and tells her simply, “You lost your fight with her because the Darkhold wanted you to lose.”

It was a reasonably easy conclusion to reach, once Rio quizzed Agatha’s neighbors in Westview and heard their tales and stories of her wife’s fight with the Scarlet Witch. If Agatha mastered the Darkhold well enough to use it as a magical battery and wield its spells without succumbing to the corrupting darkness of the book, then it only makes sense that the Darkhold wished to change hands. Wanda Maximoff was the perfect candidate to lead astray and start taking over as a new vessel for Chthon’s dark magic.

This is, apparently, news to Agatha, though, who first of all looks stunned - so stunned that she freezes, and Scratchy hops up to her to bat at her foot in concern - and then, as Rio’s words sink in, that shock transforms into outrage.

“A fucking book sabotaged my fight with the Scarlet Witch?” Agatha squawks. “Are you saying I would have won that fight otherwise!?”

Without the Darkhold clouding her mind and doing its best to sabotage her? Rio reckons it would have been a close fight, but Agatha’s experience would have given her an advantage that would have allowed her to triumph in the end. Wanda Maximoff may have possessed more raw power than Agatha, but her wife has studied and mastered magic for centuries, and is a categorical genius - especially when it comes to tricking witches.

“Jokes on the Darkhold, it left you for her and then she ended up destroying every copy of it in the multiverse,” Rio chuckles amusedly. She waves the chunky yellow mushroom in Agatha’s face teasingly, before placing it in the bag hanging from her arm. “Talk about toxic relationship.”

Agatha huffs, and holds her hand out for Rio’s knife. The green witch quirks a questioning eyebrow. Rolling her eyes, Agatha makes a gimme motion by flapping her fingers, and then narrows her eyes suspiciously when Rio hesitates.

Should she really be passing her wife a deadly weapon - especially one as dangerous as Death’s scythe - when she is currently suffering from seizures and current dissociative amnesia? What if Agatha has another episode, and harms herself, or tries to harm Rio? She’s more likely to accidentally hurt herself than hurt Rio… or intentionally hurt herself, given her self-destructive tendencies.

Scratchy’s head pops up from where he’s hidden in the undergrowth, his tall hare ears swivelling from side to side. He creeps up towards them and then sits on his haunches, head craned upwards to keep an eye on his witch.

He casts a quick glance towards Rio, nose twitching, and she can sense that he is trying to reassure her that he will help her keep an eye on Agatha while she has a blade in her hands.

Rio sighs, and with immense reluctance, passes her scythe blade over to her wife. The grin that spreads across Agatha’s mouth is far too toothy and thrilled to be normal, and her eyes light up the instant she has possession of a weapon.

Agatha is an expert with knives due to her decades spent living in the New England forests, catching and skinning small animals. As far as Rio knows, Agatha also spent some time collecting, sharpening, and pilfering bayonets during the American Civil War, not caring who exactly she sold them to.

The spirit witch smiles wickedly as she swishes Rio’s blade through the air and twirls it around her fingers; thank the Goddess its spacetime-cutting powers only activate when it’s wielded by Rio, because Agatha could bring the entire universe to its knees if she had that ability. Perversely, Rio almost wants Agatha to attack her and try to gut her; it would reassure her that her wife is feeling stronger, if she were to take a chance at starting up a little foreplay.  

Fortunately, Agatha Harkness, notorious mass murderer and bane of Lady Death’s existence, does not wish to use her all-powerful scythe knife to rip the universe apart. Instead, she kneels down in the leaf litter and roots around, with Scratchy helping her dig with his tiny paws, to uncover a small patch of morel mushrooms.

She slices the stems close to the soil, leaving the mushroom bases buried. She brushes dirt off the delicate fungi with her fingertips and then offers her bounty to Rio shyly, with a tentative little smile.

“Mushrooms for my mushroom,” she says quietly. “These are your favourites.”

“I’m not a mushroom,” Rio replies automatically, and then softens, because Agatha called her hers. 

She’s staking a claim over Rio again, showing hints of the possessive but attentive lover she used to be. The warmth that follows being claimed is quickly washed away, however, by a cold feeling of dread and concern. Agatha shouldn’t remember calling Rio a mushroom, because that conversation occurred after their dinner - and Agatha’s fatigued mind is suppressing those memories.

Rio can’t figure out whether it’s a good thing or a bad thing that tiny morsels of memory are beginning to peek through the cracks. She’s relieved, of course, that her wife’s memories are returning, indicating that her mind is healing, and yet she knows that as soon as Agatha’s memories of their argument return… the teasing playfulness and rebuilding of trust between them will cease.

The green witch accepts the morels and places them into her foraging bag. “You remember what my favourite kind of mushroom is?”

Agatha scoffs, shaking her head. “Hard not to. You’d stink the cottage out frying them in butter with garlic and shallots and then hide beneath the kitchen table as you scarfed them down because you were worried about me stealing them from you.” 

“Because you did try and steal them from me. If I left my plate unattended for a second, you’d be on it like a starving dog,” Rio laughs.

She remembers distinctly that Agatha used to insist that Rio’s food tasted better than her own, hence why she constantly used to sneak bites off her plate. Never mind that their meals were exactly the same - Agatha always resorted to thievery, and Rio didn’t mind, because it was adorable watching her stuff the food into her cheeks like a chipmunk as she scampered away when caught red-handed. 

“They’re your favourite mushrooms too,” Rio notes.

Agatha sighs wistfully. “They taste earthy and nutty, like chestnuts, and the chestnut harvest was always a short one in the fall. Goddess, American chestnuts were my favourite snack. Gorgeous roasted and tossed with sea salt or sugar - plentiful, before those idiots brought that disease to New England and wiped out our forests of them.”

“Chestnut blight,” Rio murmurs, remembering.

Her wife takes out her frustration on a stray log, which she gives a vicious kick. “The nuts would turn rancid after the spring thaw, and the morels always tend to pop up around that time to satiate my cravings for nutty things… well, they fruit in spring when a green witch isn’t accidentally spreading her magic through the forest and messing up with the fruiting schedule,” Agatha says pointedly, glancing around at the swaying trees.

Rio winces, because yes, spreading tendrils of her green magic through the woods to ensure they are safe for their stroll is triggering some strange ecosystem behaviour. These mushrooms would not usually appear during the fall. Hopefully, the forest will recover.

“Morels aren’t just our favorite,” Agatha tells her suddenly, her gaze intense, blue eyes piercing. “I would cook them exactly how you would, in a little cast iron skillet over a campfire, with goat butter and wild garlic… and he always requested them for his birthday.”

A lump forms in Rio’s throat. Yet another little morsel of information about their son that she was previously unaware of: Nicky loved morels just like his mothers. “Knew he had taste,” she tries to joke, but her voice is hoarse.

The spirit witch begins to pick her way through the undergrowth again, occasionally kneeling to cut some morels poking out through the damp leafy groundcovering. Scratchy scampers ahead, locating the mushrooms on his bonded witch’s behalf and acting like a pointer dog - pointer hare - whenever he finds some. Rio follows along behind her, mostly so she can keep a close eye on how Agatha is wielding her knife, but also so she can hold out the mesh bag as her wife drops mushrooms into it.

“When you say toxic relationship, do you mean between Wanda and me, or Wanda and the Darkhold?” Agatha asks suddenly, returning to their prior conversation.

Rio huffs a laugh. “Both?” she suggests wryly.

Agatha emits a chuckle, and her smile lifts her cheeks enough to display the crow's feet of her eyes. “Touché,” she allows.

Rio’s heart skips a beat. How long has it been, since she has seen her wife’s laugh lines?

She is struck by the sudden memory of when she and Agatha used to do this back in the early 18th century, during the early years of their marriage. After the cottage was built, they would take long, meandering strolls through the woods to forage the forest’s bounty; they would joke around, teasing and playfully chasing each other, hiding behind trees and flying just below the canopy.

It always ended with the pair taking a tumble onto a bed of lichen and moss, tearing each other’s clothes off and making love surrounded by nature.

Agatha was so young. Despite all the hardships she’d faced in her upbringing, with her mother’s abuse and her coven ostracizing and then trying to kill her, she was still strong and full of life. A true survivor, who delicately placed her heart in Rio’s hands once she learned to trust her. Her peals of laughter used to echo through these woods, often triggered by Rio pinning her to a tree and attacking her beautiful face and pale throat with kisses and hickeys.

Once Agatha lowered her walls around Rio and began to trust her, falling in love with her, she was so open and eager when it came to intimacy, with constant touches and kisses and adoring glances. Rio misses the casual loving affection between them. She misses it profusely, deeply, to her core. She misses it more than she can ever hope to express in words, because the last couple of centuries have just been… hollow. Empty.

Rio has been so alone. And while before, that wouldn’t have bothered her - Lady Death is a very lonely occupation, after all - after loving Agatha, being alone was awful. It was like being abandoned and stranded in the most arid of deserts, after indulging in having a fresh, clean, ice-cold water spring at her disposal for decades.

“You look constipated,” Agatha says with a smirk, drawing her back to the present. To Rio’s surprise, she offers Rio’s scythe blade back. “Thinking about Wanda and me flirting with each other, hmm?”

“Thinking about her bodyslamming you using a car as an improvised battering ram, actually,” Rio lies easily, accepting her blade and sheathing it. When the Westviewers informed her of Wanda attacking her wife like that, Rio was livid. Even with all the power of the Darkhold, that could have seriously injured Agatha, or even killed her. “There’s fighting as foreplay and then there’s going entirely off the rails. No wonder the Darkhold corrupted her as quickly as it did, considering the darkness already inside of her soul.”

“Wanda was an idiot,” the spirit witch murmurs, almost absentmindedly, flicking a loose strand of hair out of her face with an airy hand. “You know, I tried to warn her that she had no idea what she was doing, and was gonna get in over her head with the book. I told her that she was gonna need me. She traps me in mind-altering torture spell for three years, and look what happens?” she laughs mirthlessly, her eyes dark and lips pursed. 

Pausing, Agatha reaches out to grasp Rio’s wrist, much to her surprise. She feels her wife’s warm fingers encircle and close around her forearm, and she nearly drops the mesh bag full of mushrooms in shock.

The green witch’s gaze snaps up to meet her partner’s gaze, and she is instantly struck by how sky blue Agatha’s eyes are, with little flecks of grey and hazel and green. Rio has had the privilege of sparking supernovas, her touch causing stars to collapse in on themselves to create staggeringly gorgeous explosions of pure energy and cosmic debris; no supernova could ever be as mesmerizing as the galaxies that Rio can see in her wife’s eyes. 

“What did happen?” Agatha asks her, in an oddly subdued voice.

Rio tilts her head. “You don’t know?”

The spirit witch exhales forcefully, shrugging her hunched shoulders in an aloof, detached manner. But it’s clear it does bother her, to be in the dark. “I woke up from her curse and you very promptly kidnapped me, so no, not really,” she mutters, angrily plucking off leaves from the nearest witch-hazel bush and scrunching them up in her fist.

Rio tugs her wrist free of Agatha’s grip, and hesitantly slips her hand into her wife’s. Agatha jolts, at first, and for a brief second, the green witch is afraid she is going to flinch away with a sound of disgust and glower at her in disdain. But all Agatha does in reaction is narrow her eyes and stare at their joined hands for a moment before raising her head and looking away.

They continue to walk on through the forest along the deer trail, now holding hands. Victoria swoops down to peck at Rio’s hair mid-tail dive, croaking loudly, and then flutters down into the bushes to land next to Scratchy, who bounces up to her in greeting. As the two witches stroll along, their two familiars play with each other. Scratchy bats at the raven with his paws as if to box her, and Victoria nips at his rump with her beak, hopping behind him with flaps of her coal wings.

The tightness Rio feels in her chest is born from a mixture of anxiety and excitement. Agatha is allowing her to hold her hand. She’s nervous because part of her knows that her wife would not, perhaps, be so willing to partake in physical affection with her if she had her memories of their argument, but elated because it means that the trust between them is truly starting to rebuild.

Rio leans in and informs her, vibrating with amusement bcause she knows Agatha will find this funny as well, “If you want to know what happened to Wanda… a mountain fell on top of her.”

Agatha’s jaw drops open. “You’re kidding,” she splutters.

“Nope. She went kinda crazy because of the Darkhold warping her mind, sent a bunch of demons after some child who could jump between universes because she wanted to steal her power and find her kids. Huge murder-spree at Kamar-Taj, which let me tell you, was not fun to clean up when all the sorcerers keep trying to attack you for doing your job. Terrorised the multiverse for a bit but then had some sort of come-to-Jesus moment. Destroyed all the Darkhold copies, and Mount Wundagore crushed her.”

Agatha bursts out laughing. She has to bend at the waist as she rocks with the force of it, and unlike her other bitter chuckles or small snorts of amusement, this is a proper, fully-belly laugh. It’s probably the first time in literal decades that Rio has heard her wife laugh without abandon, and it causes her heart to flutter in a way that makes her wonder if it’s normal for an organ to experience that sort of sensation just because of the joyous sound of her lover’s glee.

“Agatha Demetra Harkness, a woman suffered a psychotic break, killed a bunch of people and then ultimately killed herself. Don’t laugh, have some class,” Rio scolds slightly, squeezing her hand in admonishment. It’s not real, though - she is just as amused at her wife.

When Agatha straightens back up again, she mock-wipes away tears from her eyes, chuckling darkly. “I’m sorry - it’s just - she paraded herself as this holier-than-thou superhero who could never do anything wrong. When she cast the Hex over Westview and she mind-controlled the entire town - she hid behind the excuse that it was an accident, that she didn’t understand her own power.” Blowing a stray strand of hair out of her face, she scoffs, “You know, she accused me of killing my mother and coven on purpose.”

What? How dare she!? Rio is fully aware that Agatha is by no means innocent - she’s a serial killer, after all, an apex predator and essentially a cannibal, as she absorbs and feeds off the magic of the witches she kills.

There have been plenty of people that she’s killed in cold blood, for revenge or just because she was annoyed and bored. But Agatha’s first mass murder was an act of self-defense. Her mother’s coven deserved to die. She was killing her abusers.

“You were a child, barely eighteen,” Rio says, shaking her head in frustration. “They were cowards, ambushing you in your sleep, blindfolding you, and tying you to a stake in the middle of the night, so you were disoriented and couldn’t fight back. They were attempting to execute you for powers you couldn’t control.”

What Agatha doesn’t know, which Rio doesn’t want her to, is that Evanora was such a horrific, vile woman that she’d wanted to kill Agatha as a day-old infant, as soon as she was born. Simply because of the circumstances of her conception and birth. Agatha experienced multiple near-death experiences as a child that she is entirely unaware of, but were a result of her mother’s negligence - and her hope that it would lead Agatha to an early death, in some cases. 

She was regularly starved and sent into the forest as a young girl to gather ritual ingredients, with Evanora not caring about the wild bears, wolves and mountain lions that could have attacked her, or the poisonous foragables she might ingest because of her hunger.

Agatha only survived due to the strength of her spirit magic and her ability to siphon. The spirit witchling evaded death despite the dangerous situations she found herself in, never quite crossing that line that separated the living from the dead, but coming teeteringly close.

“She saw my memory of that night, but I doubt she was paying enough attention to take notice of that,” Agatha rolls her eyes, her mouth twisting into a smirk. “So forgive me if I find it utterly hilarious that she went to such extreme lengths to bring Billy and Bobby back using the Darkhold, when they never truly existed in the first place - I offered to help her with it, and could have told her from the very beginning that it wasn’t possible.” She kicks a stone on the ground with particular vehemence.

Rio cocks her head. How would Agatha know that it wasn’t possible… if she hadn’t tried herself? She’s always wondered Agatha’s true motivation in reading the Book of the Damned. She has long since believed that her wife wanted to get her hands on it for a specific reason, and not just because of her pursuit of magical knowledge and wanting to use its dark magic to hide from Rio’s sight.

“Why did you go after the Darkhold?” she asks.

And then instantly regrets the question, knowing just from the way Agatha stiffens that it is a stupid, thoughtless, wounding one. For a fleeting, split second, her wife’s expression crumples into one of abject anguish - the kind of expression she only ever adopts when she is thinking about the loss of their son. Her eyes gleam as she meets Rio’s gaze, filled with pain and wet with tears.

But then, that devastated look on the spirit witch’s face dissipates, replaced with a fearsome scowl so deep and visceral that Rio feels like some small creature that Agatha wants to crush underfoot.

She is Death, endless and cosmic and eternal, and yet one piercing look from Agatha has her on her knees and begging for forgiveness in an instant.

“You already know the answer to that question,” the spirit witch gripes, curling her lip. Her free hand, the one not currently within Rio’s grasp, subconsciously raises up to grasp at the locket hanging around her neck.

Rio does know the answer: Nicky. It always comes down to Nicky. But she suspects that Agatha has never admitted that out loud. Agatha’s severe, unprocessed grief over the loss of their son has transformed her into someone barely recognisable from the young witch, eager to learn and starved for love and affection, that Rio first met all those centuries ago.

Nicky was Agatha’s motivation for chasing down the Darkhold, and although Rio suspects she knows why, she doesn’t understand what the catalyst was for her wife to begin that hunt. She can imagine why Agatha would want the damned book - to try and bring Nicky back to life.

But would Agatha ever confess that to Rio?

“Humor me,” Rio says.

Which, once again, is the worst thing she could possibly say.

Her anger ignited, Agatha tears her hand from Rio’s grasp, recoiling from her. “I’m not here to amuse you, Rio,” she snarls.

Rio flinches. Seeing her wife backing away from her with those flinty eyes, pale face, and vitriolic expression gives her intense, almost debilitating flashbacks to how her wife has greeted her over the centuries after their son’s passing.

Considering she is meant to be an all-powerful and eternal cosmic entity, she despises how small her wife is capable of making her feel. She supposes she understands Agatha’s current anger - asking her to humor Rio was a terrible move.

She extends her hand back out, pleading soothingly, “Agatha.”

But the spirit witch shakes her head, scoffing in disgust and turning her nose up at her. “My pain, my suffering, it’s not something for you to laugh at,” she sneers, slapping her hand away. “You laugh at the misfortune of others, but not at your wife’s.”

Rio holds her breath. She can see why Agatha might think she is mocking or condescending her, but it hurts to hear that her wife thinks she would find her pursuit of the Darkhold, driven by her struggles with grief and anguish, entertaining. Managing to snag Agatha’s hand again, she holds on tight even when her wife tries to yank away, raising it to her lips to press an apologetic kiss to her knuckles.

“I’m sorry. I’m not laughing, mi vida, I promise,” she murmurs softly.

Huffing, Agatha refuses to look at her again, although the tension does appear to dissipate from her body, her shoulders relaxing. When she extracts her hand from Rio’s this time, it’s more gently than before. She tucks them beneath her arms as she strides ahead, head bowed, but she appears more pensive than angry. Every so often, she bends down to rip a mushroom from the ground, continuing to collect them.

Exhaling, Rio shakes her head. She does sometimes feel like Agatha’s emotional state can be a minefield to navigate; she may be an eternal and omnipotent metaphysical entity, unkillable and unharmable, but human emotions have always been difficult for her since she herself is not the same species.

Agatha has always been her subject when studying human emotions and trying to understand their complexity, but after hundreds of years - the majority of them regrettably spent separated - she is just as enigmatic and inscrutable as she was when Rio first met her.

At first, Rio is quick to fall into step behind her wife, not wanting Agatha to stray too far ahead, but she halts mid-stride when Scratchy pops up within the thick, knee-length grass in front of her with his eyes glowing red and a deep, rumbling growl erupting from his chest.

He’s angry that she accidentally upset his witch again.

He pops up into a hare’s boxing position, baring his incisors warningly. Rio is not phased. She flicks a green spark towards him, which makes him duck and squeak in indignation. He wheels around and bounds off to tackle Victoria in retaliation instead, pinning her wings to the ground with his paws.

Rio’s familiar shoots her a dirty look, and she can feel her annoyance like a pinch on her essence, but she simply shrugs.

Agatha stumbles slightly upon straightening back up from where she crouched down to pluck a particularly big morel, as if she is dizzy. Rio races forward to grab her by the waist and steady her, pulling her partner back to lean against her front, so that she’s supported upright. Scratchy pauses in his posturing, scrambling off Victoria to bound towards them in concern. 

“Agatha?” Rio murmurs softly.

“I’m fine,” she mutters. She pushes away, running her fingers through her hair in frustration. She drops the morel into the mesh bag hanging from Rio’s arm.

Rio sighs. “You’re getting tired.”

“I’m not,” her wife bristles, shrugging her off and stepping away - but not particularly far, staying within grasping distance. It’s as much of an acceptance of Rio’s apology as she is likely to get. “Tiredness is for losers. Just stood up too fast.”

She’s worried that it’s a side effect of her trauma-induced memory loss, but she can’t exactly say that while Agatha is unaware of what happened. There is, of course, another explanation for Agatha’s lightheadedness and general weakness. “Being under that hex was terrible for you,” the cosmic entity notes.

Agatha scrunches up her nose scornfully, but it makes her look like an adorable little pouty kitten, rather than a contemptuous, vengeful witch. “Understatement. That Weasley family reject didn’t know what the hell she was doing when she put me under it. She was just trying so desperately to play hero by locking up the big bad witch in sitcom hell.”

Recalling what her partner previously said, Rio asks incredulously, “Did you seriously offer Wanda aid with the Darkhold, before she cursed you?”

“Yes,” Agatha huffs.

“That was… out of character and unusually generous of you.” She would have thought she was more likely to kill Wanda, than allow her to gain any sort of power that Agatha could have possessed herself.

“Oh please, I was trying to save my own hide, not actually help her,” the spirit witch groans. She is quite obviously exhausted, because she plops herself down on a fallen tree log for a break, pretending as if she is fascinated by the moss and lichen on it, so she doesn’t have to admit to her fatigue. “We both know that as soon as her back was turned, I would’ve blasted the shit out of her to start a siphon or fled like a bat out of hell.”

Rio stifles a laugh upon hearing that, because yes, Agatha is really the epitome of the fight or flight response, with fight being the most overpowering instinct. She is extremely antagonistic to a hilarious degree, and then always acts shocked and appalled, playing innocent, when people bite back at her.

But Rio also knows that Agatha lashes out preemptively at people as a defence mechanism. She learnt as a tiny child from her mother’s coven that she could never let her guard down around other witches, and that her kin are far more likely to harm her than express kindness towards her.

If she saw Wanda as a threat - which she absolutely was - then it makes sense she was trying to force Wanda off balance, to try and gain the upper hand. 

Taking a seat on the other side of the log from her wife, Rio quips back, “Heard from your neighbours that the siphoning backfired on you.”

“Yes, it did, and then it turned out Wanda was much more of a sadist than I could have imagined,” Agatha grumbles. She leans over to scoop up Scratchy onto her lap when he lopes over and bats at her legs, stroking over his soft fur. “I like a bit of roughhousing, manipulation, and gaslighting when it comes to my prey, but the Scarlet Witch apparently goes all-in with psychological torture hexes.” She hisses those final three words in an incensed tone, forehead vein throbbing as her fingers scratch her bunny-turned-hare familiar’s pelt.

Psychological torture… Rio cannot even begin to imagine what it was like. She can scarcely fathom it, actually, because while she knows how fragile human minds can be, she has always thought of Agatha as being so immensely resilient. Her mind was psychically fortified to the point where even with their bond, it was hard for Rio to read it. Without her magic, Agatha’s walls are lowered, not that Rio would violate her by testing her psychic boundaries.

“I suppose she was somewhat merciful in not taking Señor Scratchy,” her wife says absentmindedly, playing with a tuft of the hare’s fur. “I mean, I did kill her sons’ dog, so she was within her rights to go all ‘an eye for an eye, a pet for a pet’ and steal him.”

Rio nearly falls off the log onto the ground in her shock. Agatha has killed countless scores of witches… and humans who have pissed her off as well (mostly men), but she is not somebody who engages in needless violence against animals. And she knows that Rio adores animals. Killing them for food and furs, for survival, is something Rio understands, and even encouraged when Agatha was living alone in the woods. But a dog?

“You killed her dog?” Rio asks in a disappointed voice. Victoria hops over, raven wings fluttering as she jumps up to perch on the cosmic entity’s knee. She echoes Rio’s disapproval with a sharp caw, ruffling her feathers when Scratchy hisses in response.

“Oh, don’t look at me like that. It wasn’t a real dog! It was a cockroach I transformed into a puppy.” Agatha rolls her eyes. Rio relaxes somewhat upon hearing that, but is still not entirely happy, because cockroaches still experience pain, and are important for ecosystems. When Rio continues to frown at her, her wife scowls and argues, “Look, her robot boyfriend was reportedly dead, yet he was present in the Hex with her. I was testing to see if she had true resurrection powers or if she was just reanimating her sentient toaster of a husband’s corpse.”

She sneers the word toaster with scorn, so much that Rio has to stifle a snort of amusement. But there is an unspoken implication in Agatha’s comment about Wanda’s magic that quickly sobers her. Resurrection. That was the power her wife was chasing.

“You wanted to steal that power from her,” Rio says, eyeing the spirit watch cautiously. “You wanted the power of true resurrection, not just necromancy and reanimation.” 

As a spirit witch, Agatha is capable of both those last forms of magic, but no witch has ever mastered bringing a person back completely from the dead. Rio has never allowed it. It would, after all, shatter the delicate balance of the Universe and potentially lead to catastrophic fallout. But figuring out a way to bring Nicky back from the dead has been Agatha’s main goal for centuries.

“She was undeserving of it,” Agatha seethes. Lurching to her feet, she begins to pace back and forth like a restless tiger, gnashing her teeth and growling. She clutches her familiar to her chest, petting him almost aggressively. “Fuck, she was insufferable, Rio, you really have no idea.”

Quirking an eyebrow, Rio encourages, “Tell me.”

Her wife halts in her pacing abruptly, shooting her a dubious look. Almost as if she can’t fathom why the green witch would be bothered. As if she can hardly believe this conversation is happening at all. Which, to be fair, is understandable, because this might be the longest conversation they’ve had in Goddess knows how long. It’s certainly the longest conversation they’ve had since Agatha broke free from the Hex-turned-curse.

When Rio nods promptingly, the spirit witch releases an aggravated sound, and lets loose.

Pacing again, she rages, “All Wanda did was complain about how exhausted she was and how her husband and sons were driving her crazy.” The laugh that bursts out of Agatha’s chest is agonised, dripping with revulsion. There’s something somewhat reassuring about the fact that Rio can be certain that she is not the person Agatha hates the most (at least, not anymore). “As if she wasn’t the entire reason the craziness was happening in the first place, since it was her magic powering the whole Hex.” She hugs Scratchy tightly, burying her face in his fur, voice dropping to a pained whisper. “As if I wouldn’t have given anything to have my wife and child by my side again, my family complete, craziness and all.”

Rio cannot find the words to speak. There is a lump in her throat that has grown so large that she feels as if she is going to choke on it, heavy and hard like a ball of lead. Her magic has coiled in her chest like a python, clenching and cinching around her obsidian heart, vibrating with anger - anger towards Wanda. Agatha must have felt as if she was being gut-punched and emotionally beaten to a pulp within the Scarlet Witch’s Hex, forced to watch on as Wanda got to play happy family while Agatha was constantly reminded of what she lost.

“So yes, I killed her cockroach dog,” Agatha continues fiercely, stopping in place so she can glare at Rio, as if daring her to voice her criticism of her decision. “She’s lucky I didn’t kill her tykes, they were certainly annoying enough. Just constant whinging and yapping, so entitled. I cannot begin to explain how enjoyable it was to put those brats on leashes and hold them hostage.”

“You don’t hurt children, Agatha,” Rio reminds her gently.

Agatha has an extremely strict code: she never targets kids. Ever. In fact, Agatha deliberately avoids getting caught in situations where children could even be accidentally hurt or end up as collateral. Because Agatha may be a serial killer succubus witch, but there is one other thing that she is above all else: a mother. Her son being dead doesn’t change that. She is and will always be a mother, who cares for children even if they are not her own.

Rio remembers, from her time watching Agatha secretly from afar during their separation after Nicky’s death; her wife tried her hardest to hide her fondness of kids, acting as if they were tiny nuisances. She’s always suspected that Agatha only pretends to find them irritating because she simply can’t stand how much the children remind her of Nicky, and it hurts too much to care for them.

She has no doubt that even in the short period of time the spirit witch spent inside the Hex with the Sokovian and her brood, Agatha would have developed some affection for Wanda’s magical patchwork children.

Worn out from her pacing, the spirit witch plops back down onto the fallen log - directly next to Rio, this time, so close that their thighs brush. “Well, it’s not like they were real,” she mumbles, visibly sulking. “It was within a Hex, it wouldn’t have had any serious impact on reality. Don’t worry, your precious sacred balance wasn’t affected,” she dismisses.

Rio frowns. “Actually, it’s been off ever since,” she says thoughtfully. Not off enough to disrupt the entire universe, but just… slightly tilted to the right a little. “I don’t know what the Scarlet Witch did, whether she somehow screwed around with spirit magic as well as chaos, but for the past three years I’ve never been able to shake the feeling that there are souls out there that need collecting, but I can’t figure out who, or how.”

It’s like an itch in the center of her spine, one that she can never reach to scratch. Scratch… huh. Rio’s eyes flash to the hare in Agatha’s lap.

“She didn’t accept the dog as her familiar, did she?” Familiars typically die along with their witch, but if Wanda took the dog as her familiar, infused it with chaos magic, and its soul is still romping around, that may account for the shift in the sacred balance.

Agatha snort-laughs so hard that it makes Rio’s chest tighten. “She was an infant witch, I doubt she even knew what a familiar is,” she snickers. “No, the damn cockroach dog was not the Scarlet Witch’s familiar, Rio. I may be an asshole, but I’m not that big of an asshole that I would kill a witch’s familiar for an experiment.”

She pets her rabbit familiar gently, which triggers Victoria to jump from Rio’s knee onto Agatha’s, plucking little loose tufts of fur from Scratchy’s pelt with her beak. She strokes a single finger over the raven’s feathers. Rio feels the ghost sensation of it, like ice sliding down her vertebrae.

“I know more than anybody how invaluable and cherished they become, once you bond with one,” her wife muses aloud.

“How did Scratchy come to be? When did you bond with him?” the entity asks curiously. “If I’m remembering correctly, when we lived in the cottage together back before we had Nicky, you swore you would never take a familiar because of how it could be used to target you.”

Plus, Agatha didn’t even think it would be possible because of how it would mean giving away a piece of her soul and magic to an animal, and she had mentioned once to Rio that she thought that she would siphon and accidentally kill it immediately during the process.

“Yes, well, Scratchy was… a special case,” Agatha says slowly, lowering her eyes to gaze down at the rabbit, who pretends to be innocent and adorable by batting her hands with his paws. There’s no mistaking the pure affection in her voice as she explains softly, “It was after I acquired the Darkhold. I did something… not dissimilar to what Wanda did. Except I didn’t travel to different universes - I merely went on an extended jaunt through all the different underworlds, trying to get a better grasp on resurrection magic, exploring some of the Darkhold’s rituals. I don’t think I need to explain to you why.” Her eyes flick up to briefly meet Rio’s, a faint grimace spreading over her face as Rio stares at her, dumbfounded and livid, because Agatha did what? “You’re angry.”

“You knew I would be,” Rio fires back, her voice sharp, a razorblade slashing through her wife’s defences. “You vacationed in all the different pantheons’ versions of Hell? Do you have any idea how dangerous that is!? I wouldn’t’ve been able to reach you!”

Not without Rio requesting permission from the different pantheons first, because while she is Death, she also respects Hades, Oriris, Mictlantecuhtli, and many of the other gods of death, enough so that she wouldn’t enter their territory without at least giving them a heads-up. But she then would have had to admit to the gods that she wanted to enter their realms to fetch her wandering, world-hopping wife, and that would have created even greater danger, as her enemies may have sought to control Agatha, to inadvertently attempt to control her.

“That’s what you wanted, though, right?” Rio challenges. “That’s why you blocked our soul bond, because you knew I would stop you.”

Agatha doesn’t reply. Doesn’t interrupt, doesn’t retort back with something sarcastic and furious. Just… looks at her, with hollow yet beady eyes. Her hand frozen in Scratchy’s fur. The demeanor is that of a prey animal caught in the sights of a predator, uncertain of how hungry it might be. She anticipated Rio having this reaction. And judging by her body language, which is tense and withdrawn, it’s as if she’s waiting for Rio to lash out at her physically.

Scratchy glares at Rio and squeaks forcefully. Dude, stop snapping at her, she can tell he is saying. Even Victoria is glancing over at her with a somewhat judgmental look, cocking her head and ruffling her feathers, half-flaring her wings as if to shield Agatha from her.

She deflates. “Go on. Which dimension did you meet Scratchy in?”

“You’re going to get angrier,” the spirit watch warns. “Mephisto’s.” When a deep, resounding snarl erupts from Rio’s throat, her rage taking over upon hearing Agatha mutter that monster’s name, her wife raises her voice, asserting, “Do you want to hear this story or not? If you’re just going to fly off the handle every time I open my mouth, then there’s no point in me speaking!”

Rio exhales. Squashing her down fury, she calms the aggrieved magic boiling and bubbling inside of her chest and threatening to burst out of her. “I’m sorry, mi vida. Please, tell me. I will listen. I want to hear about how you found the familiar who reminded you so much of Nicky that you named him after our son.”

“Hmm.” Agatha eyes her shrewdly for a moment, as if unsure whether or not Rio is truly going to hold herself back from interrupting or growling again.

Scratchy huffs as well, clearly unhappy with her. Rio hates that little cabrón leporid with every fibre of her being, but knows she can’t touch him. Instead, her displeasure transfers over to her own familiar; Victoria nips Scratchy with her beak, squawking at him. The spirit witch tuts at her and scoops her familiar up to cradle him in his arms instead of just letting him rest on her lap.

“I traveled to Mephisto’s dimension in search of a Pandemonium Cube, for a necromantic ritual described in the Darkhold,” Agatha begins to explain. “I didn’t realise that there is only one Cube and that Mephisto himself is the owner of it, and by the time I figured it out, several of his archdemons were on my tail. They were using canid demons to hunt me - hellhounds.” The cosmic entity’s obsidian heart seizes. Even though she knows that Agatha survived, and managed to escape, it’s horrifying to hear how she was being chased by demons who would have undoubtedly torn her apart if they’d caught her. “The only way I managed to evade them was by casting a dark self-illusion to lead them astray, and then transforming into my cat form and caking myself in ash to hide in one of the ghost poplar trees.”

Rio has to admit… she’s mightily impressed by her wife, and also incredibly proud of her cunning. “You tricked Mephisto’s Hunt? Fuck, Agatha, you’re insane. And a genius. You might be the only being in existence who has ever managed to do that,” she says in disbelief, smoothing back her hair.

“Yes, I’m exceptional, we both know that,” Agatha preens with a smirk. But then her gaze drops to focus on the hare she’s cuddling to her chest, hand very gently stroking over his ears. “Only one hellhound didn’t fall for the trick, and it was young female pregnant one. She refused to follow the trail I left, and the demon lords became furious with her. They beat her and left her for dead. She gave birth in her last breaths, and all the puppies were dead except for one.” A fragile smile cracks her solemn expression as Scratchy nuzzles into the crook of her neck affectionately.

Rio barks a laugh of disbelief. “You stole a hellhound puppy from Mephisto’s realm and raised him as your familiar?”

“He was a runt! They would have killed him!” Agatha says defensively, her hackles raised. Her grasp must become a little too tight on her familiar, because he squeaks in admonishment. Rio is stunned to witness her wife instantly softening, breathing out shakily as she whispers an apology to the rabbit. Hugging Scratchy tightly, her voice breaks when she mumbles, “He was small, and weak, and so frail. I - I couldn’t leave him.”

Rio shakes her head fondly. “Oh, Agatha, you and your soft squishy bleeding heart.”

The spirit witch turns bright red, stammering in mortification, “Shut up! How dare you say that, I’m - I’m an unlovable evil mass murdering witch serial killer, I am anything but - but SOFT!”

But the manner in which she cradles her hellhound-turned-rabbit familiar and musses Scratchy’s thick belly fur is evidence of otherwise. Although, Rio thinks, Agatha is extremely selective with her affection. She has only ever opened her heart up to three beings in existence: Rio, Nicky, and her familiar. She is warm and gentle only towards those whom she deems worthy of her love - and who have loved her in return.

“Evil mass murdering serial killer, yes,” Rio replies with a smile. “Unlovable? Agree to disagree. I happen to love you very much. And I think our son would side with me, if he were here.” She slowly rises to her feet, rocking back on her heels as she offers her wife her hand. “Come on, the longer you stay sitting down, the colder you’re going to get. I can sense there’s a stream up ahead. We can take a brief water break?”

“Fine.”

Agatha doesn’t hesitate to take it this time, grunting as she hauls herself up. Victoria clambers up onto her shoulder to perch there while Scratchy is carried in the crook of her arm. The sight of her familiar pecking at stray hairs to tuck them behind Agatha’s ear makes Rio feel light, a weight having been lifted from her.

They begin to walk again, Rio leading the way this time. Agatha lags behind only slightly, content to stand and watch as the green witch continues with her self-imposed task of picking mushrooms and foraging within the bushes. For a moment, she contemplates making a joke about her wife letting her do all the work, but Rio can’t bring herself to when Agatha appears so calm for once. She’s a little distant, her gaze straying out into the forest, but Rio can sense through their strained bond that her anxiety is not as prevalent as before.

“What about your darling little familiar?” her wife asks, eyeing the raven with interest. “I didn’t think it was possible for Death itself to even have a familiar. When did you get her?”

Raising an eyebrow, the cosmic entity blinks over at them, the extension of her power peering back with beady black eyes. “Funnily enough, I’ve had Victoria longer than you’ve had Scratchy. Death may not be able to have a familiar, but Rio, the green witch, can.” She holds her arm out, and Victoria obediently swoops over to land on it, her effortless glide barely making a sound. “She appeared to me, the day… Nicky was born.”

Agatha barely reacts to that, beyond a minuscule narrowing of her eyes, before her expression returns to one of controlled blankness. “You didn’t summon her?”

“Perhaps subconsciously.”

Rio cannot remember precisely, but she understands that she had retreated and hidden from Agatha, immensely upset after the events of Nicky’s stillbirth, and in pain from the universe cracking at the seams around her, the sacred balance screaming at her to restore it. She had been formless, lashing out with her power and yet desperately trying to rein it in, when Victoria had come into existence.

“She’s a Shade, a living shadow. I knew that you would never let me near you or our son, or at least - not knowingly,” she murmurs. “So I sent her to watch over you in my stead. I can see through her eyes, and she can send summons to me in the case of emergencies. She was there, by your side, every day from the moment Nicky came into this world, until he left it.”

And Victoria had been there to welcome Nicky through the Gates into her realm, and ensured his protection during those early days until he was settled. Even now, her familiar still returns to the afterlife to check up on her son on her behalf. She can’t imagine Agatha would react well to that information, however, so Rio ultimately decides to omit it.

An odd look overtakes Agatha’s face now. It’s strange - borderline suspicious, but with a tinge of bemusement. Rio wishes so badly that their telepathic and empathic bond were fully restored so she could just tell what she is thinking. “And why Victoria?”

“You mean the name? It’s Latin. The name of the Roman goddess of victory. The counterpart to the Greek goddess Nike.”

Rio is in the middle of examining a thick bunch of sunchoke and trying to figure out if the roots would be ready to harvest yet when she is suddenly shoved from behind. She’s off balance already, which is the only reason why she ends up falling over. Victoria manages to react in time to not go topping onto the forest floor alongside her, landing on delicate wings and immediately transforming into a beech marten to tackle Scratchy, who has just jumped down from Agatha’s arms, to the ground. The two familiars grapple with each other as the spirit witch glowers down at her, and Rio dusts the dirt off her hands with a sigh.

“What was that for?” the green witch asks her.

Agatha points at her accusingly. “You named your familiar in Nicky’s honor too!”

Oh. “Yes, I did,” she replies, entirely unapologetic. She has nothing to apologise for, in that regard, even if her wife is glaring at her as if she does. “The whole point of her existence was to protect and watch over you and our son. It made sense to name her in dedication of Nicky.”

It helped Rio feel as if she played some small part of his life… even as she was forced to stay away and watch on from afar, never truly allowed real contact with her son or to get to know him. And it was better that way, because lingering around a soul calling to be reaped for too long would have been torturous for her, especially knowing that it was her own flesh and blood on the constant verge of death.

Agatha’s eyes are wide - and appear marginally watery, as if she’s near tears. “You named your familiar after Nicky. You do have a heart.”

Rio’s hand flies to her sternum, where her heart of obsidian lies beneath her clothes, a perfect volcanic glass gem containing clippings of Agatha and Nicky’s hair. “It belongs to you,” she murmurs. “To you, to our unborn children, and to Nicky. It always has. You taught me what it means to love, Agatha. Nicky was born from that love. And our other children, they didn’t survive, but not from a lack of it.”

For a moment, the cosmic entity isn’t sure whether Agatha is about to kiss her or slap her. Agatha is staring at her so intensely, though, that she wouldn’t be surprised if it were the latter. Which is why she is stunned into near silence when her wife brushes her fingers over her shoulder and quietly responds, “Thank you.”

Rio reaches up to rest her hand on top of Agatha’s for a brief moment, but is quick to let go when her wife draws back, not wanting to force contact between them. But the fact that Agatha has willingly initiated touch between the two of them so many times today is very promising. Although Rio would prefer for her to be doing it with her full memories of their argument last night and the events in Nicky’s nursery.

She leans into humor, instead, knowing that if she focuses too much on how her wife seems to be gradually softening towards her, she will swiftly become overwhelmed by emotion. “Did I mishear, or did the words ‘thank’ and ‘you’ just emerge from Agatha Harkness’ mouth consecutively?” she teases.

Agatha scoffs and rolls her eyes, giving the cosmic entity another shove, although this time it’s more playful. “Yeah, yeah, don’t make a big deal out of it,” she grumbles.

Her eyes dart over to Scratchy and Victoria - who have now stopped fighting and are grooming one another affectionately. Her cheeks grow rosy watching them, because just like Rio, she is probably thinking about how their familiars’ tenderness towards one another is a reflection of their own emotions and desire to reconnect, echoing through their souls. Animals have far fewer boundaries than humans, though, and Scratchy caring for Victoria is likely the only way that the spirit witch feels truly comfortable and safe expressing her love for Rio, in her current vulnerable and mostly closed-off state.

“What are you thanking me for?” Rio probes.

She’s not entirely expecting Agatha to respond, perhaps anticipating her wife to shrug her off or offer up some nonchalant response or bogus explanation. Instead, Agatha’s reply is almost too genuine, her sincerity bleeding through into her voice and making her sound just a touch too honest for Rio to feel at ease with. “Just… for… making sure we were safe. Living out in the woods, moving around, stealing from towns, and swindling witches while raising Nicky - it wasn’t an easy existence, and there were nights, especially during the winter, when I was scared the cold would take him before his sickness would. Knowing that you were keeping an eye on us, from a distance, it… it makes me feel better.” Agatha visibly swallows, crossing her arms over her chest and peering down at the forest floor. “The whole reason we lived out in the forest was because it was my hope that Nicky may have inherited green magic, and it would give him strength. And also… so that I could feel close to you.”

Rio is at a near loss for words. “I thought you stayed constantly on the move so that I couldn’t track you,” she says helplessly.

Her wife shakes her head. “If that were the case, then I would have stopped hanging around after killing witches to give you time to see us, and taken him to the city where it would have been harder to find us.”

Taken aback upon hearing that, Rio pauses for a moment to process that. She’s never considered that before. That Agatha could have bundled Nicky up and rushed him away after feeding off a coven, so that they were long gone when Rio arrived to reap them. She purposefully stayed in the area so that the green witch would have a chance to check in on them from a distance.

And yes, if they had fled to one of the larger cities, such as Boston or New York, or even Philadelphia, which would have made them even harder to find given that it was the most populous at the time. Rio would have been able to track Agatha down using their soul bond, but all of the dead souls hollering at her to be reaped within those cities would have muffled their connection and made it more difficult to pin Agatha and Nicky down.

She has to jog to catch up with Agatha, who is following their two familiars, who are bounding and fluttering ahead, where Rio can sense the forest’s stream pounding on the rockbed like a beating heart. “Thank you,” she echoes, upon reaching her wife’s side, gently bumping her with her shoulder. “For staying immersed in nature, for honoring my connection to the Earth’s green magic.” She nods ahead, through the trees. “Are you happy to keep going? I want to forage some mountain sorrel and black walnuts.” Glanicng around, the green witch suddenly realises exactly where they are within the forest. “Hey, you know it’s chestnut season.”

Agatha hums thoughtfully, running her fingers - her hand is still trembling just a little from all the physical exertion - through her thick mane of hair. “We’d have to find a blight-resistant chestnut tree, and I know for a fact that the blight ravaged the National Park when it escaped New York.”

“And if I told you that I know of a tree that survived?” Rio says, grinning. “One not too far from here, that my magic infused in the forest has kept alive and blight-free for centuries?”

“Really?” her wife questions, suddenly eager. With a refreshed pep in her step, she forges onwards, calling back over her shoulder, “Well, what are you waiting for!? I want roasted chestnuts for dessert tonight, Rio!”

Shaking her head in amusement, Rio chases after her.

Chasing after Agatha is one of the things she is best at, after all.
